<dt class="glossary" id="aaw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">AAW</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An acronym for <a href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare" title="Anti-aircraft warfare">anti-aircraft warfare</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aback" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aback</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(of a <a href="/wiki/Sail" title="Sail">sail</a>) Filled by the wind on the opposite side to the one normally used to move the vessel forward. On a <a href="/wiki/Square_rig" title="Square rig">square-rigged</a> ship, any of the square sails can be <a href="#brace"><span title="See entry on this page at § brace" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">braced</span></a> round to be aback, the purpose of which may be to reduce speed (such as when a <a href="/wiki/Ship-of-the-line" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship-of-the-line">ship-of-the-line</a> is keeping station with others), to <a href="#heave_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § heave to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">heave to</span></a>, or to assist moving the ship's head through the eye of the wind when <a href="/wiki/Tacking_(sailing)" title="Tacking (sailing)">tacking</a>. A sudden shift in the wind can also cause a square-rigged vessel to be unintentionally "caught aback" with all sails aback. This is a dangerous situation that risks serious damage. In a <a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rigged</a> vessel, a <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a> is backed either by hauling it across with the <span title="See entry on this page at § weather sheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#weather_sheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">weather sheet</a></span> or by tacking without releasing the sheet. It is used to heave to or to assist with tacking.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarland1984181–188,_222,_225–228_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarland1984181–188,_222,_225–228-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> See also <i><a href="#back_and_fill"><span title="See entry on this page at § back and fill" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">back and fill</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="abaft" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">abaft</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Toward the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>, relative to some object (e.g. "abaft the cockpit").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="abaft_the_beam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">abaft the beam</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Farther <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> than the <a href="#beam"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beam</span></a>; a relative bearing of greater than 90 degrees from the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>; e.g. "two points abaft the beam, starboard side" would describe "an object lying 22.5 degrees toward the rear of the ship, as measured clockwise from a perpendicular line from the right side, center, of the ship, toward the horizon".<sup id="cite_ref-navalslang_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-navalslang-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="abandon_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">abandon ship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An imperative to leave the vessel immediately, usually in the face of some imminent overwhelming danger.<sup id="cite_ref-hope_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> It is an order issued by the <span title="See entry on this page at § master" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#master" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">master</a></span> or a delegated person in command, and must be a verbal order. It is usually the last resort after all other mitigating actions have failed or become impossible, when destruction or loss of the ship is imminent, and is customarily followed by a command to "man the <a href="/wiki/Lifeboat_(shipboard)" title="Lifeboat (shipboard)">lifeboats</a>" or life rafts.<sup id="cite_ref-hope_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-layton_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-layton-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="abeam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">abeam</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On the <a href="#beam"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beam</span></a>; a relative bearing at right angles to the ship's <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a>; e.g. describing an object located at a bearing of 90 degrees (<a href="/wiki/Port_and_starboard" title="Port and starboard">starboard</a>) or 270 degrees (<a href="/wiki/Port_and_starboard" title="Port and starboard">port</a>) as measured clockwise from the ship's <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="able_seaman_(ab)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Able_seaman" title="Able seaman">able seaman</a> (AB)</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>able-bodied seaman</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A merchant seaman qualified to perform all routine duties on a vessel, or a junior rank in some navies.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On or in a vessel. Synonymous with "on board". See also <i><a href="#close_aboard"><span title="See entry on this page at § close aboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">close aboard</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="about" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">about</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To change the course of a ship by <a href="/wiki/Tacking_(sailing)" title="Tacking (sailing)">tacking</a>. "Ready about" is the order to prepare for tacking.<sup id="cite_ref-Naval_encyclopedia_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naval_encyclopedia-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="above_board" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">above board</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On or above the <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a>; in plain view; not hiding anything. Pirates would often hide their crews below decks, thereby creating the false impression that an encounter with another ship was a casual matter of chance rather than a planned assault.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="above-water_hull" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">above-water hull</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The section of a vessel's <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> above the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>; the visible part of a ship. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § topsides" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsides" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsides</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="absentee_pennant" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">absentee pennant</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A special pennant flown to indicate the absence of a ship's commanding officer, admiral, chief-of-staff, or an officer whose flag is nonetheless flying (a division, squadron, or <a href="/wiki/Flotilla" title="Flotilla">flotilla</a> commander).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="absolute_bearing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bearing_(angle)#Absolute" title="Bearing (angle)">absolute bearing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The bearing of an object in relation to north: either <i>true bearing</i>, using the geographical or <a href="/wiki/True_north" title="True north">true north</a>, or <i>magnetic bearing</i>, using <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_declination" title="Magnetic declination">magnetic north</a>. See also <i><a href="#bearing"><span title="See entry on this page at § bearing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bearing</span></a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Bearing_(angle)#Relative" title="Bearing (angle)">relative bearing</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="accommodation_ladder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Accommodation_ladder" title="Accommodation ladder">accommodation ladder</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A portable flight of steps down a ship's side.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="accommodation_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barracks_ship" title="Barracks ship">accommodation ship</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>accommodation hull</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A ship or <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> used as housing, generally when there is a lack of quarters available ashore. An operational ship can be used, but more commonly a hull modified for accommodation is used.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="act_of_pardon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Act of Pardon</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="Act_of_Grace"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>Act of Grace</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A letter from a state or power authorising action by a <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateer</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_marque" title="Letter of marque">letter of marque</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="action_stations" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">action stations</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#battle_stations"><span title="See entry on this page at § battle stations" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battle stations</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="admiral" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">admiral</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A senior naval officer of flag rank. In ascending order of seniority in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>: rear admiral, vice admiral, admiral, and (until about 2001, when all British five-star ranks were discontinued) <a href="/wiki/Admiral_of_the_fleet" title="Admiral of the fleet">admiral of the fleet</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a>: rear admiral (lower half), rear admiral, vice admiral, admiral, and fleet admiral. The term is derived from the Arabic <i>Amir al-Bahr</i> ("ruler of the sea").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="admiralty" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Admiralty_(navy)" title="Admiralty (navy)">admiralty</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A high naval authority in charge of a state's <span title="See entry on this page at § navy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#navy" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">navy</a></span> or a major territorial component. In the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> (UK), the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Board_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiralty Board (United Kingdom)">Board of Admiralty</a>, executing the office of the <a href="/wiki/Lord_High_Admiral_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Lord High Admiral of the United Kingdom">Lord High Admiral</a>, promulgates naval law in the form of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Regulations" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Regulations"><i>Queen<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s</i> (or king's) <i>Regulations</i></a> and admiralty instructions.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Another name for <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_law" title="Admiralty law">admiralty law</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="admiralty_law" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Admiralty_law" title="Admiralty law">admiralty law</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The body of law that deals with maritime cases. In the UK, it is administered by the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiralty Court">Admiralty Court</a>, a special court within the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Bench" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Bench">Queen's Bench Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court of Justice</a>. The Admiralty Court is now in the Rolls Building.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="adrift" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">adrift</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Afloat and unattached in any way to the shore or seabed, but not <span title="See entry on this page at § underway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#underway" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">underway</a></span>. When referring to a vessel, it implies that the vessel is not being or able to be controlled and therefore goes where the wind and current take her; a vessel in this condition may also be described as "loose from her moorings" or "out of place".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Any gear not fastened down or stored properly.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Any person or thing that is misplaced or missing. When applied to a member of the Navy or Marine Corps, such a person is said to be "absent without leave" (AWOL) or, in U.S. Navy and U.S. Marine Corps terminology, is guilty of an "unauthorized absence" (UA).<sup id="cite_ref-covey_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covey-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="advance_note" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">advance note</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A note for one month's wages issued to a sailor on his signing a <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s articles" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_articles" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's articles</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="adviso" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">adviso</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="/wiki/Aviso" title="Aviso">aviso</a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="afloat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">afloat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(of a vessel) Floating freely (not <a href="#aground"><span title="See entry on this page at § aground" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aground</span></a> or sunk). The term may also be used more generally of any floating object or person.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In service, even if not currently <span title="See entry on this page at § underway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#underway" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">underway</a></span>, but not stranded, crewless, in repair, or under construction (e.g. "the company has 10 ships afloat").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="afore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">afore</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In, on, or toward the <a href="#fore"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore</span></a> or front of a vessel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In front of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aft" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Aft" title="Aft">aft</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Toward the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> or rear of a vessel.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Contrast <i><a href="#fore"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore</span></a></i>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The portion of a vessel behind the middle area of the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="afterbrow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">afterbrow</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On larger ships, a secondary <a href="#gangway"><span title="See entry on this page at § gangway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gangway</span></a> rigged in the area <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> of <span title="See entry on this page at § midship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#midship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">midship</a></span>. On some military vessels, such as U.S. naval vessels, enlisted personnel below E-7 board the ship at the afterbrow; officers and <a href="/wiki/Chief_petty_officer_(United_States)" title="Chief petty officer (United States)">CPO</a>/<a href="/wiki/Senior_chief_petty_officer" title="Senior chief petty officer">SCPO</a>/<a href="/wiki/Master_chief_petty_officer" title="Master chief petty officer">MCPO</a> board the ship at the brow.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aftercastle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Aftercastle" title="Aftercastle">aftercastle</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>sterncastle</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> structure behind the <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzenmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzenmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzenmast</a></span> and above the <span title="See entry on this page at § transom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#transom" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">transom</a></span> on large sailing ships, much larger but less common than a <a href="#forecastle"><span title="See entry on this page at § forecastle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forecastle</span></a>. The aftercastle houses the captain′s cabin and sometimes other cabins and is topped by the <span title="See entry on this page at § poop deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#poop_deck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">poop deck</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="afternoon_watch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">afternoon watch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The 1200–1600 <span title="See entry on this page at § watch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#watch" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">watch</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aground" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aground</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Resting on or touching the ground or land, or the bottom of a body of water (either unintentionally or deliberately, such as in a drying harbour), as opposed to <a href="#afloat"><span title="See entry on this page at § afloat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">afloat</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ahead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ahead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Forward of the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ahoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ahoy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A cry to draw attention. Used to hail a boat or a ship, e.g. "boat ahoy".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ahull" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ahull</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Lying <a href="#broadside"><span title="See entry on this page at § broadside" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">broadside</span></a> to the sea.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To ride out a storm with no sails and <a href="#helm"><span title="See entry on this page at § helm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">helm</span></a> held to <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aid_to_navigation_(aton)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Navigational_aid" title="Navigational aid">aid to navigation</a> (ATON)</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="navigational_aid"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>navigational aid</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Any device external to a vessel or aircraft specifically intended to assist navigators in determining their position or safe course, or to warn them of dangers or obstructions to navigation.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Any sort of marker that aids a traveler in navigation, especially with regard to nautical or aviation travel. Such aids commonly include <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buoy" title="Buoy">buoys</a>, <a href="#fog_signal"><span title="See entry on this page at § fog signal" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fog signals</span></a>, and <a href="#day_beacon"><span title="See entry on this page at § day beacon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">day beacons</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aircraft_carrier" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also simply <b>carrier</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Warship" title="Warship">warship</a> designed with a primary mission of deploying and recovering aircraft while at sea, thereby acting as a seagoing airbase. Since 1918, the term generally has been limited to a warship with an extensive <a href="/wiki/Flight_deck" title="Flight deck">flight deck</a> designed to operate conventional fixed-wing aircraft. In US Navy slang, also called a "flat top" or a "bird farm".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aka" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Polynesian_multihull_terminology" title="Polynesian multihull terminology">aka</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Structural section of a vessel that joins the hulls of a <a href="/wiki/Multihull" title="Multihull">multihulled</a> vessel together.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="alee" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">alee</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;On the <a href="#lee"><span title="See entry on this page at § lee" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lee</span></a> side of a ship.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="all_hands" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">all hands</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship's entire company, including both officers and enlisted personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="all_night_in" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">all night in</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Having no night <span title="See entry on this page at § watch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#watch" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">watches</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="all_standing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">all standing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Bringing a person or thing up short; i.e. an unforeseen and sudden stop.<sup id="cite_ref-covey_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covey-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="allision" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">allision</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The impact of a moving vessel with a stationary object (not submerged), such as a bridge abutment or dolphin, pier or wharf, or another vessel made fast to a pier or wharf. More than incidental contact is required. The vessel is said to "allide" with the fixed object and is considered at fault. Contrast <i><a href="#collision"><span title="See entry on this page at § collision" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">collision</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aloft" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aloft</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In the <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span> of a sailing ship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Above the ship's uppermost solid structure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Overhead or high above.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="alongside" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">alongside</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">By the side of a ship or pier.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ama" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Polynesian_multihull_terminology" title="Polynesian multihull terminology">ama</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A secondary hull or float attached to the primary hull of a vessel for stability, or the hulls of a modern <a href="/wiki/Catamaran" title="Catamaran">catamaran</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="amidships" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">amidships</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A position half way along the length of a ship or boat.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A position half way between the port and starboard sides of a ship or boat, as in "helm amidships", when the rudder is in line with the keel.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ammunition_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ammunition_ship" title="Ammunition ship">ammunition ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A naval <a href="#auxiliary_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § auxiliary ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">auxiliary ship</span></a> specifically configured to carry ammunition, usually for combatant ships and aircraft.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Anchor" title="Anchor">anchor</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Any object designed to prevent or slow the drift of a ship, attached to the ship by a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> or <a href="#anchor_chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">chain</span></a>; usually a metal, hook, or plough-like object designed to grip the solid seabed under the body of water. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § sea anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sea_anchor" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sea anchor</a></span></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To deploy an anchor (e.g. "she anchored offshore").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_ball" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor ball</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A round, black shape hoisted in the forepart of a vessel to show that it is anchored.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_buoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor buoy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small <a href="#buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoy</span></a> secured to a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> attached to the crown of an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>. The line allows the anchor to be unhooked from an obstruction, such as a rock or another vessel's anchor cable, so preventing raising the anchor in the normal way.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_chain" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor chain</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="anchor_cable"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>anchor cable</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A chain connecting a ship to an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_detail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor detail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A group of men who handle ground tackle when the ship is anchoring or getting under way.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_home" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor home</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">When the anchor is secured aboard the ship for sea; i.e. when it is not deployed. Typically rests just outside the <a href="#hawsepipe"><span title="See entry on this page at § hawsepipe" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hawsepipe</span></a> on the outer side of the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>, at the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_light" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor light</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A white light displayed by a ship to indicate that it is at anchor. Two such lights are displayed by a ship over 150 feet (46&#160;m) in length.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_rode" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor rode</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also simply <b>rode</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The anchor line, rope, or cable connecting the <a href="#anchor_chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor chain</span></a> to the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_sentinel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor sentinel</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>kellet</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A separate weight on a separate line that is loosely attached to the <a href="#anchor_rode"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor rode" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor rode</span></a> so that it can slide down it easily. It is made fast at a distance slightly longer than the <a href="#draft"><span title="See entry on this page at § draft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">draft</span></a> of the boat. It is used to prevent the anchor rode from becoming fouled on the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> or other underwater structures when the boat is resting at anchor and moving randomly during <span title="See entry on this page at § slack tide" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#slack_tide" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">slack tide</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_watch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor watch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The crewmen assigned to take care of a ship while it is anchored or moored, and charged with such duties as making sure that the anchor is holding and the vessel is not drifting. Most marine <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">GPS</a> units have an anchor watch alarm capability.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor_winch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor winch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A horizontal <a href="#capstan"><span title="See entry on this page at § capstan" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">capstan</span></a> in the bow used for weighing anchor.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchorage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchorage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any place suitable for a ship to anchor, often an area of a port or harbor.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anchor&#39;s_aweigh" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anchor's aweigh</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Said of an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> to indicate that it is just clear of the bottom and that the ship is therefore no longer anchored.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="andrew" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Andrew</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Traditional lower-deck slang term for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anemometer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Anemometer" title="Anemometer">anemometer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An instrument used to measure wind speed.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aneroid_barometer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Aneroid_barometer" class="mw-redirect" title="Aneroid barometer">aneroid barometer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An instrument used to measure air pressure, often with the aim of predicting changes in weather.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="angle_of_attack" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Angle_of_attack" title="Angle of attack">angle of attack</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The angle between the <a href="/wiki/Apparent_wind" title="Apparent wind">apparent wind</a> and the chord line of the sail.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="angle_on_the_bow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Angle_on_the_bow" class="mw-redirect" title="Angle on the bow">angle on the bow</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A naval submariner's term for the angle between a target's course and the line of sight to the submarine. It is expressed as port or starboard, so never exceeds 180 degrees. This is one of the figures entered into the Torpedo Data Computer that makes all the calculations necessary for a <a href="/wiki/Torpedo" title="Torpedo">torpedo</a> attack on the target. Not to be confused with <i><a href="#doubling_the_angle_on_the_bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § doubling the angle on the bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">doubling the angle on the bow</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="answer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">answer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The expected response of a vessel to control mechanisms, such as a turn "answering" to the <span title="See entry on this page at § wheel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#wheel" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">wheel</a></span> and <span title="See entry on this page at § rudder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rudder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rudder</a></span>. "She won't answer" might be the report from a helmsman when turning the wheel under a pilot's order fails to produce the expected change of direction.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anti-rolling_tanks" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anti-rolling tanks</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pair of fluid-filled tanks mounted on opposite sides of a ship below the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>. The tanks are cross-linked by piping or ducts to allow water to flow between them and at the top by vents or air pipes. The piping is sized so that as the fluid flows from side to side it damps the amount of <span title="See entry on this page at § roll" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#roll" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">roll</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anti-submarine_net" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_net" title="Anti-submarine net">anti-submarine net</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>anti-submarine boom</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A heavy underwater net attached to a boom and placed so as to protect a harbor, anchorage, or strait from penetration by submerged <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="apeak" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">apeak</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">More or less vertical. Having the <a href="#anchor_rode"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor rode" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor rode</span></a> or <a href="#anchor_chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">chain</span></a> as nearly vertical as possible without freeing the <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aport" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aport</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Toward the <span title="See entry on this page at § port" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#port" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">port</a></span> side of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="apron" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">apron</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A piece of wood fitted to the after side of the <span title="See entry on this page at § stem" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stem" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stem</a></span> post and the fore side of the <span title="See entry on this page at § sternpost" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sternpost" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sternpost</a></span> of a <a href="#clinker"><span title="See entry on this page at § clinker" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clinker-built</span></a> boat, where the planking is secured.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdmiralty_manual_of_seamanship1972242_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdmiralty_manual_of_seamanship1972242-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="apparent_wind" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Apparent_wind" title="Apparent wind">apparent wind</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The combination of the true wind and the headwind caused by the boat's forward motion. For example, it causes a light side wind to appear to come from well ahead of the <a href="#beam"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beam</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="arc_of_visibility" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">arc of visibility</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The portion of the horizon over which a lighted <a href="#aid_to_navigation"><span title="See entry on this page at § aid to navigation" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aid to navigation</span></a> is visible from <span title="See entry on this page at § seaward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#seaward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">seaward</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="archboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">archboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A plank along the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> where the name of a ship is commonly painted.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="armament" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">armament</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship's complement of weapons.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="armor_belt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">armor belt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><dfn id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)#belt_armor" title="Glossary of nautical terms (A-L)"><span title="See entry at: Glossary of nautical terms (A-L) § belt armor" style="color:inherit;" class="glossary-link">belt armor</span></a></dfn></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="armory" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">armory</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Area on a warship for storage of <a href="/wiki/Small_arms" class="mw-redirect" title="Small arms">small arms</a> and ammunition.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="articles_of_war" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Articles_of_War" title="Articles of War">Articles of War</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Regulations governing the military and <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">naval</a> forces of the UK and US; read to every <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s company" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_company" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's company</a></span> on <a href="#commission"><span title="See entry on this page at § commission" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">commissioning</span></a> and at specified intervals during the commission.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="as_the_crow_flies" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">as the crow flies</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">As measured by a straight line between two points (which might cross land), in the way that a crow or other bird would be capable of traveling rather than a ship, which must go around land. See also <i><a href="#great_circle"><span title="See entry on this page at § great circle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">great circle</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="asdic" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/ASDIC" class="mw-redirect" title="ASDIC">ASDIC</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Purportedly an acronym for Allied Submarine Devices Investigation Committee, and a type of <a href="/wiki/SONAR" class="mw-redirect" title="SONAR">SONAR</a> used by the Allies for detecting submarines during the First and Second World Wars. The term has been generically applied to equipment for "under-water supersonic echo-ranging equipment" of submarines and other vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-Abbot_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbot-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ashore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ashore</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;On the beach, shore, or land (as opposed to <a href="#aboard"><span title="See entry on this page at § aboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aboard</span></a> or <i>on board</i> a vessel).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Towards the shore.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;"To run ashore": to collide with the shore (as opposed to "to run <a href="#aground"><span title="See entry on this page at § aground" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aground</span></a>", which is to strike a submerged feature such as a reef or sandbar).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="assembly_station" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">assembly station</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><span title="See entry on this page at § muster station" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#muster_station" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">muster station</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="astarboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">astarboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Toward the <span title="See entry on this page at § starboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#starboard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">starboard</a></span> side of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="astern" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">astern</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Toward the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> or rear of a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Behind a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="astern_gear" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">astern gear</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The gear or gears that, when engaged with an engine or motor, result in backwards movement or force. Equivalent to reverse in a manual-transmission automobile.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="asylum_harbour" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">asylum harbour</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A harbour used to provide shelter from a storm. See <i><a href="#harbor_of_refuge"><span title="See entry on this page at § harbor of refuge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">harbor of refuge</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="asw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ASW</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An acronym for <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine warfare</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="athwart" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">athwart</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="athwartships" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">athwartships</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">At right angles to the <a href="#fore"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore</span></a> and <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> or centerline of a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="auxiliary_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_ship" title="Auxiliary ship">auxiliary ship</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="auxiliary"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also simply <b>auxiliary</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A naval ship designed to operate in any number of roles supporting combatant ships and other naval operations, including a wide range of activities related to replenishment, transport, repair, harbor services and research.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="avast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">avast</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Stop, cease or desist from whatever is being done. From the Dutch <i>hou' vast</i> ("hold on"), the imperative form of <i>vasthouden</i> ("to hold on to") or the Italian word <i>basta</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-covey_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covey-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Compare <i><span title="See entry on this page at § Ya basta" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#Ya_basta" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">Ya basta</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aviso" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aviso</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="adviso"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Formerly also <b>adviso</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A kind of <a href="#dispatch_boat"><span title="See entry on this page at § dispatch boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dispatch boat</span></a> or advice boat. Survives particularly in the French Navy. They are considered equivalent to modern <span title="See entry on this page at § sloop" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sloop" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sloops</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="awash" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">awash</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">So low in the water that the water is constantly washing across the surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aweigh" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aweigh</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The position of an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> that is just clear of making contact with the bottom.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="axial_fire" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">axial fire</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Fire oriented towards the ends of the ship; the opposite of <a href="#broadside"><span title="See entry on this page at § broadside" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">broadside</span></a> fire. In the Age of Sail, this was known as "raking fire".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aye,_aye" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aye, aye</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>) A reply to an order or command to indicate that it, firstly, is heard; and, secondly, is understood and will be carried out (e.g. "Aye, aye, sir" to officers). Also the proper reply from a hailed boat, to indicate that an officer is on board.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="azimuth_circle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">azimuth circle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An instrument used to take the bearings of celestial objects.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="azimuth_compass" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Azimuth_compass" title="Azimuth compass">azimuth compass</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An instrument employed for ascertaining the position of the Sun with respect to <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_north" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnetic north">magnetic north</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Azimuth" title="Azimuth">azimuth</a> of an object is its <a href="#bearing"><span title="See entry on this page at § bearing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bearing</span></a> from the observer measured as an angle clockwise from <a href="/wiki/True_north" title="True north">true north</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="azimuth_thruster" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Azimuth_thruster" title="Azimuth thruster">azimuth thruster</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Steerable drive leg fitted through the bottom of a hull, carrying a propeller. Compare with <span title="See entry on this page at § stern drive" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern_drive" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern drive</a></span> and <span title="See entry on this page at § sail drive" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail_drive" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail drive</a></span> </dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="B">B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="b_&amp;_r_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">B &amp; R rig</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A style of standing rigging used on sailboats that lacks a <a href="#backstay"><span title="See entry on this page at § backstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">backstay</span></a>. The mast is said to be supported like a "tripod", with swept-back spreaders and a <a href="#forestay"><span title="See entry on this page at § forestay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forestay</span></a>. Used widely on Hunter brand sailboats, among others. Designed and named by Lars Bergstrom and Sven Ridder.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="back" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">back</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To make a sail fill with wind on the opposite side normally used for sailing forward. A fore and aft headsail is backed by either not moving the sail across when tacking, or by hauling it to windward with the weather sheet. A square sail is backed by hauling the yards round with the braces. The sail is then <a href="#aback"><span title="See entry on this page at § aback" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aback</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(With <span title="See entry on this page at § oars" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#oars" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">oars</a></span>) to push against the water with the oar in the opposite direction than normally used for moving the boat forward. This is used to slow the speed of the boat, or to move astern when manoeuvring.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="back_and_fill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">back and fill</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="back_and_fill"></span>
<dd class="glossary">A method of keeping a square-rigged vessel under control while drifting with the tide along a narrow channel. The ship lies <a href="#broadside"><span title="See entry on this page at § broadside" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">broadside</span></a> to the current, with the main <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span> backed and the fore and mizzen topsail full: essentially a <a href="#heave_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § heave to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hove-to</span></a> position. Selective backing and filling of these sails moves the ship <a href="#ahead"><span title="See entry on this page at § ahead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ahead</span></a> or <a href="#astern"><span title="See entry on this page at § astern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">astern</span></a>, so allowing it to be kept in the best part of the channel. A <a href="#jib"><span title="See entry on this page at § jib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jib</span></a> and the <span title="See entry on this page at § spanker" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spanker" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spanker</a></span> are used to help balance the sail plan. This method cannot be used if the wind is going in the same direction and at the same speed as the tide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarland1984199–202_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarland1984199–202-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="backstay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Backstay" title="Backstay">backstay</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A stay or cable, reaching from the mast heads, of the <a href="/wiki/Topmast" title="Topmast">topmast</a>, the <span title="See entry on this page at § topgallant-mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topgallant-mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topgallant-mast</a></span> the <span title="See entry on this page at § royal-mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#royal-mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">royal-mast</a></span>, the <span title="See entry on this page at § skysail-mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#skysail-mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">skysail-mast</a></span> to the ship's side abaft the lower rigging; used to support the mast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="back_wash" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">back wash</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Water forced <a href="#astern"><span title="See entry on this page at § astern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">astern</span></a> by the action of the <span title="See entry on this page at § propeller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#propeller" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">propeller</a></span>. Also, the receding of waves.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="baggywrinkle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Baggywrinkle" title="Baggywrinkle">baggywrinkle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A soft covering for standing rigging (such as <a href="/wiki/Shroud_(sailing)" title="Shroud (sailing)">shrouds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stays_(nautical)" title="Stays (nautical)">stays</a>) that reduces sail chafing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bailer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hand_bailer" class="mw-redirect" title="Hand bailer">bailer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any device for removing water that has entered a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bail_out" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bail out</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Tacking away from other boats to obtain <i>clear air</i>. Often used for starting situations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="baldie" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">baldie</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of Scottish sailboat introduced in 1860, used for fishing. A baldie is <a href="/wiki/Carvel_(boat_building)" title="Carvel (boat building)">carvel</a>-built, with her mast far forward and rigged with a lug sail and sometimes a <a href="#jib"><span title="See entry on this page at § jib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jib</span></a>. Some historians believe "Baldie" is a contraction of "Garibaldi", a reference to the Italian general and nationalist <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>, whose name was a household word at the time the baldie was introduced.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="balance_rudder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">balance rudder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Actually not a single rudder, but a set of three or four rudders operating together to maneuver a sternwheel steamboat. Placed just forward of the paddlewheels, the effectiveness of the balance rudder is increased by the flow of water generated by the paddles, giving such steamboats a high degree of maneuverability.<sup id="cite_ref-hunter1993_pp173-174_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hunter1993_pp173-174-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ballast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ballast" title="Ballast">ballast</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Heavy material that is placed in a position low in the hull to provide stability. It can be moveable material, such as gravel or stones, permanently or semi-permanently installed, or integral to the hull, such as the (typically) lead or cast-iron ballast keel of a sailing yacht. See also <i><a href="#in_ballast"><span title="See entry on this page at § in ballast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">in ballast</span></a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ballast_tank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ballast_tank" title="Ballast tank">ballast tank</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A compartment which can be filled  or partly filled with water, used on ships, submarines and other submersibles to control buoyancy and stability.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="baltimore_clipper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Clipper" title="Baltimore Clipper">Baltimore Clipper</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fast sailing ship&#160;&#8211;&#32;an early form of <a href="#clipper"><span title="See entry on this page at § clipper" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clipper</span></a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;built on the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_seaboard" title="Mid-Atlantic seaboard">Mid-Atlantic seaboard</a> of the United States, especially at <a href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimore, Maryland">Baltimore, Maryland</a>. Popular as <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant ship</a></span>s in both the United States and the United Kingdom by the late 18th century, Baltimore Clippers usually were two-<span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>ed <span title="See entry on this page at § schooner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#schooner" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">schooner</a></span>s or <a href="#brigantine"><span title="See entry on this page at § brigantine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">brigantine</span></a>s. </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="balls_to_four_watch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">balls to four watch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The 0000–0400 <a href="/wiki/Watch_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Watch system">watch</a> (US Navy).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bank_(topography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank (topography)">bank</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large area of elevated sea floor, deep enough to allow navigation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="banyan" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Banyan_(nautical_term)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Banyan (nautical term) (page does not exist)">banyan</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A traditional Royal Navy term for a day or less of rest and relaxation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bar" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">bar</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Mass of sand or earth raised above the general seabed depth by the motion of water. Bars are often found at the mouth of rivers or entrances to harbours and can make navigation over them extremely dangerous at some states of tide and current flow, but can also confer tranquility in the inshore waters by acting as a barrier to large waves. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § touch and go" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#touch_and_go" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">touch and go</a></span></i> and <i><a href="#grounding"><span title="See entry on this page at § grounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">grounding</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bar_pilot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Maritime_pilot" title="Maritime pilot">bar pilot</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A navigator who guides a ship over dangerous sandbars at the mouths of rivers and bays.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barber_hauler" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Running_rigging#Shaping" title="Running rigging">barber hauler</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A technique of temporarily rigging a sailboat lazy sheet so as to allow the boat to sail closer to the wind; i.e. using the lazy jib sheet to pull the <a href="#jib"><span title="See entry on this page at § jib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jib</span></a> closer to the mid line, allowing a point of sail that would otherwise not be achievable.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barbette" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barbette" title="Barbette">barbette</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A fixed armored enclosure protecting a ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s guns aboard warships without gun turrets, generally taking the form of a ring of armor over which guns mounted on an open-topped rotating turntable could fire, particularly on ships built during the second half of the 19th century.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The inside fixed trunk of a warship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s turreted gun-mounting, on which the turret revolves, containing the hoists for shells and cordite from the shell-room and magazine, particularly on ships built after the late 19th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barca-longa" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barca-longa" title="Barca-longa">barca-longa</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A two- or three-masted <a href="#lugger"><span title="See entry on this page at § lugger" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lugger</span></a> used for fishing on the coasts of Spain and Portugal and more widely in the Mediterranean Sea in the late 17th and 18th centuries. The British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> also used them for shore raids and as <a href="#dispatch_boat"><span title="See entry on this page at § dispatch boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dispatch boats</span></a> in the Mediterranean.</dd>
