<dt class="glossary" id="bareboat_charter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bareboat_charter" title="Bareboat charter">bareboat charter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An arrangement for the chartering or hiring of a vessel, whereby the vessel<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s owner provides no crew or provisions as part of the agreement; instead, the people who rent the vessel are responsible for crewing and provisioning her.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bare_poles" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bare poles</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Sailing without any <a href="#canvas"><span title="See entry on this page at § canvas" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">canvas</span></a> raised, usually in a strong wind.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barge" title="Barge">barge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A towed or self-propelled flat-bottomed boat, built mainly for river, canal or coastal transport of heavy goods.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<i>Admiral<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s barge</i>: A boat at the disposal of an <a href="#admiral"><span title="See entry on this page at § admiral" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">admiral</span></a> for his or her use as transportation between a larger vessel and the shore, or within a harbor.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barge_slip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ferry_slip" title="Ferry slip">barge slip</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A specialized docking facility designed to receive a <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a> or <a href="#car_float"><span title="See entry on this page at § car float" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">car float</span></a> that is used to carry wheeled vehicles across a body of water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bark" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bark</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An alternate spelling of <a href="#barque"><span title="See entry on this page at § barque" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barque</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barkentine" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">barkentine</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An alternate spelling of <a href="#barquentine"><span title="See entry on this page at § barquentine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barquentine</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barque" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barque" title="Barque">barque</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also spelled <b>bark</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing vessel of three or more masts, with all masts <a href="/wiki/Square_rig" title="Square rig">square-rigged</a> except the sternmost, which is <a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rigged</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barquentine" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barquentine" title="Barquentine">barquentine</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also spelled <b>barkentine</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing vessel with three or more masts, with all masts <a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rigged</a> except the foremast, which is <a href="/wiki/Square_rig" title="Square rig">square-rigged</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barrack_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">barrack ship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship or craft designed to function as a floating <a href="/wiki/Barracks" title="Barracks">barracks</a> for housing military personnel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barratry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barratry_(admiralty_law)" title="Barratry (admiralty law)">barratry</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In <a href="#admiralty_law"><span title="See entry on this page at § admiralty law" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">admiralty law</span></a>, an act of gross misconduct against a <a href="/wiki/Shipowner" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipowner">shipowner</a> or a ship's <a href="/wiki/Demise_charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Demise charter">demise charterer</a> by a ship′s master or crew that damages the ship or its <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">cargo</a>. Acts of barratry can include <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">desertion</a>, illegal <span title="See entry on this page at § scuttling" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#scuttling" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">scuttling</a></span>, theft of the ship or cargo and committing any actions that may not be in the shipowner's or demise charterer′s best interests.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barometer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barometer" title="Barometer">barometer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An instrument for measuring air pressure. Used in weather forecasting.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="barrelman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Barrelman" title="Barrelman">barrelman</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailor stationed in the <a href="#crow&#39;s_nest"><span title="See entry on this page at § crow&#39;s nest" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crow's nest</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="batten" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Sail_batten" title="Sail batten">batten</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A stiff strip used to support the <span title="See entry on this page at § roach" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#roach" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">roach</a></span> of a sail, increasing the sail area.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Any thin strip of material (wood, plastic, etc.).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="batten_down_the_hatches" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Batten_down_the_hatches" class="mw-redirect" title="Batten down the hatches">batten down the hatches</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To prepare for inclement weather by securing the closed <a href="/wiki/Cargo_hatch" class="mw-redirect" title="Cargo hatch">cargo hatch</a> covers with wooden <a href="#batten"><span title="See entry on this page at § batten" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battens</span></a> so as to prevent water from entering from any angle.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="battle_stations" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/General_quarters" title="General quarters">battle stations</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>general quarters</b> or <b>action stations</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;An announcement made aboard a naval warship to signal the crew to prepare for battle, imminent damage, or any other emergency (such as a fire).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Specific positions in a naval warship to which one or more crew members are assigned when battle stations is called.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="battlecruiser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Battlecruiser" title="Battlecruiser">battlecruiser</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of large <a href="#capital_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § capital ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">capital ship</span></a> of the first half of the 20th century, similar in size, appearance, and cost to a <a href="#battleship"><span title="See entry on this page at § battleship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battleship</span></a> and typically armed with the same kind of heavy guns, but much more lightly armored (on the scale of a <a href="#cruiser"><span title="See entry on this page at § cruiser" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cruiser</span></a>) and therefore faster than a battleship but more vulnerable to damage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="battleship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Battleship" title="Battleship">battleship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of large, heavily armored warship of the second half of the 19th century and first half of the 20th century, armed with heavy-caliber guns and designed to fight other battleships in a <a href="#line_of_battle"><span title="See entry on this page at § line of battle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line of battle</span></a>. It was the successor to the <span title="See entry on this page at § ship-of-the-line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship-of-the-line" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship-of-the-line</a></span> used during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beaching" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Beaching_(nautical)" title="Beaching (nautical)">beaching</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Deliberately running a vessel <a href="#aground"><span title="See entry on this page at § aground" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aground</span></a> so as to load or unload it (as with <a href="/wiki/Landing_craft" title="Landing craft">landing craft</a>), or sometimes to prevent a damaged vessel from sinking or to facilitate repairs below the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beacon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Beacon" title="Beacon">beacon</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A lighted or unlighted fixed <a href="#aid_to_navigation"><span title="See entry on this page at § aid to navigation" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aid to navigation</span></a> attached directly to the Earth's surface. Examples include lighthouses and daybeacons.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beakhead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Beakhead" title="Beakhead">beakhead</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The ram on the prow of a fighting <a href="#galley"><span title="See entry on this page at § galley" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">galley</span></a> of ancient and medieval times.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The protruding part of the foremost section of a sailing ship of the 16th to the 18th centuries, usually ornate, which was used as a working platform by sailors handling the sails of the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a>. It also housed the crew<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s heads (toilets).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Beam_(nautical)" title="Beam (nautical)">beam</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The width of a vessel at its widest point, or a point alongside the ship at the midpoint of its length.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beam_ends" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">beam ends</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The sides of a ship. To describe a ship as "on her beam ends" may mean the vessel is literally on her side and possibly about to capsize; more often, the phrase means the vessel is listing 45 degrees or more.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beam_reach" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">beam reach</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Sailing with the wind coming across the vessel's <a href="#beam"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beam</span></a>. This is normally the fastest <span title="See entry on this page at § point of sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#point_of_sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">point of sail</a></span> for a <a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rigged</a> vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beam_sea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">beam sea</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sea in which waves are moving perpendicular to a vessel's course.<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_V3_1965_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders_V3_1965-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beam_wind" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">beam wind</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A wind blowing perpendicular to a vessel's course.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bear" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bear</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large, squared-off stone used with sand for scraping wooden decks clean.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bear_down" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bear down</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="bear_away"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bear away</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">To turn or steer a vessel away from the wind, often with reference to a transit.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bear_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bear up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To turn or steer a vessel into the wind.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bearing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bearing_(navigation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bearing (navigation)">bearing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The horizontal direction of a line of sight between two objects on the surface of the Earth. See also <i><a href="#absolute_bearing"><span title="See entry on this page at § absolute bearing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">absolute bearing</span></a></i> and <i><span title="See entry on this page at § relative bearing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#relative_bearing" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">relative bearing</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beat_to_quarters" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Beat_to_quarters" class="mw-redirect" title="Beat to quarters">beat to quarters</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Prepare for battle (in reference to beating a drum to signal the need for battle preparation).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beating_or_beat_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Points_of_sail" class="mw-redirect" title="Points of sail">beating or beat to</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="beat_to"></span>
<dd class="glossary">Sailing as close as possible towards the wind (perhaps only about 60°) in a zig-zag course so as to attain an upwind direction into which it is otherwise impossible to sail directly. See also <i><a href="/wiki/Tacking_(sailing)" title="Tacking (sailing)">tacking (sailing)</a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="beaufort_scale" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Beaufort_scale" title="Beaufort scale">Beaufort scale</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A scale describing wind speed, devised by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Beaufort" title="Francis Beaufort">Admiral Sir Francis Beaufort</a> in 1808, in which winds are graded by the effects of their force on the surface of the sea or on a vessel (originally, the amount of sail that a fully rigged frigate could carry).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="becalm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">becalm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To cut off the wind from a sailing vessel, either by the proximity of land or by another vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="becalmed" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">becalmed</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Unable to move due to a lack of wind, said of a sailing vessel; resigned merely to drift with the current rather to move by controlled management of sails.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="becket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">becket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short piece of <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> usually <span title="See entry on this page at § spliced" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spliced" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spliced</a></span> into a circle or with an <a href="#eye_splice"><span title="See entry on this page at § eye splice" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">eye</span></a> on either end.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="before_the_mast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">before the mast</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Literally, the area of a ship before the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a> (the <a href="#forecastle"><span title="See entry on this page at § forecastle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forecastle</span></a>). Most often used to refer to men whose living quarters are located here: officers were typically quartered in the sternmost areas of the ship (near the <span title="See entry on this page at § quarterdeck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#quarterdeck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">quarterdeck</a></span>), while officer-trainees lived between the two ends of the ship and become known as "midshipmen". Crew members who started out as seamen and then became midshipmen, and later, officers, were said to have gone from "one end of the ship to the other". See also <i><a href="#hawsepiper"><span title="See entry on this page at § hawsepiper" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hawsepiper</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="belay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">belay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To make fast a line around a fitting, usually a cleat or <a href="#belaying_pin"><span title="See entry on this page at § belaying pin" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">belaying pin</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To secure a climbing person in a similar manner.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;An order to halt a current activity or countermand an order prior to execution.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="belaying_pin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Belaying_pin" title="Belaying pin">belaying pin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short movable bar of iron or hard wood to which running rigging may be secured, or "belayed". Belaying pins are inserted in holes in a pin-rail.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s bell" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_bell" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's bell</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bell_rope" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bell rope</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short length of <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> made fast to the clapper of the <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s bell" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_bell" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's bell</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bell_buoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bell buoy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <a href="#buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoy</span></a> with a large bell and hanging hammers that sound by wave action.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="below" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">below</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On or into a lower deck.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="below_decks" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">below decks</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In or into any of the spaces below the main deck of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="belt_armor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Belt_armor" title="Belt armor">belt armor</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>armor belt</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A layer of heavy metal armor plated onto or within the outer <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> of a warship, typically on <a href="#battleship"><span title="See entry on this page at § battleship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battleships</span></a>, <a href="#battlecruiser"><span title="See entry on this page at § battlecruiser" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battlecruisers</span></a>, <a href="#cruiser"><span title="See entry on this page at § cruiser" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cruisers</span></a> and <a href="#aircraft_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § aircraft carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aircraft carriers</span></a>, usually covering the warship from her main deck down to some distance below the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>. If built within the hull, rather than forming the outer hull, the belt would be installed at an inclined angle to improve the warship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s protection from shells striking the hull.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bend" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/List_of_bend_knots" title="List of bend knots">bend</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A knot used to join two ropes or lines. See also <i><a href="#hitch"><span title="See entry on this page at § hitch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hitch</span></a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To attach a rope to an object.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Fastening a sail to a yard.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiddlecombe19902_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiddlecombe19902-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bermuda_rig_or_bermudan_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bermuda_rig" title="Bermuda rig">Bermuda rig</a> or Bermudan rig</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A triangular <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span>, without any upper <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span>, which is hoisted up the mast by a single <a href="#halyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § halyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">halyard</span></a> attached to the head of the sail. This configuration, introduced to Europe about 1920, allows the use of a tall mast, enabling sails to be set higher where wind speed is greater.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bermuda_sloop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bermuda_sloop" title="Bermuda sloop">Bermuda sloop</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rigged</a> sailing vessel with a single mast setting a <a href="#bermuda_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § Bermuda rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Bermuda rig</span></a> mainsail and a single <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a>. The Bermuda sloop is a very common type of modern sailing yacht.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="berth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Berth_(moorings)" title="Berth (moorings)">berth</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A location in a port or harbor used specifically for mooring vessels while not at sea.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A safe margin of distance to be kept by a vessel from another vessel or from an obstruction, hence the phrase "to give a wide berth".<sup id="cite_ref-Bathe_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bathe-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A bed or sleeping accommodation on a boat or ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="best_bower_(anchor)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">best bower (<a href="/wiki/Anchor" title="Anchor">anchor</a>)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The larger of two <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchors</span></a> carried in the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>; so named as it was the last, "best" hope for anchoring a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="between_the_devil_and_the_deep_blue_sea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">between the devil and the deep blue sea</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#devil_seam"><span title="See entry on this page at § devil seam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">devil seam</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="between_wind_and_water" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">between wind and water</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The part of a ship's <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> that is sometimes submerged and sometimes brought above water by the rolling of the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bight" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bight</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A loop in a rope or line – a hitch or knot tied "on the bight" is one tied in the middle of a rope, without access to the ends.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An indentation in a coastline.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bilander" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bilander" title="Bilander">bilander</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="billander"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>billander</b> or <b>be<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>landre</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A small European merchant sailing ship with two masts, the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainmast</a></span> <a href="#lateen_rigging"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen-rigged</span></a> with a trapezoidal <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span>, and the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a> carrying the conventional square course and square <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span>. Used in the Netherlands for coast and canal traffic and occasionally in the North Sea, but more frequently used in the Mediterranean Sea.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bilge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bilge" title="Bilge">bilge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The part of the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> that the ship rests on if it takes the ground; the outer end of the <a href="#floor"><span title="See entry on this page at § floor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">floor</span></a>s. The "turn of the bilge" is the part of the hull that changes from the (approximately) vertical sides of the hull to the more horizontal bottom of the ship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteffy2013_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteffy2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(Usually in the plural: "bilges") The compartment at the bottom of the hull of a ship or boat where water collects and must be pumped out of the vessel; the space between the bottom hull planking and the ceiling of the hold.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;To damage the hull in the area of the bilge, usually by <a href="#grounding"><span title="See entry on this page at § grounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">grounding</span></a> or hitting an obstruction.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;To fail an academic course ("bilge") or curriculum ("bilge out").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bilge_keel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bilge_keel" title="Bilge keel">bilge keel</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of a pair of <a href="#keel"><span title="See entry on this page at § keel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">keels</span></a> on either side of the hull, usually slanted outwards. In <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yachts</a>, they allow the use of a drying mooring, the boat standing upright on the keels (and often a <i>skeg</i>) when the tide is out.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bilged_on_her_anchor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bilged on her anchor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship that has run upon her own <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> such that the <a href="#anchor_chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor cable</span></a> runs under the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bill" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bill</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The extremity of the arm of an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>; the point of or beyond the fluke.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="billethead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Billethead" class="mw-redirect" title="Billethead">billethead</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;On smaller vessels, a smaller, non-figural carving, most often a curl of foliage, might be substituted for a <a href="/wiki/Figurehead" title="Figurehead">figurehead</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A round piece of timber at the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> or <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> of a whaleboat, around which the harpoon line is run out when the whale darts off.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bimini_top" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bimini_top" title="Bimini top">Bimini top</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An open-front canvas top for the cockpit of a boat, usually supported by a metal frame.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bimmy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flagellation" title="Flagellation">bimmy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A punitive instrument.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="binnacle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Binnacle" title="Binnacle">binnacle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The stand on which the ship's <a href="#compass"><span title="See entry on this page at § compass" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">compass</span></a> is mounted, usually near the <a href="#helm"><span title="See entry on this page at § helm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">helm</span></a>, permitting ready reference by the <a href="#helmsman"><span title="See entry on this page at § helmsman" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">helmsman</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="binnacle_list" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">binnacle list</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship's sick list. The list of men unable to report for duty was given to the officer or mate of the watch by the ship's surgeon. The list was kept at the <a href="#binnacle"><span title="See entry on this page at § binnacle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">binnacle</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bird_farm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bird farm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">United States Navy slang for an <a href="#aircraft_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § aircraft carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aircraft carrier</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bite" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bite</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Verb used in reference to a <span title="See entry on this page at § rudder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rudder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rudder</a></span>, as in "the rudder begins to bite". When a vessel has steerageway the rudder will act to steer the vessel, i.e. it has enough water flow past it to steer with. Physically this is noticeable with tiller or unassisted wheel steering by the rudder exhibiting resistance to being turned from the straight ahead – this resistance is the rudder "biting" and is how a helmsman first senses that a vessel has acquired steerageway.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bitt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bitt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A post or pair of posts mounted on the ship's <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> for fastening ropes or cables.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A strong vertical timber or iron fastened through the deck beams that is used for securing ropes or <a href="#hawser"><span title="See entry on this page at § hawser" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hawsers</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bitt_heads" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bitt heads</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The tops of two massive timbers that support the <span title="See entry on this page at § windlass" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windlass" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windlass</a></span> on a sailing barge.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bitter_end" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Knot#Bitter_end" title="Knot">bitter end</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The last part or loose end of a rope or cable. The <a href="#anchor_cable"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor cable" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor cable</span></a> is tied to the <a href="#bitt"><span title="See entry on this page at § bitt" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bitts</span></a>; when the cable is fully paid out, the bitter end has been reached.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="black_gang" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Black_gang_(ship)" title="Black gang (ship)">black gang</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The engineering crew of the vessel, i.e. crew members who work in the vessel<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s engine room, fire room and/or boiler room, so called because they would typically be covered in coal dust during the days of coal-fired steamships.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="blinker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">blinker</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A search light, used for signaling by code. Usually fitted with a spring controlled shutter.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="block" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Block_(sailing)" title="Block (sailing)">block</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pulley with one or more <span title="See entry on this page at § sheave" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheave" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheaves</a></span> or grooves over which a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> is roved. It can be used to change the direction of the line, or in pairs used to form a tackle.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="block,_fiddle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">block, fiddle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A block with two <span title="See entry on this page at § sheave" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheave" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheaves</a></span> in the same plane, one being smaller than the other, giving the block a somewhat violin appearance.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="block,_snatch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">block, snatch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A single <span title="See entry on this page at § sheave" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheave" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheave</a></span> block with one end of the frame hinged and able to be opened, so as to admit a line other than by forcing an end through the opening.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="blockship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Blockship" title="Blockship">blockship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A vessel sunk deliberately to block a waterway to prevent the waterway′s use by an enemy.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="blue_ensign" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Blue_Ensign" title="Blue Ensign">Blue Ensign</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A flag flown as an <a href="#ensign"><span title="See entry on this page at § ensign" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ensign</span></a> by certain British ships. Prior to 1864, ships of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>′s <a href="/wiki/Coloured_squadrons_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Coloured squadrons of the Royal Navy">Blue Squadron</a> flew it; since the reorganisation of the Royal Navy in 1864 eliminated its naval use, it has been flown instead by British merchant vessels whose officers and crew include a certain prescribed number (which has varied over the years) of retired Royal Navy or <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Reserve" title="Royal Naval Reserve">Royal Naval Reserve</a> personnel or are commanded by an officer of the Royal Naval Reserve in possession of a government warrant; Royal Research Ships by warrant, regardless of their manning by naval, naval reserve and <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant Navy">Merchant Navy</a> personnel; or British-registered <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yachts</a> belonging to members of certain <a href="/wiki/Yacht_club" title="Yacht club">yacht clubs</a>, although yachts were prohibited from flying the Blue Ensign during World War I and World War II.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="blue_peter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/International_maritime_signal_flags" title="International maritime signal flags">Blue Peter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A blue and white flag (the flag for the letter <i>P</i>) hoisted at the foretrucks of ships about to sail. Formerly a white ship on a blue ground, but later a white square on a blue ground.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bluejacket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bluejacket</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">also <b>blue-jacket</b></span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § sailor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sailor" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sailor</a></span> or <a href="/wiki/Enlisted_personnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlisted personnel">enlisted person</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> navies, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a>. <i>Bluejacket</i> derives from a blue jacket naval enlisted personnel once wore while ashore. In the Royal Navy and Commonwealth navies, the term generally is synonymous with <i><span title="See entry on this page at § rating" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rating" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rating</a></span></i> and often includes <a href="/wiki/Petty_officer" title="Petty officer">petty officers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chief_petty_officer" title="Chief petty officer">chief petty officers</a>. In the U.S. Navy and U.S. Coast Guard, the term excludes chief petty officers.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;More loosely, a sailor or enlisted person of any navy.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="&#39;&#39;bluejacket&#39;s_manual&#39;&#39;" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/The_Bluejacket%27s_Manual" title="The Bluejacket&#39;s Manual"><i>Bluejacket's Manual</i></a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Basic handbook for U.S. Navy personnel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="board" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">board</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To step onto, climb onto or otherwise enter a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The side of a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The distance a sailing vessel runs between <span title="See entry on this page at § tacking" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tacking" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tacks</a></span> when working to <span title="See entry on this page at § windward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windward</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boat" title="Boat">boat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Any small craft or vessel designed to float on and provide transport over or under water.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Naval slang for a <span title="See entry on this page at § submarine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#submarine" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">submarine</a></span> of any size.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boat_hook" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boat_hook" title="Boat hook">boat hook</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pole with a blunt tip and a hook on the end, sometimes with a ring on its opposite end to which a line may be attached. Typically used to assist in docking and undocking a boat, with its hook used to pull a boat towards a dock and the blunt end to push it away from a dock, as well as to reach into the water to help people catch <a href="#buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoys</span></a> or other floating objects or to reach people in the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boat_keeper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boat keeper</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A boatkeeper was a <a href="/wiki/Sailor" title="Sailor">sailor</a> that knew the harbor thoroughly and was able to act as a pilot. He was in command after the last pilot had left to board a ship and brought the pilot boat back to harbor. He was required to know how to use a <a href="/wiki/Sextant" title="Sextant">sextant</a> as he could be 300 miles from port.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boathouse" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boathouse" title="Boathouse">boathouse</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A building especially designed for the storage of boats, typically located on open water such as a lake or river. Boathouses are normally used to store smaller sports or leisure craft, often <a href="/wiki/Rowing_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Rowing boat">rowing boats</a> but sometimes craft such as <a href="/wiki/Punt_(boat)" title="Punt (boat)">punts</a> or small <a href="/wiki/Motor_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor boat">motor boats</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatsteerer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boatsteerer" title="Boatsteerer">boatsteerer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A member of the crew of a 19th-century whaling ship responsible for pulling the forward oar of a whaleboat and for harpooning whales.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatswain" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boatswain" title="Boatswain">boatswain</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="bosun"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bosun</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A non-commissioned officer responsible for the sails, ropes, rigging and boats on a ship who issues "piped" commands to seamen.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatswain&#39;s_call" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bosun%27s_call" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosun&#39;s call">boatswain's call</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bosun's call</b>, <b>boatswain's pipe</b>, <b>bosun's pipe</b>, <b>boatswain's whistle</b> or <b>bosun's whistle</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A high-pitched pipe or a non-diaphragm-type whistle used on naval ships by a <a href="#boatswain"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain</span></a>, historically to pass commands to the crew but in modern times limited to ceremonial use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatswain&#39;s_chair_or_bosun&#39;s_chair" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bosun%27s_chair" title="Bosun&#39;s chair">boatswain's chair</a> or bosun's chair</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A short board or swatch of heavy canvas, secured in a bridle of ropes, used to hoist a man aloft or over the ship's side for painting and similar work. Modern boatswain's chairs incorporate safety harnesses to prevent the occupant from falling.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A metal chair used for ship-to-ship personnel transfers at sea while underway.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatswain&#39;s_pipe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boatswain's pipe</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain&#39;s_call"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain&#39;s call" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain's call</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatswain&#39;s_whistle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boatswain's whistle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain&#39;s_call"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain&#39;s call" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain's call</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boatwright" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boatwright</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A maker of boats, especially of traditional wooden construction.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bob_or_bobfly" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bob or bobfly</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A pennant or flag bearing the owner's colors and mounted on the <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span> trunk.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bobstay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bobstay" title="Bobstay">bobstay</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A stay that holds the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a> downwards, counteracting the effect of the <a href="#forestay"><span title="See entry on this page at § forestay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forestay</span></a> and the lift of sails. Usually made of wire or chain to eliminate stretching.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="body_plan" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">body plan</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a>, an end <a href="/wiki/Elevation_(view)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elevation (view)">elevation</a> showing the contour of the sides of a ship at certain points of her length.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boiler" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boiler_(power_generation)" title="Boiler (power generation)">boiler</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A power generation system component that produces steam.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boilerman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boilerman</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#fireman&#39;&#39;."><span title="See entry on this page at § fireman&#39;&#39;." class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fireman<i>.</i></span></a></i></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boiler_room" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boiler room</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#fire_room"><span title="See entry on this page at § fire room" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fire room</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bolt_rope" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bolt_rope" title="Bolt rope">bolt rope</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rope, sewn on to reinforce the edges of a sail.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bollard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bollard" title="Bollard">bollard</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">From "bol" or "bole", the round trunk of a tree. A substantial vertical pillar to which lines may be made fast. Generally on the quayside rather than the ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bomb_vessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bomb_vessel" title="Bomb vessel">bomb vessel</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bomb</b>, <b>bombard</b>, <b>bombarde</b>, <b>bomb ketch</b> or <b>bomb ship</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A type of specialized naval wooden sailing vessel of the late 17th through mid-19th centuries designed for bombarding fixed positions on land, armed for this purpose with <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapons)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortar (weapons)">mortars</a> mounted forward near the bow.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bombard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bombard</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also spelled <b>bombarde</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A small, two-masted vessel common in the Mediterranean in the 18th and 19th centuries, similar in design to an English <a href="#ketch"><span title="See entry on this page at § ketch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ketch</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An alternative name used in the 18th and 19th centuries for a <a href="#bomb_vessel"><span title="See entry on this page at § bomb vessel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bomb vessel</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bombay_runner" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Bombay runner</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large cockroach.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bonded_jacky" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bonded jacky</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of tobacco or sweet cake.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bone_in_her_teeth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bone in her teeth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A phrase describing the appearance of a vessel throwing up a prominent <a href="#bow_wave"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow wave" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow wave</span></a> while travelling at high speed. From a vantage point in front of the vessel, the wave rising in either side of the bow evokes the image of a dog carrying a bone in its mouth, and the vessel is said to have <i>a bone in her teeth</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bonnet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bonnet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An additional strip of canvas laced to the foot of a sail to increase its area in light winds.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch1972359_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch1972359-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="booby" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Booby" title="Booby">booby</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of bird that has little fear and therefore is particularly easy to catch.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="booby_hatch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">booby hatch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A raised framework or hood like covering over a small <a href="#hatchway"><span title="See entry on this page at § hatchway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hatchway</span></a> on a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boom" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boom_(navigational_barrier)" title="Boom (navigational barrier)">boom</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A floating barrier to control navigation into and out of rivers and harbors.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> attached to the foot of a fore-and-aft sail.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> to extend the foot of gaffsail, trysail or jib.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> to extend the yards of square-rigged masts to allow the carrying of <span title="See entry on this page at § studding sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#studding_sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">studding sail</a></span>s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boom_defence_vessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boom defence vessel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An alternative term for a <span title="See entry on this page at § net laying ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#net_laying_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">net laying ship</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boomer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boomer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Slang term in the US Navy for a <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarine</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boom_crutch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boom crutch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A frame in which the <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> rests when the <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> is not <a href="#hoist"><span title="See entry on this page at § hoist" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hoisted</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boom_gallows" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boom gallows</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A raised crossmember that supports a <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> when the sail is lowered (and which obviates the need for a <span title="See entry on this page at § topping lift" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topping_lift" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topping lift</a></span>).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boomie_or_booms&#39;l_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boomie or booms'l rig</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#ketch"><span title="See entry on this page at § ketch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ketch</span></a>-rigged barge with <a href="#gaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a> (instead of <span title="See entry on this page at § spritsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spritsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spritsail</a></span>) and <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> on main and <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzen" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzen</a></span>. Booms'l rig could also refer to cutter-rigged early barges.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boom_vang_or_vang" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boom_vang" title="Boom vang">boom vang</a> or vang</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sail control that lets one apply downward tension on a boom, countering the upward tension provided by the sail. The boom vang adds an element of control to sail shape when the sheet is let out enough that it no longer pulls the boom down. Boom vang tension helps control leech twist, a primary component of sail power.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boomkin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boomkin" title="Boomkin">boomkin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#bumpkin_or_boomkin"><span title="See entry on this page at § bumpkin or boomkin" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bumpkin or boomkin</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="booms" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">booms</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Masts or yards, lying on board in reserve.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boot-top" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">boot-top</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The area on the ship's <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> along the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>, usually painted a contrasting color.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bore,_as_in_bore_up_or_bore_away" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bore, as in bore up or bore away</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To assume a position to engage, or disengage, the enemy ships.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bosun" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bosun</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bosun&#39;s_call" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bosun's call</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain&#39;s_call"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain&#39;s call" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain's call</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bosun&#39;s_chair" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bosun's chair</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain&#39;s_chair"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain&#39;s chair" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain's chair</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bosun&#39;s_pipe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bosun's pipe</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain&#39;s_call"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain&#39;s call" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain's call</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bosun&#39;s_whistle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bosun's whistle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#boatswain&#39;s_call"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain&#39;s call" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boatswain's call</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bottlescrew" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Turnbuckle" title="Turnbuckle">bottlescrew</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A device for adjusting tension in stays, shrouds and similar lines.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bottom" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bottom</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The underside of a vessel; the portion of a vessel that is always underwater.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A ship, most often a <a href="/wiki/Cargo_ship" title="Cargo ship">cargo ship</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A cargo hold.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bottomry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bottomry" title="Bottomry">bottomry</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Pledging a ship as security in a financial transaction.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bow_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bow (ship)">bow</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The front of a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Either side of the front (or bow) of the vessel, i.e. the <i>port bow</i> and <i>starboard bow</i>. Something ahead and to the left of the vessel is "off the port bow", while something ahead and to the right of the vessel is "off the starboard bow". When "bow" is used in this way, the front of the vessel sometimes is called her <i>bows</i> (plural), a collective reference to her port and starboard bows synonymous with <i>bow</i> (singular).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bow_chaser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bow chaser</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#chase_gun"><span title="See entry on this page at § chase gun" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">chase gun</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bowline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bowline" title="Bowline">bowline</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A type of knot producing a strong loop of a fixed size, topologically similar to a sheet bend.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A rope attached to the side of a sail to pull it towards the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> (for keeping the windward edge of the sail steady).<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A rope attached to the <a href="#foresail"><span title="See entry on this page at § foresail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foresail</span></a> to hold it <a href="#aback"><span title="See entry on this page at § aback" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aback</span></a> when <a href="/wiki/Tacking_(sailing)" title="Tacking (sailing)">tacking (sailing)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bowman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bowman</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The person, in a team or among oarsmen, positioned nearest the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bowpicker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bowpicker</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Gillnetter" class="mw-redirect" title="Gillnetter">gillnetter</a> that fishes by deploying a <a href="/wiki/Gillnet" class="mw-redirect" title="Gillnet">gillnet</a> from her <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bowse" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bowse</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To pull or hoist.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bow_sea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bow_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Bow sea">bow sea</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Seas approaching a vessel from between 15° and 75° to port or starboard.<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_V3_1965_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders_V3_1965-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bows_on" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bows on</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Said of a vessel directly approaching an observer, e.g., "The ship approached us <i>bows on</i>." </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bowsprit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bowsprit" title="Bowsprit">bowsprit</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> projecting from the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> that is used as an anchor for the <a href="#forestay"><span title="See entry on this page at § forestay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forestay</span></a> and other rigging. On a barge it may be pivoted so it may be steeved up in harbor.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bows_under" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bows under</dfn></dt>
