<dd class="glossary">Said of a vessel shipping water over her <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>, e.g., "The ship was <i>bows under</i> during the storm." </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bow_thruster" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bow_thruster" class="mw-redirect" title="Bow thruster">bow thruster</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small propeller or water-jet at the bow, used for manoeuvring larger vessels at slow speed. May be mounted externally, or in a tunnel running through the bow from side to side.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bow_visor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bow_visor" title="Bow visor">bow visor</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A feature of some ships, particularly ferries and roll-on/roll-off ships, that allows a vessel's bow to articulate up and down to provide access to her cargo ramp and storage deck near the waterline.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bow_wave" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bow wave</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The wave created on either side of a vessel's bow as she moves through the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boxing_the_compass" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boxing_the_compass" class="mw-redirect" title="Boxing the compass">boxing the compass</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To state all 32 points of the compass, starting at north and proceeding clockwise. Sometimes applied to a wind that is constantly shifting.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="boy_seaman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Boy_seaman" title="Boy seaman">boy seaman</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A young sailor, still in training.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brace" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brace</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square rigged</a></span> ships, a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> attached to the <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yard</a></span> to turn it, for <span title="See entry on this page at § trim" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#trim" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">trimming</a></span> the <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brace_abox" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brace abox</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To bring the <a href="#foreyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § foreyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foreyards</span></a> flat <a href="#aback"><span title="See entry on this page at § aback" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aback</span></a> to stop the ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brail" title="Brail">brail</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To furl or truss a sail by pulling it in towards the mast. "To brail up" or "to hale up the brails" is to stow the sails.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A small line used to haul the edges or corners of sails up or in before furling them. In a ship rig, brails are most often found on the mizzen sail.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brail_net" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brail net</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of net incorporating <a href="#brail"><span title="See entry on this page at § brail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">brail</span></a> lines on a small fishing net on a boat.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brailer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brailer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A device consisting of a net of small-mesh webbing attached to a frame, used aboard fishing vessels for unloading large quantities of fish.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brake" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brake</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The handle of the pump, by which it is worked.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brass_monkey_or_brass_monkey_weather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brass_monkey_(colloquial_expression)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brass monkey (colloquial expression)">brass monkey</a> or brass monkey weather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Used in the expression "it is cold enough to freeze the balls off a brass monkey".
Apocryphally, it is often claimed that a brass monkey was a frame used to hold cannon balls, and low temperature would cause the frame to contract to a greater degree than the iron balls and thus allow them to roll off.  The probable actual etymology is given <a href="/wiki/Brass_monkey_(colloquial_expression)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brass monkey (colloquial expression)">here</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brass_pounder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brass pounder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Early 20th-century slang term for a vessel<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s radio operator, so-called because he repeatedly struck a brass key on his transmitter to broadcast in <a href="/wiki/Morse_code" title="Morse code">Morse code</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="breachway" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Breachway" title="Breachway">breachway</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The shore along a channel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The whole area around the place where a channel meets the ocean.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="break_bulk_cargo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Break_bulk_cargo" class="mw-redirect" title="Break bulk cargo">break bulk cargo</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>breakbulk cargo</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">Goods that must be loaded aboard a ship individually and not in intermodal containers or in bulk, carried by a general cargo ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="breaker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">breaker</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A shallow portion of a reef over which waves break.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href="/wiki/Breaking_wave" title="Breaking wave">breaking wave</a> that breaks into foam against the shore, a shoal, a rock or a reef. Sailors use breakers to warn themselves of their vessel's proximity to an underwater hazard to navigation or, at night or during periods of poor visibility, of their vessel's proximity to shore.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A <a href="/wiki/Ship_breaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship breaker">ship breaker</a>, often used in the plural, e.g. "The old ship went to the breakers".</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;A small cask of liquid kept permanently in a <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_boat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's boat</a></span> in case of becoming separated from the ship or if used as a lifeboat.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="breakwater" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">breakwater</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A structure constructed on a coast as part of a coastal defense system or to protect an <a href="#anchorage"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchorage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchorage</span></a> from the effects of weather and <a href="/wiki/Longshore_drift" title="Longshore drift">longshore drift</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A structure built on the <a href="#forecastle"><span title="See entry on this page at § forecastle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forecastle</span></a> of a ship intended to divert water away from the forward superstructure or gun mounts.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="breeches_buoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Breeches_buoy" title="Breeches buoy">breeches buoy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ring <a href="/wiki/Lifebuoy" title="Lifebuoy">lifebuoy</a> fitted with canvas breeches, functionally similar to a <a href="/wiki/Zip_line" title="Zip line">zip line</a>, used to transfer people from one ship to another or to rescue people from a wrecked or sinking ship by moving them to another ship or to the shore.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="breastrope" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">breastrope</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A mooring rope fastened anywhere on a ship's side that goes directly to the quay, so that it is roughly at right angles to both.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMayne2000_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayne2000-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bridge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bridge_(nautical)" title="Bridge (nautical)">bridge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A structure above the weather deck, extending the full width of the vessel, which houses a command center, itself called by association <i>the bridge</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bridge_wing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bridge_(nautical)#Bridge_wing" title="Bridge (nautical)">bridge wing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A narrow walkway extending outward from both sides of a <span title="See entry on this page at § pilothouse" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#pilothouse" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">pilothouse</a></span> to the full width of a ship or slightly beyond, to allow <a href="#bridge"><span title="See entry on this page at § bridge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bridge</span></a> personnel a full view to aid in the maneuvering of the ship, such as when docking.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brig" title="Brig">brig</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A vessel with two <a href="/wiki/Square_rig" title="Square rig">square-rigged</a> masts.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(in the US) An interior area of a ship that is used to detain prisoners (possibly <a href="/wiki/Prisoners-of-war" class="mw-redirect" title="Prisoners-of-war">prisoners-of-war</a>, in wartime) or <span title="See entry on this page at § stowaway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stowaway" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stowaways</a></span>, and to punish delinquent crew members. Usually resembles a prison cell with bars and a locked, hinged door.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brig_sloop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brig_sloop" class="mw-redirect" title="Brig sloop">brig sloop</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <a href="/wiki/Sloop-of-war" title="Sloop-of-war">sloop-of-war</a> introduced in the 1770s that had two square-rigged masts like a <a href="#brig"><span title="See entry on this page at § brig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">brig</span></a> (in contrast to <i>ship sloops</i> of the time, which had three masts).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brigantine" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brigantine" title="Brigantine">brigantine</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="hermaphrodite_brig"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>hermaphrodite brig</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A two-masted vessel, <a href="/wiki/Square_rig" title="Square rig">square-rigged</a> on the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a> but <a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rigged</a> on the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainmast</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brightwork" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brightwork" title="Brightwork">brightwork</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Exposed varnished wood on a boat or ship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMayne2000_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayne2000-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bring_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bring to</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To cause a ship to be stationary by arranging the sails.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="broach" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Broach_(nautical)" title="Broach (nautical)">broach</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">When a sailing or power vessel loses directional control when travelling with a following sea. The vessel turns sideways to the wind and waves and in more serious cases may <a href="#capsize"><span title="See entry on this page at § capsize" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">capsize</span></a> or <span title="See entry on this page at § pitchpole" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#pitchpole" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">pitchpole</a></span>. Advice on dealing with heavy weather includes various strategies for avoiding this happening.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ocean_Navigator_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ocean_Navigator-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="broad" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">broad</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Wide in appearance from the vantage point of a lookout or other person viewing activity in the vicinity of a ship, e.g. another ship off the <span title="See entry on this page at § starboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#starboard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">starboard</a></span> <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> with her side facing the viewer's ship could be described as "broad on the starboard bow" of the viewer's ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="broad_fourteens" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Broad_Fourteens" title="Broad Fourteens">Broad Fourteens</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An area of the southern <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> which is fairly consistently 14 <a href="/wiki/Fathom" title="Fathom">fathoms</a> (84 feet; 26 metres) deep. On a nautical chart with depths indicated in fathoms, it appears as a broad area with many "14" notations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="broadhorn" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">broadhorn</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An alternate term for a <a href="#flatboat"><span title="See entry on this page at § flatboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flatboat</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="broadside" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Broadside_(naval)" title="Broadside (naval)">broadside</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;One side of a vessel above the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;All the guns on one side of a warship or mounted (in rotating turrets or <a href="#barbette"><span title="See entry on this page at § barbette" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barbettes</span></a>) so as to be able to fire on the same side of a warship.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The simultaneous firing of all the guns on one side of a warship or able to fire on the same side of a warship.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;<i>Weight of broadside</i>: the combined weight of all projectiles a ship can fire in a broadside engagement, or the combined weight of all the shells which a group of ships that have formed a <a href="#line_of_battle"><span title="See entry on this page at § line of battle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line of battle</span></a> can collectively fire on the same side.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brouwer_route" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Brouwer_Route" title="Brouwer Route">Brouwer Route</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"> A route used by ships in the 17th century while sailing east from the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_East_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Netherlands East Indies">Netherlands East Indies</a> which took advantage of the strong westerly winds in the southern <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> known as the "<a href="/wiki/Roaring_Forties" title="Roaring Forties">Roaring Forties</a>" to speed the trip but required ships to turn north in the eastern Indian Ocean to reach the East Indies. With no accurate means of determining <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> at the time, ships which missed the northward turn ran the risk of being wrecked on the west coast of Australia.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="brow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">brow</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#gangplank"><span title="See entry on this page at § gangplank" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gangplank</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bucket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bucket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Alternative name for a paddle on a paddlewheel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="buffer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">buffer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The chief <a href="#boatswain"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bosun</span></a>'s mate (in the Royal Navy), responsible for discipline.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bug_shoe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bug_shoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Bug shoe">bug shoe</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A length of hardened material placed on a <span title="See entry on this page at § skeg" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#skeg" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">skeg</a></span> to protect the skeg from damage by <a href="/wiki/Shipworm" title="Shipworm">shipworms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bugeye" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bugeye" title="Bugeye">bugeye</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of sailboat developed in the Chesapeake Bay by the early 1880s for oyster dredging, superseded as the chief oystering boat in the bay by the <span title="See entry on this page at § skipjack" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#skipjack" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">skipjack</a></span> at the end of the 19th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bulbous_bow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bulbous_bow" title="Bulbous bow">bulbous bow</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A protruding bulb at the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of a ship just below the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span> which modifies the way water flows around the hull, reducing drag and thus increasing speed, range, fuel efficiency and stability.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bulk_cargo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bulk_cargo" title="Bulk cargo">bulk cargo</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Commodity cargo that is transported unpackaged in large quantities.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bulk_carrier" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bulk_carrier" title="Bulk carrier">bulk carrier</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bulk freighter</b> or <b>bulker</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A merchant ship specially designed to transport unpackaged <a href="#bulk_cargo"><span title="See entry on this page at § bulk cargo" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bulk cargo</span></a> in its cargo holds.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bulkhead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bulkhead_(partition)" title="Bulkhead (partition)">bulkhead</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An upright wall within the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> of a ship, particularly a watertight, load-bearing wall.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bulwark" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bulwark</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="bulward"></span><span class="anchor" id="bulwark"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bulward</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The extension of a ship's side above the level of the weather deck.</dd>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulwark2_(PSF).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Bulwark2_%28PSF%29.png/220px-Bulwark2_%28PSF%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Bulwark2_%28PSF%29.png/330px-Bulwark2_%28PSF%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/Bulwark2_%28PSF%29.png 2x" data-file-width="430" data-file-height="317" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulwark2_(PSF).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bulwark (or bulward)</div></div></div>
<dt class="glossary" id="bull_ensign" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bull ensign</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>boot ensign</b> or <b>George ensign</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The senior ensign of a US Navy command (i.e., a ship, squadron or shore activity).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bullseye" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Porthole" title="Porthole">bullseye</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A glass window above the captain's cabin to allow viewing of the sails above deck.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bumboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bumboat" title="Bumboat">bumboat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A private boat selling goods.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bumpkin_or_boomkin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bumpkin or <a href="/wiki/Boomkin" title="Boomkin">boomkin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span>, similar to a <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a>, but which projects from the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> rather than the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>. May be used to attach the <a href="#backstay"><span title="See entry on this page at § backstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">backstay</span></a> or mizzen sheets <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955107-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An iron bar projecting outboard from a ship's side to which the lower and <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span> brace blocks are sometimes hooked.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bunk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bunk</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A built-in bed on board ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bunker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bunker</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A container for storing coal or fuel oil for a ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s engine.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bunker_fuel_or_bunkers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bunker fuel or bunkers</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="bunkers"></span>
<dd class="glossary">Fuel oil for a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bunt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bunt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Middle cloths of a square sail. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Centre of a furled square sail. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bunt-gasket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">bunt-gasket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"> Canvas apron used to fasten the bunt of a square sail to the yard when furled. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="bunting_tosser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Bunting_tosser" title="Bunting tosser">bunting tosser</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A signalman who prepares and flies flag hoists. Also known in the American Navy as a <i>skivvy waver</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="buntline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Clewlines_and_buntlines" title="Clewlines and buntlines">buntline</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the lines leading from the foot of a square sail over a block at the head and down to the deck; and used to haul it up to the yard when furling.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="buoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Buoy" title="Buoy">buoy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A floating object, usually anchored at a given position and fulfilling one of a number of uses, recognised by a defined shape and color for each, including <a href="#aids_to_navigation"><span title="See entry on this page at § aids to navigation" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aids to navigation</span></a>, warnings of danger such as submerged wrecks or divers, or for attaching mooring lines, <a href="/wiki/Lobster_pot" class="mw-redirect" title="Lobster pot">lobster pots</a>, etc.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="buoyed_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">buoyed up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Lifted by a <a href="#buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoy</span></a>, especially a cable that has been lifted to prevent it from trailing on the bottom.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="burthen" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Builder%27s_Old_Measurement" title="Builder&#39;s Old Measurement">burthen</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="/wiki/Builder%27s_Old_Measurement" title="Builder&#39;s Old Measurement">Builder's Old Measurement</a>, expressed in "tons bm" or "tons BOM", a volumetric measurement of cubic cargo capacity, <i>not</i> of weight. This is the <a href="/wiki/Tonnage" title="Tonnage">tonnage</a> of a ship, based on the number of <a href="/wiki/Tun_(unit)" title="Tun (unit)">tuns</a> of wine that it could carry in its holds. One 252-gallon tun of wine takes up approximately 100 cubic feet, and weighs 2,240 lbs (1 <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long ton</a>, or Imperial ton).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="burgee" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Burgee" title="Burgee">burgee</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small flag, typically triangular, flown from the masthead of a yacht to indicate yacht-club membership.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="burgoo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Burgoo" title="Burgoo">burgoo</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A dish of ships biscuit crumbs and minced salt pork, usually a meal of last resort for officers when other food stores are exhausted.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="butt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">butt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Where the butt of one plank joins with the butt of another.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="by_and_large" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">by and large</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><i>By</i> means into the wind, while <i>large</i> means with the wind. "By and large" is therefore used to indicate all possible situations, e.g. "the ship handles well both by and large".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="by_the_board" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">by the board</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Anything that has gone <span title="See entry on this page at § overboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#overboard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">overboard</a></span>.</dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="C">C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="cabin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cabin_(ship)" title="Cabin (ship)">cabin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An enclosed room on a <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> or flat, especially one used as living quarters.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cabin_boy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cabin_boy" title="Cabin boy">cabin boy</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An attendant to passengers and crew, often a young man.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cabin_cruiser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cabin_cruiser" title="Cabin cruiser">cabin cruiser</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <a href="/wiki/Power_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Power boat">powered</a> pleasure craft that provides accommodation for its crew and passengers inside the structure of the craft. A cabin cruiser usually is 7.6 to 13.7 metres (25 to 45&#160;ft) in length, with a powered pleasure craft craft larger than that considered a <a href="/wiki/Motor_yacht" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor yacht">motor yacht</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cable" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Wire_rope" title="Wire rope">cable</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;An especially large or thick rope.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#cable_length"><span title="See entry on this page at § cable length" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cable length</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cable_length" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cable_length" title="Cable length">cable length</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Sometimes simply called a <b>cable</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A measure of length or distance equivalent to <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">10</span></span> nautical mile (608 feet; 185 metres) in the United Kingdom and 100 fathoms (600 feet; 183 metres) in the United States; other countries use different equivalents.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="caboose" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Caboose_(ship%27s_galley)" title="Caboose (ship&#39;s galley)">caboose</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small ship's kitchen or <a href="#galley"><span title="See entry on this page at § galley" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">galley</span></a> on deck.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cabotage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cabotage" title="Cabotage">cabotage</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The transport of goods or passengers between two points within the same country, alongside coastal waters, by a vessel or an aircraft registered in another country.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cage_mast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cage_mast" class="mw-redirect" title="Cage mast">cage mast</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#lattice_mast"><span title="See entry on this page at § lattice mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lattice mast</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="camels" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">camels</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Loaded vessels lashed tightly, one on each side of another vessel, and then emptied to provide additional buoyancy that reduces the <a href="#draft"><span title="See entry on this page at § draft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">draft</span></a> of the ship in the middle.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Floating platforms brought alongside for use by yard workers or crew.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="can" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">can</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <a href="#aid_to_navigation"><span title="See entry on this page at § aid to navigation" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">navigational</span></a> <a href="#buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoy</span></a>, often a vertical drum, but otherwise always square in silhouette, colored red in <a href="/wiki/Lateral_mark#Region_A" title="Lateral mark">IALA region A</a> (Europe, Africa, Greenland, and most of Asia and Oceania) or green in <a href="/wiki/Lateral_mark#Region_B" title="Lateral mark">IALA region B</a> (the Americas, Japan, Korea, and the Philippines). In channel marking its use is opposite that of a <span title="See entry on this page at § nun buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#nun_buoy" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">nun buoy</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="canal_boat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">canal boat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A specialized watercraft designed for operation on a <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canal</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="canaller" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">canaller</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship designed to transit the locks of the <a href="/wiki/Welland_Canal" title="Welland Canal">Welland Canal</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="canister_shot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Canister_shot" title="Canister shot">canister shot</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>langrage</b> or simply <b>canister</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A type of antipersonnel cannon load in which lead balls or other loose metallic items were enclosed in a tin or iron shell. On firing, the shell would disintegrate, releasing the smaller metal objects with a shotgun-like effect.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="canoe_stern" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">canoe stern</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A design for the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> of a <span title="See entry on this page at § yacht" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yacht" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yacht</a></span> such that it is pointed like a <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>, rather than squared off as a <span title="See entry on this page at § transom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#transom" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">transom</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="canvas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">canvas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A collective term for all of the <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sails</a></span> on a vessel; the total area of all sails aboard her may be expressed as the area of her canvas. Care needs to be taken in understanding what may appear to be an area of canvas for a sail; a stated number may be the length of canvas that is needed off the roll, and it was made several different standard widths.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">cap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fitting or band used to connect the head of one <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> to the lower portion of the mast above.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cape_horn_fever" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Cape Horn fever</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A feigned illness from which a <a href="/wiki/Malingering" title="Malingering">malingerer</a> is pretending to suffer.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cape_horn_roller" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Cape Horn roller</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>graybeard</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A type of large ocean wave commonly encountered in the stormy seas of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a> south of South America′s <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">Cape Horn</a>, often exceeding 60 feet (18.3&#160;m) in height. The geography of the Southern Ocean, uninterrupted by continents, creates an endless <a href="#fetch"><span title="See entry on this page at § fetch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fetch</span></a> that is favorable for the propagation of such waves.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cap-stay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">cap-stay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#backstay"><span title="See entry on this page at § backstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">backstay</span></a> leading from a mast <a href="#cap"><span title="See entry on this page at § cap" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cap</span></a> to the ship's side.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955108-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="capital_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Capital_ship" title="Capital ship">capital ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of a set of ships considered a navy<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s most important warships, generally possessing the heaviest firepower and armor and traditionally much larger than other naval vessels, but not formally defined. During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>, capital ships were generally understood to be <a href="/wiki/Ship_of_the_line" title="Ship of the line">ships of the line</a>; during the second half of the 19th century and the 20th century, they were typically <a href="/wiki/Battleship" title="Battleship">battleships</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battlecruiser" title="Battlecruiser">battlecruisers</a>} and since the mid-20th century, the term may also include <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carriers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarines</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="capsize" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Capsize" class="mw-redirect" title="Capsize">capsize</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(of a vessel) To <a href="#list"><span title="See entry on this page at § list" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">list</span></a> so severely that the vessel rolls over, exposing the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a>. On large vessels, this often results in the sinking of the ship. Compare <i><span title="See entry on this page at § turtling" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#turtling" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">turtling</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="capstan" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Capstan_(nautical)" title="Capstan (nautical)">capstan</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large <span title="See entry on this page at § winch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#winch" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">winch</a></span> with a vertical axis used to wind in <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchors</span></a> or to hoist other heavy objects, and sometimes to administer flogging over. A full-sized human-powered capstan is a waist-high cylindrical machine, operated by a number of hands who each insert a horizontal <i>capstan bar</i> in holes in the capstan and walk in a circle.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="captain" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">captain</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The person lawfully in command of a vessel. "<a href="/wiki/Captain_(nautical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain (nautical)">Captain</a>" is an informal title of respect given to the commander of a naval vessel regardless of his or her formal rank; aboard a merchant ship, the ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s captain is called her <i>master</i>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href="/wiki/Captain_(naval)" title="Captain (naval)">naval officer</a> with a rank between <a href="/wiki/Commander" title="Commander">commander</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(rank)" title="Commodore (rank)">commodore</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;In the US Navy, US Coast Guard, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Public_Health_Service_Commissioned_Corps" title="United States Public Health Service Commissioned Corps">US Public Health Service</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NOAA_Commissioned_Officer_Corps" title="NOAA Commissioned Officer Corps">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Commissioned_officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Commissioned officer">commissioned officer</a> of a grade superior to a <a href="/wiki/Commander_(United_States)" title="Commander (United States)">commander</a> and junior to a <a href="/wiki/Rear_admiral_(United_States)" title="Rear admiral (United States)">rear admiral (lower half)</a>, equal in grade or rank to a US Army, US Marine Corps, or US Air Force colonel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="captain_of_the_port" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Captain_of_the_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain of the Port">Captain of the Port</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In the United Kingdom, a Royal Navy officer, usually a <a href="/wiki/Captain_(Royal_Navy)" title="Captain (Royal Navy)">captain</a>, responsible for the day-to-day operation of a naval <a href="#dockyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § dockyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dockyard</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In the United States, a US Coast Guard officer, usually a <a href="/wiki/Captain_(United_States_O-6)" title="Captain (United States O-6)">captain</a>, responsible for enforcement of safety, security, and marine environmental protection regulations in a commercial port.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="captain&#39;s_daughter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">captain's daughter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Another name for the <a href="#cat_o&#39;_nine_tails"><span title="See entry on this page at § cat o&#39; nine tails" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cat o' nine tails</span></a>, which in principle is only used on board on the captain's (or a court martial's) personal orders.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="car_carrier" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Car_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Car carrier">car carrier</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A cargo ship specially designed or fitted to carry large numbers of automobiles. Modern <i>pure car carriers</i> have a fully enclosed, box-like superstructure that extends along the entire length and across the entire breadth of the ship, enclosing the automobiles. The similar <i>pure car/truck carrier</i> can also accommodate trucks.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="car_float" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Car_float" title="Car float">car float</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>railroad car float</b> or <b>rail barge</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">An unpowered <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a> with railroad tracks mounted on its deck, used to move railroad cars across water obstacles.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="caravel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravel</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="caravelle"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>caravelle</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A small, highly maneuverable sailing ship with a <a href="#lateen_rigging"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen rig</span></a>, used by the Portuguese in the 15th and 16th centuries to explore along the West African coast and into the Atlantic Ocean.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cardinal" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">cardinal</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Referring to the four main points of the compass: north, south, east, and west. See also <i><a href="#bearing"><span title="See entry on this page at § bearing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bearing</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="careening" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Careening" title="Careening">careening</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>heaving down</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">Tilting a ship on its side, usually when <a href="#beaching"><span title="See entry on this page at § beaching" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beached</span></a>, to clean or repair the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> below the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cargo_liner" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cargo_liner" title="Cargo liner">cargo liner</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>passenger-cargo ship</b> or <b>passenger-cargoman</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A type of merchant ship that became common just after the middle of the 19th century, configured primarily for the transportation of general cargo but also for the transportation of at least some passengers. Almost completely replaced by more specialized cargo ships during the second half of the 20th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cargo_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cargo_ship" title="Cargo ship">cargo ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any ship or vessel that carries cargo, goods, and materials from one port to another, including general cargo ships (designed to carry <a href="#break_bulk_cargo"><span title="See entry on this page at § break bulk cargo" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">break bulk cargo</span></a>), <a href="#bulk_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § bulk carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bulk carriers</span></a>, <a href="#container_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § container ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">container ships</span></a>, multipurpose vessels, and <span title="See entry on this page at § tanker" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tanker" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tankers</a></span>. Tankers, however, although technically cargo ships, are routinely thought of as constituting a completely separate category.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carpenter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">carpenter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>, a warrant officer responsible for the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span>, <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spars</a></span>, and <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_boat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">boats</a></span> of a vessel, and also for sounding the well to see if the vessel was <span title="See entry on this page at § making water" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#making_water" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">making water</a></span>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A senior rating responsible for all of the woodwork aboard a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carpenter&#39;s_walk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">carpenter's walk</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On a <a href="/wiki/Tall_ship" title="Tall ship">tall ship</a>, a is a narrow unlit passageway or <a href="/wiki/Bulkhead_(partition)" title="Bulkhead (partition)">bulkhead</a> often with a low (four-foot) ceiling that is fitted around the hull at its waterline.  The carpenter's walk allowed the <a href="/wiki/Ship%27s_carpenter" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship&#39;s carpenter">ship's carpenter</a> to tour the entire waterline area of a ship to inspect it for water leaks.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  Because of its dark and seldom-visited nature and location far below decks, it was also sometimes used by <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutinous</a> sailors as a secluded place to plan a rebellion against the ship's officers.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carrack" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>nau</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A three- or four-masted oceangoing sailing ship used by Western Europeans in the Atlantic Ocean from the 15th through the early 17th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carrier" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">carrier</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carronade" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Carronade" title="Carronade">carronade</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short, smoothbore, cast-iron naval cannon, used from the 1770s to the 1850s as a powerful, short-range, anti-ship and anti-crew weapon.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carry_on" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">carry on</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Resume work or assigned duties.<sup id="cite_ref-NHHC_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHHC-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cartel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cartel_(ship)" title="Cartel (ship)">cartel</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship employed on humanitarian voyages, in particular to carry communications or prisoners between belligerents during wartime. A cartel flies distinctive flags, including a <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_truce" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag of truce">flag of truce</a>, traditionally is unarmed except for a lone signaling gun, and under <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> is not subject to seizure or capture during her outbound and return voyages as long as she engages in no warlike acts.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="carvel-built" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Carvel_(boat_building)" title="Carvel (boat building)">carvel-built</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A method of constructing a wooden <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> in which planks are butted edge-to-edge on a robust frame, so giving a smooth hull surface; traditionally the planks are not attached to each other, only to the frame, and have only a <a href="#caulk"><span title="See entry on this page at § caulk" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">caulking</span></a> sealant between them to make them watertight.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch1972359_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch1972359-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Contrast <i><a href="#clinker-built"><span title="See entry on this page at § clinker-built" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clinker-built</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="casing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Casing_(submarine)" title="Casing (submarine)">casing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A light metal structure, usually incorporating a <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a>, built over the upper surface of a <span title="See entry on this page at § submarine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#submarine" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">submarine</a></span>'s <a href="/wiki/Submarine_hull#Pressure_hull" title="Submarine hull">pressure hull</a> to create a flat surface on which crew members can walk. A feature of submarines built prior to the mid-20th century, but not of more modern submarines.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">cat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To prepare an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> after raising it by lifting it with a <span title="See entry on this page at § tackle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tackle" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tackle</a></span> to the <a href="#cathead"><span title="See entry on this page at § cathead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cathead</span></a>, prior to securing (<i>fishing</i>) it alongside for sea. An anchor raised to the cathead is said to be <i>catted</i>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The <a href="#cat_o&#39;_nine_tails"><span title="See entry on this page at § cat o&#39; nine tails" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cat o' nine tails</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#cat_rigging"><span title="See entry on this page at § cat rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cat-rigged</span></a> boat or <a href="#catboat"><span title="See entry on this page at § catboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">catboat</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cat_o&#39;_nine_tails" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cat_o%27_nine_tails" title="Cat o&#39; nine tails">cat o' nine tails</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>the cat</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A short, multi-tailed whip or flail kept by the <a href="#boatswain"><span title="See entry on this page at § boatswain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bosun</span></a>'s mate to <a href="/wiki/Flagellation" title="Flagellation">flog</a> sailors (and soldiers in the army) who had committed infractions while at sea. When not in use, the cat was often kept in a baize bag, a possible origin for the term "cat out of the bag".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> "Not enough room to swing a cat" also derives from this.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="catamaran" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Catamaran" title="Catamaran">catamaran</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any vessel with two <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hulls</span></a>. Compare <i><span title="See entry on this page at § trimaran" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#trimaran" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">trimaran</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="catboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Catboat" title="Catboat">catboat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#cat_rigging"><span title="See entry on this page at § cat rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cat-rigged</span></a> vessel with a single mast mounted close to the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> and only one sail, usually on a <a href="#gaff_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="catenary" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">catenary</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>catenary curve</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The curve of a deployed anchor chain.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="catharpin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Catharpin" title="Catharpin">catharpin</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short rope or iron clamp used to brace in the <span title="See entry on this page at § shroud" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shroud" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shrouds</a></span> toward the masts so as to give a freer sweep to the <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yards</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cathead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cathead" title="Cathead">cathead</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A beam extending out from the hull used to support an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> when raised in order to secure or "fish" it.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="cat&#39;s_paws" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_paw_(wave)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cat&#39;s paw (wave)">cat's paws</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Light, variable winds on calm waters producing scattered areas of small waves.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="caulk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Caulk" title="Caulk">caulk</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To create a <span title="See entry on this page at § watertight" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#watertight" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">watertight</a></span> seal between structures. In traditional <a href="#carvel-built"><span title="See entry on this page at § carvel-built" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">carvel</span></a> construction, this involved hammering <span title="See entry on this page at § oakum" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#oakum" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">oakum</a></span> (recycled rope fibres) or caulking cotton into the slightly tapered fine gaps between the hull or deck planks and, in older methods, covering with tar. The expansion of the fibres in water tightens up the hull, making it less prone to racking movement, as well as making the joint watertight.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteffy2013_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteffy2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="celestial_navigation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Celestial_navigation" title="Celestial navigation">celestial navigation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Navigation by the position of celestial objects, including the stars, Sun, and Moon, using tools aboard ship such as a <a href="/wiki/Sextant" title="Sextant">sextant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_chronometer" title="Marine chronometer">chronometer</a>, and compass, as well as <a href="/wiki/Ephemerides" class="mw-redirect" title="Ephemerides">published tables</a> of the expected positions of celestial objects on specific dates. Celestial navigation was the primary method of navigation until the development of electronic global positioning systems such as <a href="/wiki/LORAN" title="LORAN">LORAN</a> and <a href="/wiki/GPS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS">GPS</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ceiling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ceiling</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Planking attached to the inside of the <a href="#frame"><span title="See entry on this page at § frame" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">frames</span></a> or <a href="#floor"><span title="See entry on this page at § floor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">floors</span></a> of a wooden hull, usually to separate the cargo from the hull planking itself. The ceiling has different names in different places; e.g. <a href="#limber_boards"><span title="See entry on this page at § limber boards" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">limber boards</span></a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § spirketting" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spirketting" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spirketting</a></span>, <span title="See entry on this page at § quickwork" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#quickwork" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">quickwork</a></span>, etc. The lower part of the ceiling is, confusingly to a landsman, what you are standing on at the bottom of the <a href="#hold"><span title="See entry on this page at § hold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hold</span></a> of a wooden ship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch1972359_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch1972359-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="center_of_effort" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">center of effort</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="centre_of_effort"></span><span class="anchor" id="center_of_pressure"></span><span class="anchor" id="centre_of_pressure"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>center of pressure</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The point of origin of net aerodynamic force upon a <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span>, roughly located in the geometric center of the sail, though the actual position of the center of effort will vary with <span title="See entry on this page at § sail plan" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail_plan" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail plan</a></span>, sail trim, or airfoil profile, boat trim, and <span title="See entry on this page at § point of sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#point_of_sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">point of sail</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="center_of_lateral_resistance" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">center of lateral resistance</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="centre_of_lateral_resistance"></span>
<dd class="glossary">The point of origin of net hydrodynamic resistance on the submerged structure of a boat, especially a sailboat. This is the pivot point the boat turns about when unbalanced external forces are applied, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Center_of_gravity" class="mw-redirect" title="Center of gravity">center of gravity</a>. On a perfectly balanced sailboat, the <a href="#center_of_effort"><span title="See entry on this page at § center of effort" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">center of effort</span></a> will align vertically with the center of lateral resistance. If this is not the case, the boat will be unbalanced and will exhibit either <a href="#lee_helm"><span title="See entry on this page at § lee helm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lee helm</span></a> or <span title="See entry on this page at § weather helm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#weather_helm" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">weather helm</a></span> and will be difficult to control.</dd>

<span class="anchor" id="centreline"></span><dt class="glossary" id="centerline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">centerline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An imaginary line down the center of a vessel lengthwise. Any structure or anything mounted or carried on a vessel that straddles this line and is equidistant from either side of the vessel is said to be "on the centerline".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="centreboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Centreboard" title="Centreboard">centreboard</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="centreboard"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>centerplate</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A wooden board or metal plate which can be pivoted through a fore-and-aft slot along the <a href="#centerline"><span title="See entry on this page at § centerline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">centerline</span></a> in the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> of a sailing vessel, functioning as a retractable <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> to help the boat resist <a href="#leeway"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeway</span></a> by moving its <a href="#center_of_lateral_resistance"><span title="See entry on this page at § center of lateral resistance" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">center of lateral resistance</span></a>.
