<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E">E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="earings" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">earings</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Small lines by which the uppermost corners of the largest sails are secured to the <span title="See entry on this page at § yardarm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yardarm" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yardarms</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="east_indiaman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/East_Indiaman" title="East Indiaman">East Indiaman</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any ship operating under charter or license to the East India Company (England), or to the <a href="/wiki/Danish_East_India_Company" title="Danish East India Company">Danish East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_East_India_Company" title="Portuguese East India Company">Portuguese East India Company</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Swedish_East_India_Company" title="Swedish East India Company">Swedish East India Company</a> from the 17th to the 19th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="echo_sounding" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Echo_sounding" title="Echo sounding">echo sounding</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The measurement of the depth of a body of water using a <a href="/wiki/SONAR" class="mw-redirect" title="SONAR">SONAR</a> device. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sounding</a></span></i> and <i><span title="See entry on this page at § swinging the lead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#swinging_the_lead" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">swinging the lead</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="embayed" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">embayed</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A condition in which a sailing vessel (especially one that sails poorly to <span title="See entry on this page at § windward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windward</a></span>) is confined between two capes or headlands by a wind blowing directly onshore.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="en_echelon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">en echelon</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="en_echelon"></span>
<dd class="glossary">An arrangement of gun turrets whereby the turret on one side of the ship is placed further <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> than the one on the other side, so that both turrets can fire to either side.</dd>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg/220px-Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg/330px-Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg/440px-Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1169" data-file-height="884" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Minas_Geraes-class_battleships.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diagram showing the <i>Minas Geraes</i>-class battleship with its central guns arranged <i>en echelon</i>.</div></div></div>
<dt class="glossary" id="engine_order_telegraph" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Engine_order_telegraph" title="Engine order telegraph">engine order telegraph</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>chadburn</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A communications device used by the pilot to order engineers in the <a href="#engine_room"><span title="See entry on this page at § engine room" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">engine room</span></a> to power the vessel at a certain desired speed.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="engine_room" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Engine_room" title="Engine room">engine room</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">One of the machinery spaces of a vessel, usually the largest one, containing the ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s prime mover (usually a diesel or steam engine or a gas or steam turbine). Larger vessels may have more than one engine room.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ensign" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ensign</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Ensign" title="Ensign">(flag)</a> The principal flag or banner flown by a ship to indicate her nationality.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Ensign_(rank)" title="Ensign (rank)">rank</a>) The lowest grade of <a href="/wiki/Commissioned_officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Commissioned officer">commissioned officer</a> in the US Navy.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="escort_carrier" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Escort_carrier" title="Escort carrier">escort carrier</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <a href="#aircraft_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § aircraft carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aircraft carrier</span></a>, smaller and slower than a <a href="#fleet_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § fleet carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fleet carrier</span></a>, used by some navies in World War II to escort convoys, ferry aircraft, and provide air support for <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_operation" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphibious operation">amphibious operations</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="estimated_position" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">estimated position</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An approximate geographical position obtained by making allowances for leeway, tide, and currents to a <a href="#dead_reckoning"><span title="See entry on this page at § dead reckoning" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dead reckoning</span></a> position (which is calculated from the distance run and the course steered).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="executive_officer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">executive officer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The officer second in command on a warship.  Also called "X.O." and "Number One".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="extra_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">extra ship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A term used by the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> from the seventeenth to the nineteenth century for merchant ships it hired to make voyages for it between England (later the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>) and ports east of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, a trade over which the company held a strict monopoly. "Extra ships" were chartered for a single round-trip voyage beginning during a single sailing season (September to April) and augmented the voyages of "regular ships" (<i>q.v.</i>), which were merchant ships under long-term charter to make repeated voyages for the company over many seasons. However, if an "extra ship" operated well and the company needed its services, the company often chartered it repeatedly over a number of seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-threedecksshiproles_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-threedecksshiproles-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="extremis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">extremis</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>in extremis</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The point under International Rules of the Road (<a href="/wiki/International_Regulations_for_Preventing_Collisions_at_Sea" title="International Regulations for Preventing Collisions at Sea">Navigation Rules</a>) at which the privileged (or stand-on) vessel on collision course with a burdened (or give-way) vessel determines it must maneuver to avoid a collision. Prior to extremis, the privileged vessel must maintain course and speed and the burdened vessel must maneuver to avoid collision.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="eye_splice" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Eye_splice" title="Eye splice">eye splice</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A closed loop or eye at the end of a line, rope, cable, etc. It is made by unraveling its end and joining it to itself by intertwining it into the lay of the line. Eye <a href="/wiki/Rope_splicing" title="Rope splicing">splices</a> are very strong and compact and are frequently employed in moorings and docking lines, among other uses.</dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="F">F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="factory_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Factory_ship" title="Factory ship">factory ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large oceangoing vessel with extensive on-board facilities for processing and freezing caught fish or whales. Some also serve as <span title="See entry on this page at § mother ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mother_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mother ships</a></span> for smaller fishing or whaling vessels. Those used for processing fish are also known as <i>fish processing vessels</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fair" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fair</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A smooth curve, usually referring to a line of the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> with minimum localised deviations.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To make something flush.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> is fair when it has a clear run.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;A wind or current is fair when it offers an advantage to a boat.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fair_winds_and_following_seas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fair winds and following seas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A blessing wishing the recipient a safe journey and good fortune.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fairlead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fairlead" title="Fairlead">fairlead</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A device used to keep a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> or chain running in the correct direction or to give it a <a href="#fair"><span title="See entry on this page at § fair" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fair</span></a> <a href="#lead"><span title="See entry on this page at § lead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lead</span></a> to prevent it rubbing or fouling.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fairing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fairing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(n) A structure that improves the streamlining of a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(v) The process of making  a curve or structure <a href="#fair"><span title="See entry on this page at § fair" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fair</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fairwater" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fairwater</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A structure that improves the streamlining of a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;On submarines: The superstructure (<a href="/wiki/Conning_tower" title="Conning tower">conning tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sail_(submarine)" title="Sail (submarine)">sail</a>,etc) of the boat.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fairway" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fairway</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A navigable channel (e.g. in a harbor or offshore) that is the usual course taken by vessels in the area.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In military and naval terms, a channel from offshore, in a river, or in a harbor that has enough depth to accommodate the <a href="#draft"><span title="See entry on this page at § draft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">draft</span></a> of large vessels.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fake" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fake</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A single turn of rope in a coil or on a drum. A group of fakes is known as a <span title="See entry on this page at § tier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tier" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tier</a></span>. See also <a href="#fake_down"><span title="See entry on this page at § fake down" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fake down</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smyth_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smyth-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 200, 286">&#58;&#8202;200,&#8202;286&#8202;</span></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fake_down" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fake down</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To lay a coil of rope down so that it will run easily – that is with rope feeding off the top of the coil and the bitter end at the bottom. Often confused with <a href="#flake"><span title="See entry on this page at § flake" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flake</span></a>. See also <span title="See entry on this page at § range" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#range" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">range</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="falkuša" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Falku%C5%A1a" title="Falkuša">falkuša</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A traditional fishing boat with a <a href="#lateen"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen</span></a> sail on a single mast used by fishermen from the town of <a href="/wiki/Komi%C5%BEa" title="Komiža">Komiža</a> on the Adriatic island of <a href="/wiki/Vis_(island)" title="Vis (island)">Vis</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fall" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fall</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The part of the <span title="See entry on this page at § tackle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tackle" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tackle</a></span> that is hauled upon.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fall_off" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fall off</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>bear away</b>, <b>bear off</b>, or <b>head down</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">To change the direction of sail so as to point in a direction that is more downwind; to bring the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a>. This is the opposite of pointing up or heading up.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fantail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fantail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> end of a ship. Also known as the <span title="See entry on this page at § poop deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#poop_deck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">poop deck</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fardage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fardage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Wood placed in the bottom of a ship to keep cargo dry. See also <i><a href="#dunnage"><span title="See entry on this page at § dunnage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dunnage</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fashion_boards" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fashion boards</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Loose boards that slide in grooves to close off a <a href="#companionway"><span title="See entry on this page at § companionway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">companionway</span></a> or <a href="#cabin"><span title="See entry on this page at § cabin" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cabin</span></a> entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fast</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Fastened or held firmly (e.g. "fast <a href="#aground"><span title="See entry on this page at § aground" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aground</span></a>": stuck on the seabed; "made fast": tied securely).<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fast_combat_support_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fast_combat_support_ship" title="Fast combat support ship">fast combat support ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The largest type of U.S. Navy combat logistics ship, designed to serve as a combined oiler, ammunition ship, and supply ship. The first fast combat support ship entered service in the mid-1960s.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fast_supply_vessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fast supply vessel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#crew_boat"><span title="See entry on this page at § crew boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crew boat</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fast_support_vessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fast support vessel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#crew_boat"><span title="See entry on this page at § crew boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crew boat</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fathom" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fathom" title="Fathom">fathom</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A unit of length equal to 6 feet (1.8&#160;m), roughly measured as the distance between a man's outstretched hands. Particularly used in <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sounding</a></span> as a measurement of the depth of a body of water.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To measure the depth of water; to engage in <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sounding</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fathomer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fathomer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A person engaged in <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sounding</a></span> to determine the depth of water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fathometer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fathometer" class="mw-redirect" title="Fathometer">fathometer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">depth finder</a></span> that uses sound waves to determine the depth of water.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="favored_side" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">favored side</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The side of the course that gets you to the next mark faster, due to more wind, favorable shifts, less current, smaller waves, etc.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="felucca" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Felucca" title="Felucca">felucca</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A traditional wooden sailing boat with a <span title="See entry on this page at § rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rig</a></span> consisting of one or two <a href="#lateen"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen</span></a> sails, used in protected waters of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and eastern <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> and particularly along the <a href="/wiki/Nile_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile River">Nile</a> in Egypt and Sudan, as well as in Iraq.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fend_off" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fend off</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A command given to the crew to stop what they are now doing and to immediately manually prevent the boat from banging into the <a href="#dock"><span title="See entry on this page at § dock" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">docks</span></a> or other boats.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fender" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fender_(boating)" title="Fender (boating)">fender</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A flexible bumper used in boating to keep boats from banging into docks or each other. Often an old car tire.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ferry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>ferryboat</b></span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant ship</a></span> used to carry passengers, and sometimes vehicles and cargo, across a body of water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ferry_glide" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ferry glide</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To hold a vessel against and at an angle to the current/stream such that the vessel moves sideways over the bottom due to the effect of the current operating on the upstream side of the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ferry_slip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ferry_slip" title="Ferry slip">ferry slip</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A specialized docking facility designed to receive a ferryboat or train ferry.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fetch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fetch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The distance across water a wind or waves have traveled.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To reach a mark without <a href="/wiki/Tacking_(sailing)" title="Tacking (sailing)">tacking (sailing)</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fid" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fid</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A tapered wooden tool used for separating the strands of rope for splicing.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A bar used to fix an upper <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> in place.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fife_rail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fife_rail" title="Fife rail">fife rail</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A freestanding <span title="See entry on this page at § pinrail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#pinrail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">pinrail</a></span> surrounding the base of a <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> and used for securing that mast's sails' <a href="#halyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § halyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">halyards</span></a> with a series of <a href="#belaying_pin"><span title="See entry on this page at § belaying pin" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">belaying pins</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fifie" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fifie" title="Fifie">Fifie</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing boat with two masts with a standard rig consisting of a main dipping <a href="#lug_sail"><span title="See entry on this page at § lug sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lug sail</span></a> and a mizzen standing lug sail. Developed in Scotland and used for commercial fishing from the 1850s until the 20th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fig</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">US Navy slang for a guided-missile <a href="#frigate"><span title="See entry on this page at § frigate" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">frigate</span></a>, especially of the <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hazard_Perry-class_frigate" title="Oliver Hazard Perry-class frigate"><i>Oliver Hazard Perry</i> class</a>, derived from its class designation ("FFG").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fight_his_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fight his ship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To fight his ship (or to fight her ship) is a naval term that denotes a captain taking their vessel into combat or directing their vessel in combat.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fighting_top" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fighting top</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An enlarged <span title="See entry on this page at § top" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#top" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">top</a></span> designed to allow gunfire downward onto an enemy ship. A fighting top could have small guns installed in it or could serve as a platform for <a href="/wiki/Sniper" title="Sniper">snipers</a> armed with <a href="/wiki/Musket" title="Musket">muskets</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="figure_of_eight" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">figure of eight</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A stopper knot.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="figurehead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Figurehead_(object)" title="Figurehead (object)">figurehead</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A symbolic image, particularly a carved effigy, at the head of a traditional sailing ship or early steamer.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fin" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fin</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A term used in European and British Commonwealth countries for a tower-like structure on the dorsal (topside) surface of a submarine; called a <i><a href="/wiki/Sail_(submarine)" title="Sail (submarine)">sail</a></i> in the United States.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fine" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fine</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Narrow in appearance from the vantage point of a <a href="#lookout"><span title="See entry on this page at § lookout" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lookout</span></a> or other person viewing activity in the vicinity of a ship, e.g. another ship off the <span title="See entry on this page at § starboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#starboard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">starboard</a></span> <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> with her bow or <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> facing the viewer's ship could be described as "fine on the starboard bow" of the viewer's ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fireboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fireboat" title="Fireboat">fireboat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A specialized vessel equipped with <a href="/wiki/Firefighting" title="Firefighting">firefighting</a> equipment such as pumps and nozzles for fighting shipboard and shoreline fires.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fireman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fireman_(steam_engine)" title="Fireman (steam engine)">fireman</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>stoker</b>, <b>boilerman</b>, or <b>watertender</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A job associated with tending the fire for a boiler.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A US Navy <span title="See entry on this page at § rating" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rating" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rate</a></span> in the engineering department equivalent to <span title="See entry on this page at § seaman" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#seaman" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">seaman</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fire_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fire_ship" title="Fire ship">fire ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship loaded with flammable materials and explosives and sailed into an enemy port or fleet either already burning or ready to be set alight by its crew (who would then abandon it) in order to collide with and set fire to enemy ships.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fire_room" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fire_room" title="Fire room">fire room</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>boiler room</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The compartment in which a ship's boilers or furnaces are stoked and fired.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="first-rate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/First-rate" title="First-rate">first-rate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The classification for the largest sailing warships of the 17th through the 19th centuries. Such vessels often had up to three masts, 850+ crew, and 100+ guns.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="first_lieutenant" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/First_lieutenant" title="First lieutenant">first lieutenant</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In the Royal Navy, the senior <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant" title="Lieutenant">lieutenant</a> on board; responsible to the <a href="/wiki/Commanding_officer" title="Commanding officer">commanding officer</a> for the domestic affairs of the <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s company" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_company" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's company</a></span>. Also known as 'Jimmy the One' or 'Number One'. Removes his cap when visiting the mess decks as a token of respect for the privacy of the crew in those quarters. Officer in charge of <a href="#cable"><span title="See entry on this page at § cable" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cables</span></a> on the <a href="#forecastle"><span title="See entry on this page at § forecastle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forecastle</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In the US Navy, the officer on a ship serving as the senior person in charge of all <a href="#deck_hand"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck hand" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck hands</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="first_mate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Chief_mate" title="Chief mate">first mate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The second-in-command of a commercial ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fish" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fish</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To repair a <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> with a fillet of wood.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To secure an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> on the side of a ship for sea (otherwise known as "catting".)</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A slang term for a self-propelled <a href="/wiki/Torpedo" title="Torpedo">torpedo</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fisherman&#39;s_reef" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fisherman's reef</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing tactic for handling winds too strong for the sail area hoisted when reefing the sails is not feasible or possible. The <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a> is set normally while the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span> is let out until it is constantly <a href="#luffing"><span title="See entry on this page at § luffing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">luffing</span></a>. This creates a loss of force on the main and also reduces the efficiency of the headsail while still retaining sailing control of the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fisherman&#39;s_sail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fisherman's sail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On a <span title="See entry on this page at § staysail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#staysail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">staysail</a></span> <span title="See entry on this page at § schooner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#schooner" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">schooner</a></span>, the fisherman is a quadrilateral sail set between the two masts above the main staysail. It is used in light to moderate airs.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fitting-out" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fitting-out" class="mw-redirect" title="Fitting-out">fitting-out</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The period after a ship is <a href="/wiki/Ship_naming_and_launching" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship naming and launching">launched</a> during which all the remaining construction of the ship is completed and she is readied for <span title="See entry on this page at § sea trial" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sea_trial" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sea trials</a></span> and delivery to her owners.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fixed_propeller" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fixed propeller</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § propeller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#propeller" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">propeller</a></span> mounted on a rigid shaft protruding from the hull of a vessel, usually driven by an inboard motor; steering must be done using a <span title="See entry on this page at § rudder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rudder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rudder</a></span>. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § outboard motor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#outboard_motor" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">outboard motor</a></span></i> and <i><span title="See entry on this page at § sterndrive" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sterndrive" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sterndrive</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flag_hoist" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flag hoist</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A number of <span title="See entry on this page at § signal flag" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#signal_flag" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">signal flags</a></span> strung together to convey a message, e.g. "<a href="/wiki/England_expects_that_every_man_will_do_his_duty" title="England expects that every man will do his duty">England expects that every man will do his duty</a>".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flag_of_convenience" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_convenience" title="Flag of convenience">flag of convenience</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The business practice of registering a <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant ship</a></span> in a sovereign state different from that of the ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s owners, and flying that state<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s civil <a href="#ensign"><span title="See entry on this page at § ensign" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ensign</span></a> on the ship. The practice allows the ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s owner to reduce operating costs or avoid the regulations of the owner<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s country.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flag_officer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flag_officer" title="Flag officer">flag officer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A commissioned officer senior enough to be entitled to fly a flag to mark the ship or installation under their command, in English-speaking countries usually referring to the senior officers of a navy, specifically to those who hold any of the <a href="#admiral"><span title="See entry on this page at § admiral" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">admiral</span></a> ranks and in some cases to those holding the rank of <a href="#commodore"><span title="See entry on this page at § commodore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">commodore</span></a>. In modern American usage, additionally applied to US Coast Guard and <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration_Commissioned_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration Commissioned Corps">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration Commissioned Corps</a> officers and general officers in the US Army, US Air Force, and US Marine Corps entitled to fly their own flags.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A formal rank in the mid-19th century US Navy, conveyed temporarily upon senior <a href="#captain"><span title="See entry on this page at § captain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">captains</span></a> in command of squadrons of ships, soon rendered obsolete by the creation of the ranks of <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(United_States)" title="Commodore (United States)">commodore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rear_Admiral_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rear Admiral (United States)">rear admiral</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flagship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A vessel used by the commanding officer of a group of naval ships. The term derives from the custom of commanders of such a group of ships, characteristically a <a href="#flag_officer"><span title="See entry on this page at § flag officer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flag officer</span></a>, flying a distinguishing flag aboard the ship on which they are embarked.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Used more loosely, the lead ship in a <a href="#fleet"><span title="See entry on this page at § fleet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fleet</span></a> of naval or commercial vessels, typically the first, largest, fastest, most heavily armed, or, in terms of media coverage, best-known.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flake" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flake</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To set down in folds, as in stowing a sail or to <span title="See entry on this page at § range" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#range" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">range</a></span> a cable on deck so that it is clear to run. Not to be confused with <a href="#fake_down"><span title="See entry on this page at § fake down" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fake down</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flank_speed" title="Flank speed">flank</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The maximum speed of a ship. Faster than "full speed".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flare" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flare</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A curvature of the topsides outward towards the <a href="#gunwale"><span title="See entry on this page at § gunwale" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gunwale</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A pyrotechnic signalling device, usually used to indicate distress.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flatback" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flatback</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> slang term for a vessel without any self-unloading equipment.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flatboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flatboat" title="Flatboat">flatboat</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>broadhorn</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A rectangular, flat-bottomed boat with square ends used to transport freight and passengers on inland waterways in the United States during the 18th and 19th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flattop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flattop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A slang term for an <a href="#aircraft_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § aircraft carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aircraft carrier</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fleet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fleet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<i><a href="/wiki/Naval_fleet" title="Naval fleet">Naval fleet</a></i>: The highest operational echelon of command of ships commanded by a single person in a navy, and typically the largest type of naval formation commanded by a single person. In modern times, usually (but not necessarily) a permanent formation.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> term for any naval command larger than a squadron in size, or commanded by a <a href="/wiki/Rear_admiral_(Royal_Navy)" title="Rear admiral (Royal Navy)">rear admiral</a> and composed of five <a href="/wiki/Ship-of-the-line" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship-of-the-line">ships-of-the-line</a> and any number of smaller vessels.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;<i><a href="/wiki/Merchant_navy" title="Merchant navy">Merchant fleet</a></i>, a collective term for the <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant marine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_marine" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant marine</a></span> (known in the United Kingdom and Commonwealth countries the <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant navy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_navy" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant navy</a></span>) of a particular country.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;<i><a href="/wiki/Fishing_fleet" title="Fishing fleet">Fishing fleet</a></i>: A term for an aggregate of commercial fishing vessels, commonly used either to describe all fishing vessels belonging to a single country, operating in a single region, operating out of a particular port, or engaged in particular type of fishing (e.g., <i>the tuna fishing fleet</i>). The term does not imply that the vessels operate as part of a single organization.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">5.&#160;&#160;Informally, any grouping (based on physical proximity or sharing of a common organizational subordination) of naval or civilian vessels.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">6.&#160;&#160;Of a person, to move from one location to another aboard a vessel, or to change positions within a naval organization.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">7.&#160;&#160;To move up a rope&#160;&#8211;&#32;especially when drawing the blocks of a tackle part&#160;&#8211;&#32;to allow a greater advantage in <a href="#haul"><span title="See entry on this page at § haul" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">haul</span></a>ing.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">8.&#160;&#160;To cause a rope or chain to slip down the barrel of a <a href="#capstan"><span title="See entry on this page at § capstan" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">capstan</span></a> or <span title="See entry on this page at § windlass" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windlass" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windlass</a></span>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">9.&#160;&#160;A former term for the process aboard a vessel of moving <a href="#deadeye"><span title="See entry on this page at § deadeye" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deadeye</span></a>s when the <a href="/wiki/Shroud" title="Shroud">shrouds</a> become too long.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">10.&#160;&#160;A location where <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a>s are secured.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fleet_in_being" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fleet_in_being" title="Fleet in being">fleet in being</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A naval force that extends a controlling influence on maritime operations without ever leaving port by forcing an opposing navy to maintain forces on station to oppose it in case it comes out to fight or to <a href="#blockade"><span title="See entry on this page at § blockade" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">blockade</span></a> it in port. A navy which operates its forces as a <i>fleet in being</i> generally seeks to avoid actual combat with an enemy fleet for fear of losing a naval battle and thereby its ability to influence events and activities at sea.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flemish" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flemish</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To coil a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> that is not in use so that it lies flat on the deck.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flettner_rotor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flettner rotor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A spinning cylinder that uses the <a href="/wiki/Magnus_effect" title="Magnus effect">Magnus effect</a> to harness wind power to propel a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flight_deck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flight_deck" title="Flight deck">flight deck</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A flat deck on an <a href="#aircraft_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § aircraft carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aircraft carrier</span></a> used for the launch and recovery of aircraft.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flog_the_glass" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flog the glass</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The act of vibrating or shaking a half-hour <span title="See entry on this page at § marine sandglass" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#marine_sandglass" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">marine sandglass</a></span> — used until the early 19th century to time the length of a watch — to speed the passage of the sand in order to get off watch duty earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="floor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">floor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The transverse structural timbers to which the longitudinal bottom planking is attached. The equivalent side timbers are called the frames. The <a href="#keelson"><span title="See entry on this page at § keelson" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">keelson</span></a> is fastened on top of the floors, bolting them to the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a>. The planking is the exterior of the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>, while the ceiling is attached on top of the floors, and it forms the base of the <a href="#hold"><span title="See entry on this page at § hold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hold</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="floorhead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">floorhead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any of the upper extremities of the <a href="#floor"><span title="See entry on this page at § floor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">floor</span></a> of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flotilla" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flotilla" title="Flotilla">flotilla</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In naval usage, a group of warships under a single commander that is smaller than a <a href="#fleet"><span title="See entry on this page at § fleet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fleet</span></a> but otherwise not formally defined. A flotilla often is larger than a <span title="See entry on this page at § squadron" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#squadron" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">squadron</a></span>, and usually is made up of smaller vessels than those assigned to a squadron, but some flotillas are smaller than squadrons and some include larger vessels. In some navies, the term <i>flotilla</i> is reserved for naval formations that operate on inland bodies of water, while the terms <i>fleet</i> and <i>squadron</i> denote naval formations that operate at sea. A flotilla may be a permanent or temporary formation. In modern times, a flotilla sometimes is an administrative naval unit responsible for maintaining and supporting vessels but not for commanding their operations at sea.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Informally, a group of naval or civilian vessels operating together or in close proximity to one another.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flotilla_holiday" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flotilla holiday</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A group of chartered <span title="See entry on this page at § yacht" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yacht" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yacht</a></span>s that set out together on the same route.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flotilla_leader" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flotilla_leader" title="Flotilla leader">flotilla leader</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A warship suitable for commanding a <a href="#flotilla"><span title="See entry on this page at § flotilla" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flotilla</span></a> of destroyers or other small warships, typically a small <a href="#cruiser"><span title="See entry on this page at § cruiser" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cruiser</span></a> or a large <a href="#destroyer"><span title="See entry on this page at § destroyer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">destroyer</span></a>, in the latter case known as a <a href="#destroyer_leader"><span title="See entry on this page at § destroyer leader" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">destroyer leader</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flotsam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flotsam_and_jetsam" class="mw-redirect" title="Flotsam and jetsam">flotsam</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Debris or cargo that remains afloat after a <span title="See entry on this page at § shipwreck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shipwreck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shipwreck</a></span>. See also <i><a href="#jetsam"><span title="See entry on this page at § jetsam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jetsam</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fluke" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/fluke" class="extiw" title="wikt:Special:Search/fluke">fluke</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The wedge-shaped part of an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>'s arms that digs into the solid bottom beneath a body of water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flush_deck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flush_deck" title="Flush deck">flush deck</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An upper <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> of a vessel that extends unbroken from <span title="See entry on this page at § stem" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stem" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stem</a></span> to <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flush_decker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flush_decker" class="mw-redirect" title="Flush decker">flush decker</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Any vessel with a <a href="#flush_deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § flush deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flush deck</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A US Navy <a href="#destroyer"><span title="See entry on this page at § destroyer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">destroyer</span></a> of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>-era <a href="/wiki/Caldwell-class_destroyer" title="Caldwell-class destroyer"><i>Caldwell</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Wickes-class_destroyer" title="Wickes-class destroyer"><i>Wickes</i></a>, or <a href="/wiki/Clemson-class_destroyer" title="Clemson-class destroyer"><i>Clemson</i>&#x20;class</a>, produced in very large numbers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flushing_board" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flushing board</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A board inserted vertically in a <a href="#cabin"><span title="See entry on this page at § cabin" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cabin</span></a> entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fluyt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fluyt" title="Fluyt">fluyt</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="flute"></span><span class="anchor" id="fluit"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>fluit</b> or <b>flute</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A Dutch transoceanic sailing cargo vessel, <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> with two or three masts that were much taller than the masts of a <a href="#galleon"><span title="See entry on this page at § galleon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">galleon</span></a>, developed in the 16th century and widely used in the 17th and 18th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fly_by_night" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fly-by-night" class="extiw" title="wikt:fly-by-night">fly by night</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large sail used only for sailing downwind, requiring little attention.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="folding_propeller" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Folding_propeller" title="Folding propeller">folding propeller</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § propeller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#propeller" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">propeller</a></span> with folding blades, furling so as to reduce drag on a sailing vessel when not in use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="following_sea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Following_sea" title="Following sea">following sea</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Waves going in the same direction as a ship, or within 15° of the heading, at a speed slower than the ship. See <span title="See entry on this page at § overtaking sea" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#overtaking_sea" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">overtaking sea</a></span> for waves travelling faster than the ship.<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_V3_1965_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders_V3_1965-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="foo-foo_band" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">foo-foo band</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An impromptu musical band on late 19th-century sailing vessels, made up from members of the ship's crew.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="foot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Leach_(sail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Leach (sail)">foot</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The lower edge of any <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The bottom of a <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;An Imperial unit of length equivalent to 12 inches (30&#160;cm).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="footloose" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">footloose</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">If the <a href="#foot"><span title="See entry on this page at § foot" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foot</span></a> of a sail is not secured properly, it is footloose, blowing around in the wind.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="footboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">footboat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A barge's boat or <a href="#dinghy"><span title="See entry on this page at § dinghy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dinghy</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="footrope" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Footrope" title="Footrope">footrope</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Each yard on a <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> sailing ship is equipped with a footrope for sailors to stand on while setting or stowing the sails.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="force" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">force</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#beaufort_scale"><span title="See entry on this page at § Beaufort scale" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Beaufort scale</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fore</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="forward"></span><span class="anchor" id="for&#39;ard"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>forward</b> (often written as <b>for'ard</b>).</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">Toward the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fore-and-aft_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fore-and-aft_rig" title="Fore-and-aft rig">fore-and-aft rig</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing <span title="See entry on this page at § rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rig</a></span> consisting mainly of sails that are set along the line of the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> rather than perpendicular to it. Such sails, and the vessel itself, are often referred to as "fore-and-aft-rigged".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fore-and-afters" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fore-and-afters</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Removable wooded beams running along the centre of the hold openings, beneath the hatches that they support.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fore_horse" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fore horse</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A transverse wooden or iron beam <a href="#afore"><span title="See entry on this page at § afore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">afore</span></a> the main mast to which the <a href="#foresail"><span title="See entry on this page at § foresail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foresail</span></a> sheet is attached.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forecastle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Forecastle" title="Forecastle">forecastle</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(pronounced <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/əl/: &#39;le&#39; in &#39;bottle&#39;">əl</span></span>/</a></span></span>) A partial <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> above the upper deck and at the head of the vessel; traditionally the location of the sailors' living quarters. The name is derived from the castle fitted to bear archers in time of war.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forefoot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Forefoot_(ship)" title="Forefoot (ship)">forefoot</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The lower part of the <span title="See entry on this page at § stem" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stem" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stem</a></span> of a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forehold" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">forehold</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The forward (i.e., front) part of a <a href="#hold"><span title="See entry on this page at § hold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hold</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="foremast_jack" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">foremast jack</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An enlisted sailor, one who is housed before the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forepeak" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">forepeak</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The part of the <a href="#hold"><span title="See entry on this page at § hold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hold</span></a> of a ship within the angle of the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="foresail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Foresail" title="Foresail">foresail</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> sail set on the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The lowest sail set on the foremast of a <a href="#full-rigged_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § full-rigged ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">full-rigged ship</span></a> or other <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forestay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Forestay" title="Forestay">forestay</a></dfn></dt>
