<dd class="glossary">A long <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> or <a href="#cable"><span title="See entry on this page at § cable" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cable</span></a> reaching from the bow of the vessel to the <span title="See entry on this page at § masthead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#masthead" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mastheads</a></span>, used to support the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forestaysail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">forestaysail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A triangular sail set on the <a href="#forestay"><span title="See entry on this page at § forestay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forestay</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="foul" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Foul_(nautical)" title="Foul (nautical)">foul</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Having freedom of motion interfered with by collision or entanglement; entangled; the opposite of <a href="#clear"><span title="See entry on this page at § clear" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clear</span></a>. For instance, a rope is foul when it does not run straight or smoothly, and an anchor is foul when it is caught on an obstruction.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A ship′s bottom is foul when it is overgrown with marine life such as <a href="/wiki/Barnacle" title="Barnacle">barnacles</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;An area of water treacherous to navigation due to many shallow obstructions such as reefs, sandbars, rocks, etc.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;A breach of racing rules.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">5.&#160;&#160;<i>Foul the range</i>: To block another vessel from firing her guns at a target.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="foulies" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">foulies</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A slang term for <span title="See entry on this page at § oilskin" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#oilskin" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">oilskins</a></span>, the foul-weather clothing worn by sailors.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="founder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/founder" class="extiw" title="wikt:founder">founder</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To fill with water and sink.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="four_piper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Four_piper" title="Four piper">four piper</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A term sometimes used to refer to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> four-funneled <a href="#destroyer"><span title="See entry on this page at § destroyer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">destroyers</span></a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bainbridge-class_destroyer" title="Bainbridge-class destroyer"><i>Bainbridge</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulding-class_destroyer" title="Paulding-class destroyer"><i>Paulding</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Wickes-class_destroyer" title="Wickes-class destroyer"><i>Wickes</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clemson-class_destroyer" title="Clemson-class destroyer"><i>Clemson</i></a> classes, all built for service in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fourth_rate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fourth_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fourth rate">fourth rate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> during the first half of the 18th century, a <span title="See entry on this page at § ship-of-the-line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship-of-the-line" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship-of-the-line</a></span> mounting between 46 and 60 guns.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frame" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">frame</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A transverse structural member that gives the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> strength and shape. Wooden frames may be sawn, bent, or laminated into shape; planking is then fastened to the frames. A bent frame is called a timber.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="freeboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Freeboard_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Freeboard (ship)">freeboard</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The height of a ship's <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> (excluding the superstructure) above the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>; the vertical distance from the current waterline to the lowest point on the highest continuous watertight deck. This usually varies from one part to another.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="freighter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cargo_ship" title="Cargo ship">freighter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#cargo_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § cargo ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cargo ship</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frigate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigate</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In the 17th century, any warship built for speed and maneuverability.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In the 18th and early 19th centuries, a sailing warship with a single continuous gun deck, typically used for patrolling, blockading, etc., but not in line of battle.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;In the second half of the 19th century, a type of warship combining sail and steam propulsion, typically of ironclad timber construction, with all guns on one deck.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;In the 20th and 21st centuries, a warship, smaller than a <a href="#destroyer"><span title="See entry on this page at § destroyer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">destroyer</span></a>, originally introduced during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as an anti-submarine vessel but now general-purpose.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">5.&#160;&#160;In the US Navy from the 1950s until the 1970s, a type of <a href="/wiki/Guided-missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Guided-missile">guided-missile</a> <a href="/wiki/Antiaircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiaircraft">antiaircraft</a> ship built on a destroyer-sized hull, all of which were reclassified as "<a href="/wiki/Guided-missile_cruiser" class="mw-redirect" title="Guided-missile cruiser">guided-missile cruisers</a>" in 1975.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="full_and_by" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">full and by</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Sailing into the wind (<i>by</i>), but not as <a href="#close-hauled"><span title="See entry on this page at § close-hauled" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">close-hauled</span></a> as might be possible, so as to make sure the sails are kept <i>full</i>. This provides a margin for error to avoid being taken <a href="#aback"><span title="See entry on this page at § aback" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aback</span></a> in a tricky sea (a serious risk for <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> vessels). Figuratively it implies getting on with the job but in a steady, relaxed way, without undue urgency or strain.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="full-rigged_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Full-rigged_ship" title="Full-rigged ship">full-rigged ship</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="full-rigged"></span><span class="anchor" id="full_rigged"></span><span class="anchor" id="full_rigged_ship"></span><span class="anchor" id="full_rigging"></span><span class="anchor" id="fully-rigged"></span><span class="anchor" id="fully_rigged"></span><span class="anchor" id="fully-rigged_ship"></span><span class="anchor" id="fully_rigged_ship"></span>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing vessel with three or more <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span>, all of them <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span>. A full-rigged ship is said to have a "ship rig".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="full_steam_ahead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">full steam ahead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">With as much speed as possible.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="funnel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">funnel</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="stack"></span>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Funnel_(ship)" title="Funnel (ship)">funnel</a>) Also <b>stack</b>. The smokestack of a ship, used to expel boiler steam and smoke or engine exhaust.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<i>Ventilation funnel</i>: A curved, rotatable tube protruding from the deck of a vessel, designed to direct fresh air into her interior.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="furious_fifties" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Furious_Fifties" class="mw-redirect" title="Furious Fifties">Furious Fifties</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Strong westerly winds found in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, generally between the latitudes of <a href="/wiki/50th_parallel_south" title="50th parallel south">50</a> and <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_south" title="60th parallel south">60</a> degrees. They are stronger than the similar "<a href="/wiki/Roaring_Forties" title="Roaring Forties">Roaring Forties</a>" to their north.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="furl" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">furl</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To roll or gather a <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> against its <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fusta" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Fusta" title="Fusta">fusta</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="fuste"></span><span class="anchor" id="foist"></span><span class="anchor" id="galliot"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>fuste</b>, <b>foist</b>, or <b>galliot</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A narrow, light, and fast ship with a shallow <a href="#draft"><span title="See entry on this page at § draft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">draft</span></a>, powered both by oars and sail, with a single mast carrying a <a href="#lateen"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen</span></a> sail; a favorite of North African <a href="#corsair"><span title="See entry on this page at § corsair" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">corsairs</span></a> during the 16th and 17th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="furnace" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">furnace</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="#boiler"><span title="See entry on this page at § Boiler" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Boiler</span></a> component where fuel is burned.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="futtock_shrouds" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Futtock_shrouds" title="Futtock shrouds">futtock shrouds</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rope, wire, or chain links in the rigging of a traditional <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> ship running from the outer edges of a <span title="See entry on this page at § top" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#top" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">top</a></span> downwards and inwards to a point on the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> or lower <span title="See entry on this page at § shroud" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shroud" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shrouds</a></span>. They carry the load of the shrouds that rise from the edge of the top, preventing the top from tilting relative to the mast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="futtocks" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">futtocks</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Pieces of timber that make up a large transverse <a href="#frame"><span title="See entry on this page at § frame" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">frame</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="gaff" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaff</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Gaff_rig" title="Gaff rig">gaff rig</a>) A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> that holds the upper edge of a four-sided <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-mounted</span></a> sail. On a hoisting gaff, the lower end is supported by gaff jaws which partly encircle the mast; it is hoisted using <span title="See entry on this page at § peak" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#peak" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">peak</a></span> and <span title="See entry on this page at § throat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#throat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">throat</a></span> <a href="#halliard"><span title="See entry on this page at § halliard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">halliards</span></a>. A standing gaff remains aloft, its sails brailed when not in use.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Fishing_gaff" title="Fishing gaff">fishing gaff</a>) A hook on a long pole used to haul in fish.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaff_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gaff_rig" title="Gaff rig">gaff rig</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="gaff_rigged"></span>
<dd class="glossary">A boat rigged with a four-sided <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> sail set <a href="#abaft"><span title="See entry on this page at § abaft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">abaft</span></a> the mast, its head being spread by a <a href="#gaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a>. The gaff may be standing (permanently in position) with the sail being brailed up to the gaff when not in use, or, more commonly, is hoisted using two halliards: the peak and the throat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaff_topsail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaff topsail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> sail set above a <a href="#gaff_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff-rigged</span></a> sail, with the <a href="#clew"><span title="See entry on this page at § clew" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clew</span></a> sheeted to the end of the  <a href="#gaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaff_vang" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaff vang</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> rigged to the end of a <a href="#gaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a> and used to adjust a gaff sail's <span title="See entry on this page at § trim" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#trim" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">trim</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gale" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gale</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#ghali"><span title="See entry on this page at § ghali" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ghali</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gali" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gali</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#ghali"><span title="See entry on this page at § ghali" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ghali</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="galleass" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Galleass" title="Galleass">galleass</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;An oared warship of the 16th century equipped with a <a href="#gun_deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § gun deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gun deck</span></a>; larger and equipped with more sails than a <a href="#galley"><span title="See entry on this page at § galley" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">galley</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A flat-bottomed commercial sailing vessel of the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and western <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="galleon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Galleon" title="Galleon">galleon</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large, multi-decked sailing ship with a prominent, squared-off, raised <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>, generally carrying three or more <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span>, typically <a href="#lateen"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen</span></a> <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> on the rear mast and <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> on the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainmast</a></span> and <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a>. Galleons were used primarily as armed cargo carriers and sometimes as <span title="See entry on this page at § warship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#warship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">warships</a></span> by European states from the 16th to the 18th centuries.</dd>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15th_century_galleon.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/15th_century_galleon.JPG/220px-15th_century_galleon.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/15th_century_galleon.JPG/330px-15th_century_galleon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/15th_century_galleon.JPG/440px-15th_century_galleon.JPG 2x" data-file-width="677" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15th_century_galleon.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration of a typical 15th-century <b><a href="#galleon"><span title="See entry on this page at § galleon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">galleon</span></a></b></div></div></div>
<dt class="glossary" id="galley" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">galley</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Galley_(kitchen)" title="Galley (kitchen)">galley (kitchen)</a>) The compartment of a ship where food is cooked or prepared; a ship's kitchen.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">galley</a>) A type of ship propelled by <span title="See entry on this page at § oar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#oar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">oars</a></span>, used especially in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> for warfare, piracy, and trade from the 8th century BC to the 16th century AD, with some in use until the early 19th century.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A type of oared <a href="#gunboat"><span title="See entry on this page at § gunboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gunboat</span></a> built by the United States in the late 18th century, akin to a <a href="#brigantine"><span title="See entry on this page at § brigantine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">brigantine</span></a> but termed "galley" for administrative and funding purposes.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="galliot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">galliot</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#fusta"><span title="See entry on this page at § fusta" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fusta</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gam_(nautical_term)" title="Gam (nautical term)">gam</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A meeting of two (or more) <span title="See entry on this page at § whaler" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#whaler" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">whaling ships</a></span> at sea. The ships each send out a boat to the other, and the two captains meet on one ship, while the two chief mates meet on the other.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gammon_iron" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gammon iron</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> fitting that clamps the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a> to the <span title="See entry on this page at § stem" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stem" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stem</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gangplank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gangplank</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>brow</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A movable bridge used in boarding or leaving a ship at a pier.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gangway" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gangway</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An opening in the <a href="#bulwark"><span title="See entry on this page at § bulwark" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bulwark</span></a> of a ship to allow passengers to board or leave the ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gantline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gantline</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rope running through a <a href="#block"><span title="See entry on this page at § block" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">block</span></a> at or near the <span title="See entry on this page at § masthead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#masthead" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masthead</a></span>, with both ends reaching the <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a>. It is used solely for hoisting and lowering crew members and/or tools into the <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span> for maintenance and repair work.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="garbling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">garbling</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The illegal practice of mixing cargo with garbage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="garboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">garboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <span title="See entry on this page at § strake" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#strake" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">strake</a></span> closest to the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> (from Dutch <i>gaarboard</i>).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="garboard_planks" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">garboard planks</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The planks immediately on either side of the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gash" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gash</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any refuse or rubbish discarded into a refuse container or dustbin, also known as "gash fanny" (South African Navy).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gasket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gasket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rope used to secure a sail (particularly the <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span>) when stowed.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gate_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gate ship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An alternative term for a <span title="See entry on this page at § net-laying ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#net-laying_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">net-laying ship</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gear" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gear</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A collective term for a vessel's <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sails</a></span> and <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="geedunk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">geedunk</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Ice cream, snacks, etc. Also the place selling such items.<sup id="cite_ref-NHHC_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHHC-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="general_quarters" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">general quarters</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#battle_stations"><span title="See entry on this page at § battle stations" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battle stations</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gennaker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gennaker" title="Gennaker">gennaker</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large, lightweight sail used for sailing a <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft rig</span></a> down or across the wind, intermediate between a <a href="#genoa"><span title="See entry on this page at § genoa" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">genoa</span></a> and a <span title="See entry on this page at § spinnaker" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spinnaker" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spinnaker</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="genoa" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Genoa_(sail)" title="Genoa (sail)">genoa</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="genny"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>genny</b>. (both <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>)</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A large <a href="#jib"><span title="See entry on this page at § jib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jib</span></a>, strongly overlapping the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainmast</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ghali" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ghali_(ship)" title="Ghali (ship)">ghali</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>gali</b> or <b>gale</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">Any of several types of <a href="#galley"><span title="See entry on this page at § galley" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">galley</span></a>-like ships from the <a href="/wiki/Nusantara_(archipelago)" title="Nusantara (archipelago)">Nusantara</a> archipelago in Southeast Asia. The term refers both to Mediterranean vessels built by local people and to native vessels with Mediterranean influence.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ghost" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ghost</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To sail slowly when there is apparently no wind.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ghost_fleet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ghost fleet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In the modern United States, an informal term for a <span title="See entry on this page at § reserve fleet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#reserve_fleet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">reserve fleet</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gibe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gibe</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#gybe"><span title="See entry on this page at § gybe" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gybe</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gig_(boat)" title="Gig (boat)">gig</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of open boat designed primarily for propulsion under oar, but often fitted with a sailing rig for appropriate conditions. Used most often for the swift transport of one or a few people, as in a pilot gig or as a naval <a href="/wiki/Ship%27s_boat" title="Ship&#39;s boat">ship's boat</a>. In US Navy usage, a captain's gig is reserved for use by a ship's captain and, in modern times, is a power-boat.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gillnetter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gillnetter" class="mw-redirect" title="Gillnetter">gillnetter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fishing vessel that employs <a href="/wiki/Gillnetting" title="Gillnetting">gillnetting</a> as its means of catching fish.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gin-pole" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gin-pole</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>jin-pole</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A pole that is attached perpendicular to a <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>, to be used as a lever for raising the mast.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="girt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">girt</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Said of a vessel moored by cables to two <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchors</span></a> in such a way that the force of a current or tide causes her to swing against one of the cables.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To <a href="#capsize"><span title="See entry on this page at § capsize" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">capsize</span></a> because of forces exerted on a cable by another vessel attached to it. <i>Tug girting</i> specifically refers to girting that causes a <span title="See entry on this page at § tugboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tugboat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tugboat</a></span> to capsize because of forces placed on a cable attached to her by another vessel attached to the same cable.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="give-way" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">give-way</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In a situation where two vessels are approaching one another so as to involve a risk of collision, the vessel directed to keep out of the way of the other.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="glass" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">glass</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A marine <a href="/wiki/Barometer" title="Barometer">barometer</a>. Older barometers used mercury-filled glass tubes to measure and indicate barometric pressure.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § marine sandglass" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#marine_sandglass" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">marine sandglass</a></span> (<i>q.v.</i>).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="global_positioning_system_(gps)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">Global Positioning System</a> (GPS)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A satellite-based radionavigation system providing continuous worldwide coverage of geolocation and time information to air, marine, and land users wherever there is an unobstructed line of sight to at least four GPS satellites developed and operated by the United States Department of Defense but publicly available for use by anyone with an enabled GPS receiver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="go-fast_boat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Go-fast_boat" title="Go-fast boat">go-fast boat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small, fast boat designed with a long narrow platform and a planing <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> to enable it to reach high speeds. Colloquially equivalent to a "rum-runner" or a "cigarette boat".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="goat_locker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Goat_locker" title="Goat locker">goat locker</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A mess hall reserved for <a href="/wiki/Chief_petty_officer" title="Chief petty officer">chief petty officers</a> in the United States Navy.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="going_about" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">going about</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Changing from one <span title="See entry on this page at § tack" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tack" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tack</a></span> to another by going through the wind. See also <i><a href="#gybe"><span title="See entry on this page at § gybe" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gybe</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gondola" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gondola" title="Gondola">gondola</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A traditional, flat-bottomed Venetian rowing boat.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An alternative term for a <a href="#gundalow"><span title="See entry on this page at § gundalow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gundalow</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gooseneck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gooseneck</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fitting that attaches a <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> to a <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> yet allows it to move freely.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="goosewinged" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">goosewinged</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(of a <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> vessel) Sailing directly away from the wind, with the sails set on opposite sides of the vessel (e.g. with the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span> to port and the <a href="#jib"><span title="See entry on this page at § jib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jib</span></a> to starboard) so as to maximize the amount of canvas exposed to the wind. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § running" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#running" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">running</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="grapeshot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Grapeshot" title="Grapeshot">grapeshot</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Small balls of lead fired from a <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannon</a>, analogous to <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">shotgun</a> shot but on a larger scale; similar to <a href="#canister_shot"><span title="See entry on this page at § canister shot" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">canister shot</span></a> but with larger individual shot. Intended specifically to injure personnel and damage <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span> more than to cause structural damage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="grave" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">grave</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To clean a ship's bottom.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="graving_dock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Graving_dock" class="mw-redirect" title="Graving dock">graving dock</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A narrow basin, usually made of earthen berms and concrete, closed by gates or by a <a href="/wiki/Caisson_(engineering)" title="Caisson (engineering)">caisson</a>, into which a vessel may be floated and the water pumped out, leaving the vessel supported on blocks; the classic form of <a href="#drydock"><span title="See entry on this page at § drydock" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">drydock</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="graybeard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">graybeard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#cape_Horn_roller"><span title="See entry on this page at § Cape Horn roller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Cape Horn roller</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="great-circle_navigation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Great-circle_navigation" title="Great-circle navigation">great-circle navigation</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The practice of navigating a vessel along the arc of a <a href="/wiki/Great_circle" title="Great circle">great circle</a>. Such routes yield the shortest possible distance between any given pair of points on the surface of the Earth.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="green-to-green" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">green-to-green</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A passage of two vessels moving in the opposite direction on their <span title="See entry on this page at § starboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#starboard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">starboard</a></span> sides, so called because the green navigation light on one of the vessels faces the green light on the other vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="greenlandman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Greenlandman" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenlandman">Greenlandman</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A British term used in the 18th and 19th centuries for any <span title="See entry on this page at § whaling ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#whaling_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">whaling ship</a></span> operating in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a> or northern waters near the Arctic.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gridiron" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gridiron</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large metal cross-frame on which vessels are placed at high water for examination, cleaning, and repairs after the tide falls.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gripe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gripe</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A temporary eye in a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> (rope).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="griping" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">griping</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The tendency of a ship to turn into the wind despite the efforts of the <a href="#helmsman"><span title="See entry on this page at § helmsman" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">helmsman</span></a>, usually due to either the design of a ship or more commonly the incorrect distribution of weight on and within the hull.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gripie" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gripie</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A Cockney (London dialect) name for a <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="grog" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Grog" title="Grog">grog</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Watered-down pusser's <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a> consisting of half a gill with an equal part of water, issued to all seamen over twenty (CPOs and POs were issued with neat rum). From the British <a href="/wiki/Edward_Vernon" title="Edward Vernon">Admiral Vernon</a> who, in 1740, ordered the men's <a href="/wiki/Rum_Ration" class="mw-redirect" title="Rum Ration">ration of rum</a> to be watered down. He was called "Old Grogram" because he often wore a <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_textile_manufacturing" title="Glossary of textile manufacturing">grogram</a> coat, and the watered rum came to be called grog. Specific quantities of grog were often traded illegally as a form of currency; a sailor might repay a colleague for a favour by giving him part or all of his grog ration, ranging from "sippers" (a small amount) via "gulpers" (a larger quantity) to "grounders" (the entire tot). Additional issues of grog were made on the command "<span title="See entry on this page at § splice the mainbrace" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#splice_the_mainbrace" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">splice the mainbrace</a></span>" for celebrations or as a reward for performing especially onerous duties. The Royal Navy discontinued the practice of issuing rum in 1970.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="groggy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">groggy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Drunk from having consumed a lot of <a href="#grog"><span title="See entry on this page at § grog" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">grog</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="grommet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Grommet" title="Grommet">grommet</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A metal or plastic ring inserted in canvas to prevent wear.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A ring of rope.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;An <a href="/wiki/Grommet_(sportsperson)" title="Grommet (sportsperson)">inexperienced surfer</a> or extreme sports participant.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ground" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ground</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The bed of the sea; the underwater surface or sea floor to which an <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a> holds.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="grounding" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">grounding</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">When a ship (while afloat) touches the <a href="#ground"><span title="See entry on this page at § ground" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bed of the sea</span></a>, or runs <a href="#aground"><span title="See entry on this page at § aground" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aground</span></a>. A moored vessel that grounds as the tide goes out is said to "take the ground".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="groundway" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">groundway</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>ground way</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A substantial foundation of wood or stone for the blocks on which a vessel is built, typically lying on either side of the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> of a ship under construction, which also serves to support and guide the blocks when they slide to carry the vessel into the water when she is launched.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="growler" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">growler</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small <a href="/wiki/Iceberg" title="Iceberg">iceberg</a> or ice floe barely visible above the surface of the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="guineaman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Guineaman</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Another name for a <span title="See entry on this page at § slave ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#slave_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">slave ship</a></span>, coined after the emergence of the transatlantic slave trade from Africa in the 15th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="guards" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">guards</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>paddle guards</b> and <b>wheel guards</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(on an oceangoing sidewheel <span title="See entry on this page at § steamship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#steamship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">steamship</a></span>) Horizontal structures, usually of wood, built around the <span title="See entry on this page at § paddle box" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#paddle_box" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">paddle boxes</a></span> just above their lowest point and extending a short distance <a href="#forward"><span title="See entry on this page at § forward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forward</span></a> and <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a>, designed to protect them from damage and to provide additional support for the paddle shaft.<sup id="cite_ref-ridgely-nevitt1981_p371_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ridgely-nevitt1981_p371-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(on an American sidewheel steamboat) Extensions of the <a href="/wiki/Main_deck" title="Main deck">main deck</a> beyond the hull to the outer extremity of the paddle boxes, and tapering to the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> and <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> (thus giving the deck a characteristic oval shape), to increase the available deck space for passengers, cargo, and/or machinery.<sup id="cite_ref-ridgely-nevitt1981_p371_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ridgely-nevitt1981_p371-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="guard_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Guard_ship" title="Guard ship">guard ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Any vessel that makes the rounds of a <a href="#fleet"><span title="See entry on this page at § fleet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fleet</span></a> at anchor to see that due watch is kept at night.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § warship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#warship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">warship</a></span> stationed at a port or harbour to act as a guard there.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;In former times in the British Royal Navy, a ship that received men impressed for naval service, often the <a href="#flagship"><span title="See entry on this page at § flagship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flagship</span></a> of the <a href="#admiral"><span title="See entry on this page at § admiral" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">admiral</span></a> commanding along the coast.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;In Soviet and Russian terminology, a guard ship (<i>storozhevoj korabl<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span></i>) is a small, general-purpose patrol or escort vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gun_deck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gun_deck" title="Gun deck">gun deck</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Up through the 19th century, a <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> aboard a ship that was primarily used for the mounting of <a href="#cannon"><span title="See entry on this page at § cannon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cannon</span></a> to be fired in <a href="#broadside"><span title="See entry on this page at § broadside" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">broadsides</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;On smaller vessels (of <a href="#frigate"><span title="See entry on this page at § frigate" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">frigate</span></a> size or smaller) up through the 19th century, the completely covered level under the upper deck, though in such smaller ships it carried none of the ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s guns.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;On marine seismic survey vessels, the lowest deck on the ship, which carries the seismic source arrays, consisting of air guns arranged in clusters.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;In naval slang, to fabricate or falsify something; in modern usage, meaning especially to falsify documentation in order to avoid doing work or make present conditions seem acceptable without having made a real effort to improve them.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gundecking" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gundecking</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Falsifying of records and reports.<sup id="cite_ref-NHHC_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHHC-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gundalow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gundalow" title="Gundalow">gundalow</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of flat-bottomed sailing <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a> with a single large <a href="#lateen_sail"><span title="See entry on this page at § lateen sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lateen sail</span></a> <a href="#brail"><span title="See entry on this page at § brail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">brailed</span></a> to a heavy <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yard</a></span>, used on rivers in <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> from the mid-17th century to the early 20th century. Sometimes referred to as a <i><a href="#gondola"><span title="See entry on this page at § gondola" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gondola</span></a></i> in period accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gunner&#39;s_daughter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gunner's daughter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#kissing_the_gunner&#39;s_daughter"><span title="See entry on this page at § kissing the gunner&#39;s daughter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">kissing the gunner's daughter</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gunport" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gunport</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An opening in the side of a ship or in a turret through which a gun fires or protrudes.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gunter_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gunter_rig" title="Gunter rig">gunter rig</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>sliding gunter</b> or <b>gunter lug</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> sail set <a href="#abaft"><span title="See entry on this page at § abaft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">abaft</span></a> (behind) the mast, approximately triangular in shape, with the top half of the <a href="#luff"><span title="See entry on this page at § luff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">luff</span></a> (front) of the sail attached to a <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yard</a></span> which extends the sail above the top of the mast. The yard is raised and lowered with the sail.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> This traditional sail is popular in small boats and produces aerodynamic performance close to that of the highly developed <a href="#bermuda_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § Bermuda rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Bermuda rig</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nichols_2014_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nichols_2014-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gunwale" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Gunwale" title="Gunwale">gunwale</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Rarely <b>gunnel</b>. (both <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="/ʌ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">ʌ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/əl/: &#39;le&#39; in &#39;bottle&#39;">əl</span></span>/</a></span></span>)</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">Generally, the upper edge of the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>; more specifically, in an open (undecked) boat of timber construction, the longitudinal stringer that connects the top of the ribs.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975101_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975101-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gurdy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gurdy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A mechanical crank used to set and retrieve fishing lines.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="guy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">guy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A rope or <span title="See entry on this page at § stay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stay" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stay</a></span> leading to the side of the vessel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A rope used to steady a <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109_59-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955109-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gybe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jibe_(sailing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jibe (sailing)">gybe</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="jibe"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>jibe</b>. (both <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span></span>/</a></span></span>)</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">To change from one <span title="See entry on this page at § tack" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tack" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tack</a></span> to the other away from the wind, with the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> of the vessel turning through the wind. See also <i><a href="#going_about"><span title="See entry on this page at § going about" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">going about</span></a></i> and <i><span title="See entry on this page at § wearing ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#wearing_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">wearing ship</a></span></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gypsy_winch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gypsy winch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type or component of an anchor winch. The "gypsy" or "gypsy wheel" engages the anchor chain.</dd>
</dl>
