<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="half-breadth_plan" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">half-breadth plan</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Elevation_(view)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elevation (view)">elevation</a> of the lines of a ship, viewed from above and divided lengthwise.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="halyard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Halyard" title="Halyard">halyard</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="halliard"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>halliard</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">Originally, ropes used for hoisting a <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> with a <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> attached; today, a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> used to raise the head of any sail.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hammock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hammock" title="Hammock">hammock</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Canvas sheets, slung from the <a href="#deckhead"><span title="See entry on this page at § deckhead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deckhead</span></a> in <span title="See entry on this page at § messdecks" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#messdecks" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">messdecks</a></span>, in which seamen slept. "Lash up and stow" was a piped command to tie up hammocks and stow them (typically) in racks inboard of the ship's side so as to protect the crew from splinters from shot and provide a ready means of preventing flooding caused by damage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hamper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hamper</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Articles that normally are indispensable aboard ship but at certain times are in the way.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hand" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hand</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To furl a <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hand_bomber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hand bomber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship using coal-fired boilers shoveled in by hand.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hand_over_fist" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hand over fist</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To climb steadily upwards, from the motion of a sailor climbing <span title="See entry on this page at § shroud" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shroud" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shrouds</a></span> on a sailing ship (originally "hand over hand").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="handsomely" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">handsomely</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">With a slow even motion, as when hauling on a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> "handsomely".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="handy_billy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">handy billy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A loose block and tackle with a hook or tail on each end, which can be used wherever it is needed. Usually made up of one single and one double block.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hangar_deck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hangar deck</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An enclosed <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> on an <a href="#aircraft_carrier"><span title="See entry on this page at § aircraft carrier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aircraft carrier</span></a>, usually beneath the <a href="#flight_deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § flight deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flight deck</span></a> and intended for use as a <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangar</a> in servicing and storing aircraft.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hank</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fastener attached to the <a href="#luff"><span title="See entry on this page at § luff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">luff</span></a> of the <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a> that attaches the headsail to the <a href="#forestay"><span title="See entry on this page at § forestay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forestay</span></a>. Typical designs include a bronze or plastic hook with a spring-operated gate, or a strip of cloth webbing with a snap fastener.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harbour_of_refuge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">harbour of refuge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An artificial <a href="#harbour"><span title="See entry on this page at § harbour" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">harbour</span></a> constructed on a coast without a <span title="See entry on this page at § natural harbour" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#natural_harbour" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">natural harbour</a></span> to provide shelter for small vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harbour" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">harbour</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>harbor</b> or <b>haven</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A place where ships or smaller craft may shelter from the weather, are unloaded/loaded, or stored. Harbours can be man-made or natural.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harbour_dues" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">harbour dues</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The fees charged by the owners or operators of a harbour to those vessels using the harbour. Under British legislation, the person in charge of a vessel must report to the <a href="#harbourmaster"><span title="See entry on this page at § harbourmaster" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">harbourmaster</span></a> within 24 hours of arrival in a port where harbour dues are payable.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harbourmaster" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Harbourmaster" title="Harbourmaster">harbourmaster</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A person in charge of a <a href="#harbour"><span title="See entry on this page at § harbour" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">harbour</span></a>, with powers including the collection of the <a href="#harbour_dues"><span title="See entry on this page at § harbour dues" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">harbour dues</span></a>, instructing the masters of vessels where to moor, and overall safety within the area of the harbour, often including pilotage and navigational aids. In most countries the powers of a harbour master are laid down by legislation, and can be quite extensive.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A section of otherwise muddy shoreline suitable for mooring or hauling out.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hard-a-lee" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hard-a-lee</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#lee-oh"><span title="See entry on this page at § lee-oh" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lee-oh</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harden_in" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">harden in</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To haul in the sheet and tighten the sails.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harden_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">harden up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To turn towards the wind; to sail closer to the wind.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="harness_cask" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">harness cask</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>harness tub</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A large, usually round tub lashed to a vessel's deck and containing dried and salted provisions for daily use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hardtack" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hardtack" title="Hardtack">hardtack</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A hard and long-lasting dry biscuit, used as food on long journeys. Also called a "ship's biscuit".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hatchway" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hatchway" class="mw-redirect" title="Hatchway">hatchway</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="hatch"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>hatch</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A covered opening in a ship's <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> through which cargo can be loaded or access made to a lower deck; the cover to the opening is called a <i>hatch</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="haul" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">haul</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To steer (a vessel) closer to the direction of the wind.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To shift forward, i.e. more toward the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hauling_wind" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hauling wind</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Pointing the ship towards the direction of the wind; generally not the fastest point of travel on a sailing vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hawsepipe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hawsepipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawsepipe">hawsepipe</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="hawsehole"></span><span class="anchor" id="hawse"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>hawsehole</b> or <b>hawse</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The shaft or hole in the side of a vessel's <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> through which the <a href="#anchor_chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor chain</span></a> passes. "In through the hawsepipe" describes someone with experience and savvy.<sup id="cite_ref-NHHC_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHHC-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hawsepiper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hawsepiper" title="Hawsepiper">hawsepiper</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An informal term for an officer of a <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_ship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant ship</a></span> who began their career as an unlicensed merchant seaman, and so did not attend a traditional maritime academy to earn their officer's licence. See also <i><a href="#before_the_mast"><span title="See entry on this page at § before the mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">before the mast</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hawser" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hawser" title="Hawser">hawser</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large cable or rope used for mooring or towing a vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Head_(watercraft)" title="Head (watercraft)">head</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The forwardmost or uppermost portion of the ship.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The forwardmost or uppermost portion of any individual part of the ship, e.g. <span title="See entry on this page at § masthead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#masthead" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masthead</a></span>, <a href="#beakhead"><span title="See entry on this page at § beakhead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beakhead</span></a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § stemhead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stemhead" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stemhead</a></span>, etc.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The top edge of a sail.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;The <a href="/wiki/Toilet" title="Toilet">toilet</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latrine" title="Latrine">latrine</a> of a vessel, which in sailing ships usually projected from the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> and therefore was located in the "head" of the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head_boat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head boat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fishing boat that takes recreational fishermen out for a fee paid individually by each person (i.e. per head). A head boat differs from a <a href="#charter_boat"><span title="See entry on this page at § charter boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">charter boat</span></a>, which is a fishing boat that a party of fishermen hires for an agreed-upon period.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="head_of_navigation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Head_of_navigation" title="Head of navigation">Head of navigation</a></dfn></dt><dd class="glossary">The farthest point above the mouth of a river that can be navigated by ships.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head_rail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head rail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A curved rail that extends from the <a href="#figurehead"><span title="See entry on this page at § figurehead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">figurehead</span></a> to the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head_rope" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head rope</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The mooring rope that goes from the bow of a vessel to a point on a jetty a distance ahead of the bows.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Part of the <a href="#bolt_rope"><span title="See entry on this page at § bolt rope" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bolt rope</span></a>, at the head of a <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span>, running from the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> to the <span title="See entry on this page at § sprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sprit" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sprit</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head_sea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head sea</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sea in which waves are directly opposing the motion of the ship, or approaching within 15° of ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-Saunders_V3_1965_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saunders_V3_1965-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head-sail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head-sail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Jibs and staysails set between the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a> and the fore
<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Sometimes refers to the square sails on the fore-mast of a square rigged vessel.
<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="head-stays" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">head-stays</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Stays between the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a> and the foremost mast.
<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="header" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">header</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A change in the wind direction that forces the <a href="#helmsman"><span title="See entry on this page at § helmsman" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">helmsman</span></a> of a <a href="#close-hauled"><span title="See entry on this page at § close-hauled" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">close-hauled</span></a> sailboat to steer away from its current course to a less favorable one. This is the opposite of a <a href="#lift"><span title="See entry on this page at § lift" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lift</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heading" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Course_(navigation)#Course,_track,_route_and_heading" title="Course (navigation)">heading</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The direction in which the nose of a vessel is pointing (which is not necessarily the same as the direction in which the vessel is actually moving).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="headsail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Headsail" class="mw-redirect" title="Headsail">headsail</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Any <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> set in front of the most forward <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>. A sailing vessel may have one or more headsails. A headsail may be <a href="#hank"><span title="See entry on this page at § hank" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hank</span></a>ed to a stay, or may be set flying, with the <a href="#luff"><span title="See entry on this page at § luff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">luff</span></a> being kept taut by the tension of the halyard. Where several headsails are set, a complex arrangement might be termed (from the front and top) flying jib, outer jib, inner jib, and (fore) staysail; less complex would be <a href="#jib"><span title="See entry on this page at § jib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jib</span></a> and <span title="See entry on this page at § staysail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#staysail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">staysail</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMayne2000142_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayne2000142-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="headstick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">headstick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> laced to the head of the <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heave" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">heave</dfn></dt><dd class="glossary">A vessel's transient, vertical, up-and-down motion.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heave_down" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">heave down</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To turn a ship on its side (for cleaning), a process which is also known as <i><a href="#careening"><span title="See entry on this page at § careening" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">careening</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heave_ho!" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Heave ho!</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An exclamation sailors make when pulling forcefully on a rope.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heave_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Heave_to" class="mw-redirect" title="Heave to">heave to</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <a href="#hove_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § Hove to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Hove to</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heavy_weather" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">heavy weather</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A combination of high winds and rough seas that may be dangerous for a ship or boat, sometimes requiring changes to a passage plan (such as a precautionary diversion to a safe harbour), <a href="#heaving_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § heaving to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">heaving to</span></a>, running under bare poles, or other similar survival strategies.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="heel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Heeling_(sailing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heeling (sailing)">heel</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The lean caused by the wind's force on the <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sails</a></span> of a sailing vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The inclination or canting of a vessel to one side or the other from the vertical as she maneuvers, e.g. "The ship heeled to port as she turned to starboard".</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The lowest or last part of something, such as the <i>heel of the mast</i> or the <i>heel of the vessel</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="helm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">helm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A ship's steering mechanism, such as a <span title="See entry on this page at § tiller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tiller" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tiller</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s wheel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_wheel" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's wheel</a></span>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The wheel and/or <span title="See entry on this page at § wheelhouse" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#wheelhouse" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">wheelhouse</a></span> area.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;(v.) To take over the steering of a vessel.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="helmsman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Helmsman" title="Helmsman">helmsman</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>steersman</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A member of the <a href="#crew"><span title="See entry on this page at § crew" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crew</span></a> who is responsible for steering the ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="herring_buss" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Herring_buss" title="Herring buss">herring buss</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of seagoing fishing vessel used by Dutch and Flemish herring fishermen from the 15th through the early 19th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="highfield_lever" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">highfield lever</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of tensioning lever, usually for running <a href="#backstay"><span title="See entry on this page at § backstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">backstays</span></a>. Their use allows the <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a> backstay to be completely slackened so that the <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> can be let fully out.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hitch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/List_of_hitch_knots" title="List of hitch knots">hitch</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A knot used to tie a rope or <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> to a fixed object. See also <i><a href="#bend"><span title="See entry on this page at § bend" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bend</span></a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hobby_horsing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hobby horsing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Harmonic <a href="/wiki/Ship_motions" title="Ship motions">pitching</a> of a vessel forward and backward.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hog" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hog</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> structural member of the hull fitted over the keel to provide a fixing for the <a href="#garboard"><span title="See entry on this page at § garboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">garboard</span></a> planks.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A rough, flat scrubbing brush for cleaning a ship's bottom under water.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A semi-permanent bend in a ship's keel, especially in wooden-hulled ships, caused over time by the ship's center being more buoyant than her <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> or <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hog_frame" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hog frame</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A heavy wooden <a href="/wiki/Truss" title="Truss">truss</a> fitted lengthwise along each side of a large American steamboat, secured to the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> and rising above deck just outside the <span title="See entry on this page at § superstructure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#superstructure" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">superstructure</a></span>, to provide support for the hull and prevent <a href="#hogging"><span title="See entry on this page at § hogging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hogging</span></a>. Similar in appearance and function to a <a href="/wiki/Truss_bridge" title="Truss bridge">truss bridge</a>. See also <a href="#king_post"><span title="See entry on this page at § king post" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">king post</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hog_islander" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hog_Islander" title="Hog Islander">Hog Islander</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Slang term used for <a href="/wiki/Design_1022_ship" class="mw-redirect" title="Design 1022 ship">Design 1022</a> <a href="#cargo_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § cargo ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cargo ship</span></a>s and <a href="/wiki/Design_1024_ship" class="mw-redirect" title="Design 1024 ship">Design 1024</a> <span title="See entry on this page at § troop transport" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#troop_transport" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">troop transport</a></span>s constructed at <a href="/wiki/Hog_Island,_Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Hog Island, Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Hog Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, to address <span title="See entry on this page at § merchant marine" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#merchant_marine" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">merchant marine</a></span> shortfalls in the United States during <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a></span>. Completed too late for <span class="nowrap">World War I,</span> Hog Islanders saw <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Merchant_Marine" title="United States Merchant Marine">United States Merchant Marine</a> service prior to and during <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</span></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hogging" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hogging_and_sagging" title="Hogging and sagging">hogging</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A condition in which the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> of a vessel bends upward so the ends of the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> are lower than the middle. (Contrast with <span title="See entry on this page at § sagging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sagging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sagging</a></span>.) Hogging can occur when the peak of a wave is <a href="#amidships"><span title="See entry on this page at § amidships" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">amidships</span></a> or during loading or unloading of a vessel and can damage her or even break her in half.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A permanent distortion of the hull in the same manner caused, over time, by the bow and stern of a ship being less buoyant than the midships section. During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>, shipwrights employed a number of different designs of braces to stiffen ships' hulls against this warping.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hogging_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hogging line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A line passed under a ship from side to side to pull a collision mat into place over a leak.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Also a line passed under a ship from side to side used as a reference to indicate position of a frame during underwater inspections.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hoist" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hoist</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The height of a <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> sail as measured next to the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § stay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stay" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stay</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hold" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hold_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hold (ship)">hold</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The lower part of the interior of a ship's <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>, especially when considered as storage space, as for cargo. In earlier use, the term referred to all interior spaces below the <span title="See entry on this page at § orlop deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#orlop_deck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">orlop deck</a></span>; in later merchant vessels it extended up through the decks to the underside of the <span title="See entry on this page at § weather deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#weather_deck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">weather deck</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="holiday" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">holiday</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A gap in the coverage of newly applied paint, slush, tar, or another preservative.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="holystone" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Holystone" title="Holystone">holystone</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A chunk of <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> used to scrub a ship's <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">decks</span></a>. The name comes from both the kneeling position sailors adopt to scrub the deck (reminiscent of genuflection for prayer), and the stone itself (which resembled a Bible in shape and size).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="home_port" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Home_port" title="Home port">home port</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <span title="See entry on this page at § port" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#port" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">port</a></span> at which a vessel is based. Often confused with the ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <span title="See entry on this page at § port of registry" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#port_of_registry" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">port of registry</a></span>, which is the port listed in the vessel<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s registration documents and lettered on her <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> but which may differ from her home port. In the <a href="#cruise_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § cruise ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cruise ship</span></a> industry, the term "home port" is often incorrectly used to refer to a ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s port of departure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="homeward_bounder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">homeward bounder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A slang term for a sail repair, especially one done with large herringbone stitches.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hoop" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hoop</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Wooden or metal hoops used to secure the <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span> to the <a href="/wiki/Topmast" title="Topmast">topmast</a> so it can be speedily raised or lowered.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="horn" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">horn</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sound signal that uses electricity or compressed air to vibrate a disc diaphragm.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hornpipe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hornpipe" title="Hornpipe">hornpipe</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of dance.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="horns" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">horns</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Shaped ends to the <a href="#chock"><span title="See entry on this page at § chock" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">chocks</span></a> where the main <a href="#horse"><span title="See entry on this page at § horse" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">horse</span></a> is bolted.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="horn_timber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">horn timber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> structural member of the hull sloping up and backwards from the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> to support the <a href="#counter"><span title="See entry on this page at § counter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">counter</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="horse" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">horse</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A metal bar (sometimes a shaped aluminium extrusion), running <a href="#athwartships"><span title="See entry on this page at § athwartships" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">athwartships</span></a>, to which a <span title="See entry on this page at § sheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheet</a></span> is attached with a <a href="/wiki/Traveller_(nautical_fitting)" title="Traveller (nautical fitting)">traveller</a> that slides along the horse or is adjusted to be fixed in one position on it. Commonly used for a <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsheet</a></span>, but also seen with some <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a>s, particularly a <span title="See entry on this page at § staysail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#staysail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">staysail</a></span> fitted with a <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Sand lying mid-channel.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;(v.) To move or adjust a sail by manual force (i.e. directly with the hands) rather than by using running <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;(v.) A term used since the end of the 17th century for the action of a strong, favorable current on a sailing vessel allowing her to make good progress despite insufficient wind for sailing; the vessel is considered to be <i>horsed</i> by the current, riding it in the way a human rides a horse.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="horse_latitudes" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Horse_latitudes" title="Horse latitudes">horse latitudes</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a> between <a href="/wiki/30th_parallel_north" title="30th parallel north">30</a> and <a href="/wiki/35th_parallel_north" title="35th parallel north">35</a> degrees in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> and between <a href="/wiki/30th_parallel_south" title="30th parallel south">30</a> and <a href="/wiki/35th_parallel_south" title="35th parallel south">35</a> degrees in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> in which weather patterns often result in sailing vessels being becalmed in mid-ocean.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hospital_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hospital_ship" title="Hospital ship">hospital ship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ship designated and equipped to serve primarily as a floating medical healthcare facility or hospital, usually operated by military forces such as navies for use in or near war zones, or for the support of disaster relief and other humanitarian operations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hounds" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hounds</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Attachments of <span title="See entry on this page at § stay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stay" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stays</a></span> to <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hotel_load" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hotel load</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="/wiki/Electrical_load" title="Electrical load">electrical load</a> for all non-propulsion systems on a ship, including lighting, climate control, and services used by the crew and passengers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hove_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hove_to" class="mw-redirect" title="Hove to">hove to</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In a sailing vessel, stopping her by backing some of the sails and lashing the <a href="#helm"><span title="See entry on this page at § helm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">helm</span></a> to <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a>. In a <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> <span title="See entry on this page at § sloop" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sloop" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sloop</a></span>, this involves backing the <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a> and allowing the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span> to fill somewhat (the precise arrangement varies from one vessel to another). The vessel will gradually drift to leeward, with the speed of the drift depending on the vessel's design.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In a powered vessel, stopping her by stopping her engines.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;See <a href="#heave_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § Heave to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Heave to</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hoveller" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hoveller</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Someone who does <span title="See entry on this page at § salvage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#salvage" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">salvage</a></span> work, such as that done by <a href="/wiki/Deal,_Kent#Boatmen" title="Deal, Kent">Deal boatmen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195196_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195196-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An additional crewman who assists getting a vessel in and out of harbour. (See also <a href="#huffler"><span title="See entry on this page at § huffler" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">huffler</span></a>, but regional usage of these words varies substantially, with strongly held views on the differences)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStuckey200097_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStuckey200097-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195196_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195196-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="how&#39;s_your_head?" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">how's your head?</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A question to the helmsman to report the course the vessel is on at that moment. This may differ from the course to steer that has been ordered.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hoy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hoy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#cutter"><span title="See entry on this page at § cutter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cutter</span></a>-rigged craft, having a pole masted with a boomless <a href="#gaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a> <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span> and a steeved-up <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a>. Hoys were square, swim headed Thames estuary barges of 40 to 150 tons burthen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195155_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195155-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a> making regular passages on a fixed route with mixed third-party cargoes. Also <i>passage barge</i> or <i>goods barge</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195155_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195155-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hufflers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">hufflers</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Additional crew taken on to enter harbour or navigate in confined waters, particularly applying to Thames barges. See also <a href="#hoveller"><span title="See entry on this page at § hoveller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hoveller</span></a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195196_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195196-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hulk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hulk_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hulk (ship)">hulk</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A ship, often an old ship or one that has become obsolete or uneconomical to operate, that has had its rigging or internal equipment removed and is incapable of going to sea, but that is still <a href="#afloat"><span title="See entry on this page at § afloat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">afloat</span></a> and continues to serve a useful function, such as providing living, office, training, storage, or prison space.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(v.) To convert a ship into a hulk.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A ship that has been <a href="/wiki/Ship_naming_and_launching" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship naming and launching">launched</a> but not completed.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;An abandoned <span title="See entry on this page at § shipwreck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shipwreck" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">wreck</a></span> or shell of a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hull" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hull_(watercraft)" title="Hull (watercraft)">hull</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The shell and framework of the basic flotation-oriented part of a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hull-down" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hull-down" title="Hull-down">hull-down</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Of a vessel when only her upper parts (e.g., <a href="#funnel"><span title="See entry on this page at § funnel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">funnel</span></a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>s, and <span title="See entry on this page at § superstructure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#superstructure" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">superstructure</a></span>) are visible on the horizon but her <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> remains below the horizon. (Compare with "<a href="#hull-up"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull-up" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull-up</span></a>.")</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hull_speed" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hull_speed" title="Hull speed">hull speed</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The maximum efficient speed of a displacement-hulled vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hull-up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hull-down" title="Hull-down">hull-up</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Of a vessel when her <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> as well as her upper parts (e.g., <a href="#funnel"><span title="See entry on this page at § funnel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">funnel</span></a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>s, and <span title="See entry on this page at § superstructure" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#superstructure" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">superstructure</a></span>) are visible on the horizon. (Compare with "<a href="#hull-down"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull-down" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull-down</span></a>.")</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydrofoil" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hydrofoil" title="Hydrofoil">hydrofoil</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A boat with wing-like foils mounted on struts below the hull, lifting the hull entirely out of the water at speed and therefore greatly reducing water resistance.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="hydroplane" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Hydroplane_(boat)" title="Hydroplane (boat)">hydroplane</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">also <b>hydro</b> or <b>thunderboat</b></span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A fast motorboat with a <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> shaped so that at speed <span title="See entry on this page at § Plane" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#Plane" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">planing</a></span> forces support the boat′s weight, rather than simple <a href="#buoyancy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoyancy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoyancy</span></a>. A hydroplane moving at speed thus relies on the water for <a href="/wiki/Lift_(force)" title="Lift (force)">lift</a> instead of buoyancy.</dd>
</dl>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="icebreaker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">icebreaker</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A special-purpose ship or boat designed to move and navigate through ice-covered waters.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="icing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Icing_(nautical)" title="Icing (nautical)">icing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A serious hazard where cold temperatures (below about −10°C) combined with high wind speed (typically force 8 or above on the <a href="/wiki/Beaufort_scale" title="Beaufort scale">Beaufort scale</a>) result in spray blown off the sea freezing immediately upon contact with the ship. If the weight of the ice becomes too great, the ship will become top-heavy and <a href="/wiki/Capsize" class="mw-redirect" title="Capsize">capsize</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="idlers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">idlers</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Members of a <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s company" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_company" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's company</a></span> not required to serve watches. In general, these were specialist tradesmen such as the carpenter and the sailmaker.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="in_ballast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">in ballast</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>in ballast condition</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">(of a vessel) Having only <a href="#ballast"><span title="See entry on this page at § ballast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ballast</span></a>, and no cargo, as a load.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="in_irons" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">in irons</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>in <a href="/wiki/Stays_(nautical)" title="Stays (nautical)">stays</a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">When a sailing vessel has lost its forward momentum while heading into the wind, rendering it unable to steer.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="in_ordinary" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/In_ordinary" title="In ordinary">in ordinary</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An 18th- and 19th-century term originally used to refer to a naval vessel that is out of service for repair or maintenance, later coming to mean naval ships in reserve with no more than a caretaker crew.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="in-water_survey" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/In-water_survey" title="In-water survey">in-water survey</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A method of surveying the underwater parts of a ship while it is still afloat instead of having to <a href="#drydock"><span title="See entry on this page at § drydock" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">drydock</span></a> it for examination of these areas as was conventionally done.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="in_way_of" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">in way of</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In the vicinity of; in the area of.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inboard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Situated within a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Situated within a vessel and positioned close (or closer relative to another object) to her <a href="#centerline"><span title="See entry on this page at § centerline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">centerline</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Situated outside a vessel but nearer to her <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>, e.g. "The larger boat was tied up alongside the ship inboard of the smaller boat."</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;Nearer the pier or shore, e.g. "The tanker and cargo ship were tied up at the pier alongside one another with the tanker inboard of the cargo ship."</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inboard_motor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Inboard_motor" title="Inboard motor">inboard motor</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An engine mounted within the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> of a vessel, usually driving a fixed <span title="See entry on this page at § propeller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#propeller" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">propeller</a></span> by a shaft protruding through the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>. Generally used on larger vessels. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § sterndrive" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sterndrive" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sterndrive</a></span></i> and <i><span title="See entry on this page at § outboard motor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#outboard_motor" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">outboard motor</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inboard-outboard_drive_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inboard-outboard drive system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><span title="See entry on this page at § sterndrive" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sterndrive" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sterndrive</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inglefield_clip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Inglefield_clip" title="Inglefield clip">Inglefield clip</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of clip for attaching a flag to a flag <a href="#halyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § halyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">halyard</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="inshore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">inshore</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Near (especially in sight of) or toward the shore.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(of a wind) Blowing from the sea to the land.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="interloper" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">interloper</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A term used by the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> in the seventeenth century for a merchant ship operating in violation of the company's monopoly over trade between England (later the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>) and ports east of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>. If caught, an "interloper" and her cargo could be confiscated, and her crew faced harsh penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-threedecksshiproles_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-threedecksshiproles-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="iron_mike" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Iron Mike</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A slang term for autopilot.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="iron_topsail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">iron topsail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An auxiliary motor on a <span title="See entry on this page at § schooner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#schooner" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">schooner</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="iron_wind" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">iron wind</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">What sailors call inboard engines.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ironclad" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ironclad_warship" title="Ironclad warship">ironclad</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A steam-propelled warship protected by iron or steel armor plates of the period from 1859 until the 1890s (when the term "ironclad" fell out of use).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="island" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">island</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="/wiki/Superstructure" title="Superstructure">superstructure</a> of an <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> that extends above the <a href="/wiki/Flight_deck" title="Flight deck">flight deck</a>. A carrier that lacks one is said to be <a href="#flush_deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § flush deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flush-decked</span></a>.</dd>
</dl>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1098327943"/>
