<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="jack" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jack</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § sailor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sailor" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sailor</a></span>. Also <b>jack tar</b> or just <b>tar</b>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Jack_(flag)" title="Jack (flag)">jack (flag)</a>) A national or other official flag flown on a short <a href="#jackstaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § jackstaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jackstaff</span></a> at the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of a vessel indicating nationality or subordination to a navy or other particular seagoing service or to a government department or subnational government (such as a state or province), or to indicate membership in a <span title="See entry on this page at § yacht club" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yacht_club" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yacht club</a></span>. Typically, crew members spoke of the jack as if it were a member of the crew. A jack contrasts with an <a href="#ensign"><span title="See entry on this page at § ensign" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ensign</span></a>, which is a flag with a generally similar purpose flown from the vessel′s <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>. Typically, vessels fly a jack while in port and an ensign while at sea (in daylight hours).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Informally, any flag flown by a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jackass-barque" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jackass-barque" title="Jackass-barque">jackass-barque</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>jackass bark</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing ship with three or more <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span>, of which the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a> is <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> and the main is partially square-rigged (<span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span>, <span title="See entry on this page at § topgallant" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topgallant" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topgallant</a></span>, etc.) and partially <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> (course). The <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzen mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzen_mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzen mast</a></span> is fore-and-aft-rigged.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jack_dusty" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jack dusty</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A naval stores clerk.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jack_tar" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jack_tar" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack tar">jack tar</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailor dressed in "square rig" with square collar. Formerly with a tarred pigtail.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jackline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jackline" title="Jackline">jackline</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="jackstay"></span><span class="anchor" id="jack_stay"></span>
<dd class="glossary">On a <span title="See entry on this page at § yacht" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yacht" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yacht</a></span>, a deck lifeline of rope or (preferably) flat tape, running fore and aft, to which the crew can clip their harnesses for safety. Sometimes called a <a href="#jackstay"><span title="See entry on this page at § jackstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jackstay</span></a>, though this is a misnomer as a jackline is a <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> rather than a <span title="See entry on this page at § stay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stay" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stay</a></span>. The line must be very strong to take the weight of all crew clipped to it.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jackstaff" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jackstaff" title="Jackstaff">jackstaff</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small vertical pole on the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> of a vessel upon which is flown its flag, or <a href="#jack"><span title="See entry on this page at § jack" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jack</span></a>. The jackstaff was introduced in the 18th century.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jackstay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jackstay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A rope, bar, or <a href="#batten"><span title="See entry on this page at § batten" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">batten</span></a> running along a ship's <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yard</a></span>, to which is attached the head of a square sail.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <span title="See entry on this page at § stay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stay" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stay</a></span> for racing or cruising vessels used to steady the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> against the strain of the <a href="#gaff"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#cable"><span title="See entry on this page at § cable" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cable</span></a> between two ships or from a ship to a fixed point that supports a load during transfer of personnel or materiel along the cable.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;On a <span title="See entry on this page at § yacht" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yacht" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yacht</a></span>, a deck lifeline of rope or (preferably) flat tape may be called a jackstay, though this is a misnomer as a jackstay is a stay rather than a line.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jacob&#39;s_ladder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jacob%27s_ladder_(nautical)" title="Jacob&#39;s ladder (nautical)">Jacob's ladder</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>Jacobs ladder</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A flexible hanging <a href="/wiki/Ladder" title="Ladder">ladder</a> consisting of vertical ropes or chains supporting horizontal rungs, used to allow access over the side of a ship, either to transfer between the ship and another vessel alongside it or to perform maintenance tasks along the side of the ship. Sometimes mistakenly referred to as a <span title="See entry on this page at § pilot ladder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#pilot_ladder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">pilot ladder</a></span>, which differs from a Jacob′s ladder in its use of spreaders and in terms of specific regulations governing step size and step spacing.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A vertical ladder from the <a href="/wiki/Ratlines" title="Ratlines">ratlines</a> found on <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged</a></span> ships, used to get around the <span title="See entry on this page at § top" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#top" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">top</a></span> while climbing between the lower mast and the <a href="/wiki/Topmast" title="Topmast">topmast</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jetty" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jetty</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A man-made pier in a marina or open water, typically made of wood or rocks and rising several feet above high tide in order to create a breakwater, shelter, channel, erosion control, or other function.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jetsam" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Flotsam_and_jetsam" class="mw-redirect" title="Flotsam and jetsam">jetsam</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Floating debris ejected from a ship. See also <i><a href="#flotsam"><span title="See entry on this page at § flotsam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flotsam</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jib" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jib" title="Jib">jib</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A triangular <a href="#headsail"><span title="See entry on this page at § headsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">headsail</span></a> at the front of a sailing vessel. The <span title="See entry on this page at § tack" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tack" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tack</a></span> is attached to the <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> or to a <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a>. May be the only headsail, or one of several&#160;&#8211;&#32;in which case the jib is set forward of the fore staysail. A large jib that overlaps the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainmast</a></span> is called a <a href="#genoa"><span title="See entry on this page at § genoa" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">genoa</span></a> or genny.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jib_top" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jib top</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A high-clewed overlapping headsail for beam reaching in medium to strong winds<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jibboom" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jibboom</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> used to extend the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jibe" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jibe</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#gybe"><span title="See entry on this page at § gybe" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gybe</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jibe-ho" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jibe-ho</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#gybe-oh"><span title="See entry on this page at § gybe-oh" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gybe-oh</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jigger-mast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jigger-mast</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The fourth <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> on a ship, or the aftmost mast where it is smallest on vessels of less than four masts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110_69-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955110-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="joggle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">joggle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A slender, triangular recess cut into the <a href="/wiki/Faying" title="Faying">faying</a> surface of a frame or steamed timber to fit over the land of <a href="#clinker-built"><span title="See entry on this page at § clinker-built" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clinker</span></a> planking, or cut into the faying edge of a plank or rebate to avoid feather ends on a <span title="See entry on this page at § strake" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#strake" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">strake</a></span> of planking. The feather end is cut off to produce a <span title="See entry on this page at § nib" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#nib" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">nib</a></span>. The joggle and nib in this case is made wide enough to allow a <a href="#caulking"><span title="See entry on this page at § caulking" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">caulking</span></a> iron to enter the seam.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jollies" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jollies</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Traditional Royal Navy nickname for the Royal Marines.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jolly_boat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">jolly boat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_boat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's boat</a></span> used to ferry crew and stores.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jonah" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jonah#Cultural_influence" title="Jonah">Jonah</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A person (either a sailor or a passenger) who carries a jinx, one whose presence on board brings bad luck and endangers the ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jonah&#39;s_lift" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Jonah's lift</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The throwing overboard of a man considered to be a <a href="#jonah,"><span title="See entry on this page at § Jonah," class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Jonah,</span></a> almost always in the dark of night.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="junk" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">junk</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Old cordage past its useful service life as <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lines</span></a> aboard a ship. The strands of old junk were teased apart in a process known as "picking <span title="See entry on this page at § oakum" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#oakum" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">oakum</a></span>".</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A sailing ship of classic Chinese design with characteristic full <a href="#batten"><span title="See entry on this page at § batten" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">batten</span></a> sails that span the masts usually on unstayed rigs.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="jury_rig" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Jury_rig" class="mw-redirect" title="Jury rig">jury rig</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Both the act of <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span> a temporary <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> and/or <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sails</a></span> and the name of the resulting rig. A jury rig would be built at sea when the original rig was damaged, and then used to sail to a harbor or other safe place for permanent repairs. Also used as a general term for a temporary repair, hence "jury rudder", "jury tiller", etc.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMayne2000158_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayne2000158-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="kaep" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Kaep" title="Kaep">kaep</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <a href="/wiki/Proa" title="Proa">proa</a> native to <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="k_bo_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/w/index.php?title=K_BO_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="K BO Line (page does not exist)">K BO Line</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A line or mark on the aft end of a ship indicating the true centerline of the transom.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kedge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Kedge_anchor#Kedging" class="mw-redirect" title="Kedge anchor">kedge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A technique for moving or turning a ship by using a relatively light <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>, also known as a <i>kedge</i>. The kedge anchor may be dropped while in motion to create a pivot and thus perform a sharp turn. It may also be carried away from the ship in a smaller boat, dropped, and then weighed, pulling the ship forward.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="keel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The principal central longitudinal structural member of a <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a>, positioned at or close to the lowest point of the hull. Where the keel protrudes below the surface of the hull, it provides hydrodynamic resistance to the lateral forces that give rise to <a href="#leeway"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeway</span></a>. A <a href="#ballast"><span title="See entry on this page at § ballast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ballast</span></a> keel of (typically) lead or cast iron may be fastened underneath the structural keel in sailing vessels to provide stability and usually providing additional hydrodynamic resistance effects.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> See also <i><a href="#bilge_keel"><span title="See entry on this page at § bilge keel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bilge keel</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="keelhauling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Keelhauling" title="Keelhauling">keelhauling</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of maritime punishment by which one is dragged under the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> of a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kellet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">kellet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#anchor_sentinel"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor sentinel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor sentinel</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="keelson" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Kelson" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelson">keelson</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>kelson</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A baulk of timber or steel girder immediately above the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> that forms the backbone of a wooden ship. Chine keelson of more modest proportions are fitted at the junction of the floors and frames.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kentledge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Kentledge" title="Kentledge">kentledge</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Weights, usually <a href="/wiki/Pig_iron" title="Pig iron">pig iron</a>, used as permanent, high-density <a href="#ballast"><span title="See entry on this page at § ballast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ballast</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ketch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ketch" title="Ketch">ketch</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A two-masted <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft-rigged</span></a> sailboat with the aft mast (the <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzen" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzen</a></span>) mounted (<span title="See entry on this page at § stepped" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stepped" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stepped</a></span>) <a href="#afore"><span title="See entry on this page at § afore" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">afore</span></a> the <span title="See entry on this page at § rudder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rudder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rudder</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="killick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">killick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small <a href="#anchor"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor</span></a>. A fouled killick is the substantive badge of non-commissioned officers in the Royal Navy. Seamen promoted to the first step in the promotion ladder are called <i>killick</i>. The badge signifies that the wearer is an <a href="#able_seaman"><span title="See entry on this page at § able seaman" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">able seaman</span></a> skilled to cope with the awkward job of dealing with a fouled anchor.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kicking_strap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">kicking strap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A rope, tackle, or hydraulic ram running from the mast at or just above deck level to a point partway along the <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> of a yacht's <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzen" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzen</a></span>. Its function is to pull the boom down, flattening the sail in strong winds, reducing twist, and preventing the boom from kicking up when running.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">chain</span></a> rigged from <span title="See entry on this page at § rudder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rudder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rudder</a></span> to <span title="See entry on this page at § quarter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#quarter" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">quarter</a></span> that is tight at anchor, stopping the rudder from kicking and reducing pressure on its <a href="#gudgeon"><span title="See entry on this page at § gudgeon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gudgeons</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="king_plank" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">king plank</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="#centerline"><span title="See entry on this page at § centerline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">centerline</span></a> plank of a laid deck. Its sides are often recessed, or nibbed, to take the ends of their parallel curved deck planks.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="king_post" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">king post</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(on an American wooden-hulled steamboat): a type of <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § stanchion" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stanchion" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stanchion</a></span> located along the vessel's <a href="#centerline"><span title="See entry on this page at § centerline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">centerline</span></a> from which heavy chains, later cables, were suspended to support the weight of the <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> and provide stiffening, in much the same manner as the cables on a <a href="/wiki/Suspension_bridge" title="Suspension bridge">suspension bridge</a>; usually used in conjunction with a <a href="#hog_frame"><span title="See entry on this page at § hog frame" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hog frame</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(on a cargo ship): a strong vertical post from which a <a href="#derrick"><span title="See entry on this page at § derrick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">derrick</span></a> or <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> is suspended.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kingston_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Kingston_valve" title="Kingston valve">Kingston valve</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of <span title="See entry on this page at § seacock" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#seacock" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">seacock</a></span> designed so that the water pressure from the sea keeps it closed under normal operating conditions, but can be opened from the inside of the ship, allowing seawater to enter internal fuel, water, or <a href="#ballast_tank"><span title="See entry on this page at § ballast tank" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ballast tanks</span></a>. Kingston valves can be opened to <span title="See entry on this page at § scuttling" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#scuttling" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">scuttle</a></span> a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kissing_the_gunner&#39;s_daughter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Cat_o%27_nine_tails#Boys&#39;_punishment" title="Cat o&#39; nine tails">kissing the gunner's daughter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Bending over the barrel of a gun for punitive beating with a cane or <a href="#cat_o&#39;_nine_tails"><span title="See entry on this page at § cat o&#39; nine tails" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cat o' nine tails</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kitchen_rudder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Kitchen_rudder" title="Kitchen rudder">kitchen rudder</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A hinged cowling around a fixed <span title="See entry on this page at § propeller" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#propeller" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">propeller</a></span>, allowing the drive to be directed to the side or forwards in order to manoeuvre the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="kite" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">kite</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <span title="See entry on this page at § spinnaker" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spinnaker" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spinnaker</a></span> (<i>q.v.</i>).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="knee" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">knee</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Connects two parts roughly at right angles, e.g. deck <a href="#beam"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beams</span></a> to <a href="#frame"><span title="See entry on this page at § frame" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">frames</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A vertical rubber fender used on <span title="See entry on this page at § pushboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#pushboat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">pushboats</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § pier" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#pier" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">piers</a></span>, sometimes shaped like a human leg bent slightly at the knee.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="knighthead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">knighthead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A mitred backing timber that extends the after line of the <span title="See entry on this page at § rabbet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rabbet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rabbet</a></span> in the <span title="See entry on this page at § stem" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stem" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stem</a></span> to give extra support to the ends of the planks and the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href="#bollard"><span title="See entry on this page at § bollard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bollard</span></a> or <a href="#bitt"><span title="See entry on this page at § bitt" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bitt</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;Either of two timbers rising from the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> of a sailing ship and supporting the inner end of the bowsprit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="knock" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">knock</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#header"><span title="See entry on this page at § header" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">header</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="knockdown" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">knockdown</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The condition of a sailboat being pushed abruptly over on its side, i.e. to horizontal or "on its <a href="#beam-end"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam-end" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beam-ends</span></a>", with the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span> parallel to the water surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="knot" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knot</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A unit of speed equivalent to 1 nautical mile (1.8520&#160;km; 1.1508&#160;mi) per hour. Originally the speed of a moving vessel was measured by paying out a line from the <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span>; the line was tied into a knot every 47&#160;feet 3&#160;inches (14.40&#160;m), and the number of knots paid out in 30 seconds gave the speed through the water in nautical miles per hour. Sometimes "knots" is mistakenly stated as "knots per hour", but the latter is a measure of acceleration (i.e. "nautical miles per hour per hour") rather than of speed. Both vessel speed and wind speed are commonly reported in knots.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="know_the_ropes" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">know the ropes</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailor who <i>knows the ropes</i> can identify all the many ropes used in working a sailing vessel. On a square rigged ship, there would typically be more than 130 named ropes in the running rigging which are made fast at deck level – the majority of these are duplicated on both the port and starboard sides, so doubling that count.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1946280–288_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1946280–288-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In order to know the ropes, a sailor must first <i><a href="#learn_the_ropes"><span title="See entry on this page at § learn the ropes" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">learn the ropes</span></a></i>. There were conventions with the positioning of all the many ropes <a href="#belay"><span title="See entry on this page at § belay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">belay</span></a>ed at deck level on a square-rigged ship, so a newly signed-on hand would quickly know where to find a particular rope on a strange ship.</dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(A-L)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="lace" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lace</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To attach a <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> to a <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> by passing a rope through eyelet holes and around the spar or its <a href="#jackstay"><span title="See entry on this page at § jackstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">jackstay</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ladder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ladder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">On board a ship, all "stairs" are called ladders, except for literal staircases aboard passenger ships. Most "stairs" on a ship are extremely narrow and nearly vertical, hence the name.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lagan" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lagan</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Cargo that has been thrown overboard and buoyed so it can be found later, sunk to the seabed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="laid_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">laid up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To be placed in <span title="See entry on this page at § reserve fleet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#reserve_fleet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">reserve</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § mothball" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mothball" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mothballed</a></span>. The latter usage in modern times refers to a specific set of procedures used by the United States Navy to preserve ships in good condition.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="laker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">laker</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> slang for a vessel that spends all of her time on any of the five Great Lakes.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lakeshoring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lakeshoring</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>lakeshoring trade</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> term for the general cargo and passenger trade between settlements on the Great Lakes during the 19th and early 20th centuries. Lakeshoring usually was conducted by <span title="See entry on this page at § schooner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#schooner" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">schooners</a></span> of 50 to 60 feet (15 to 18&#160;m) in length, sometimes referred to as <i>lakeshoring schooners</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="land_lubber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">land lubber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A person unfamiliar with being on the sea.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="landmark" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">landmark</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An object ashore that is visible from sea and sufficiently distinct such that it is marked on nautical charts for the purpose of fixing position while at sea.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="landsman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Landsman_(rank)" title="Landsman (rank)">landsman</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A military rank for a naval recruit, used in the United Kingdom in the 18th century and the first half of the 19th century and in the United States in the 19th and early 20th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="langrage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Langrage" class="mw-redirect" title="Langrage">langrage</a></dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="langridge" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">langridge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Another name for <a href="#canister_shot"><span title="See entry on this page at § canister shot" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">canister shot</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Solid shot suitable for damaging rigging.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lang&#39;s_lay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lang's lay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rope in which the lay of the strands is on the same hand as the lay of the constituents of the strands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lanyard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lanyard" title="Lanyard">lanyard</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A light <span title="See entry on this page at § rope" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rope" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rope</a></span> that suspends a small item to prevent loss or is used to operate something by pulling on it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="larboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Port_(nautical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Port (nautical)">larboard</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An obsolete term for the left side of a ship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Derived from "lay-board", which provided access between a ship and a <span title="See entry on this page at § quay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#quay" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">quay</a></span> when ships normally docked with the left side to the wharf. Later replaced by "port side" or "<span title="See entry on this page at § port" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#port" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">port</a></span>", to avoid confusion with <span title="See entry on this page at § starboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#starboard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">starboard</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="large" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">large</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#by_and_large"><span title="See entry on this page at § by and large" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">by and large</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lateen_sail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lateen_sail" class="mw-redirect" title="Lateen sail">lateen sail</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="Latin-rig"></span><span class="anchor" id="Latin_rig"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>Latin-rig</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A triangular, sometimes quadrilateral, <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> set on a long <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yard</a></span> mounted at an angle to the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lateral_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lateral system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A system of <a href="#aid_to_navigation"><span title="See entry on this page at § aid to navigation" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aids to navigation</span></a> in which characteristics of buoys and beacons indicate the sides of the channel or route relative to a conventional direction of buoyage (usually upstream).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lattice_mast" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lattice_mast" title="Lattice mast">lattice mast</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b><a href="#cage_mast"><span title="See entry on this page at § cage mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cage mast</span></a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A type of observation mast constructed with a <a href="/wiki/Hyperboloid_structure" title="Hyperboloid structure">hyperboloid structure</a> using an array of thin columns at angles, crossing each other in a double-helical spiral configuration. Lattice masts were most common aboard major United States Navy warships in the early 20th century, particularly on <a href="#dreadnought"><span title="See entry on this page at § dreadnought" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dreadnought</span></a> <a href="#battleship"><span title="See entry on this page at § battleship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battleships</span></a> and <a href="#armored_cruiser"><span title="See entry on this page at § armored cruiser" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">armored cruisers</span></a>; they were largely replaced by <span title="See entry on this page at § tripod mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tripod_mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tripod masts</a></span> during the 1920s and 1930s.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="launch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">launch</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The largest <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s boat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_boat" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's boat</a></span> carried by a warship – usually an open boat and, in more recent times, fitted with an engine. Historically, fitted both to be rowed or sailed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In modern usage, a large <a href="/wiki/Motorboat" title="Motorboat">motorboat</a>; e.g. a <a href="#harbourmaster"><span title="See entry on this page at § harbourmaster" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">harbourmaster</span></a>'s launch.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;An elegant power boat of traditional character with a <a href="#displacement_hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § displacement hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">displacement hull</span></a>; e.g. a <span title="See entry on this page at § slipper launch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#slipper_launch" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">slipper launch</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-PBO_11-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBO-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Ship_naming_and_launching" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship naming and launching">To dispatch a newly built ship</a> down a <span title="See entry on this page at § slipway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#slipway" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">slipway</a></span>, usually with ceremony, prior to <a href="#fitting-out"><span title="See entry on this page at § fitting-out" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fitting-out</span></a> and <a href="/wiki/Ship_commissioning" title="Ship commissioning">commissioning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">5.&#160;&#160;To put into the water any boat that is stored or temporarily kept out of the water; e.g. "launch the <a href="#lifeboat"><span title="See entry on this page at § lifeboat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lifeboat</span></a>" or "launch a <a href="#dinghy"><span title="See entry on this page at § dinghy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dinghy</span></a>".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;To come and go, used in giving orders to the <a href="#crew"><span title="See entry on this page at § crew" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crew</span></a>, e.g. "lay forward" or "lay aloft", respectively indicating that the crew should move to the forward part of the ship or take up positions aloft.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;To direct the <a href="#course"><span title="See entry on this page at § course" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">course</span></a> of a vessel.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;(v) To twist the strands of a <span title="See entry on this page at § rope" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rope" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rope</a></span> together. (n) The direction of twist in cordage made from twisted strands</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;To travel in a direction which will reach or pass just upwind of a mark, buoy, or harbor, e.g. "We will lay the mark".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lay_day" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lay day</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An unexpected delay time during a voyage often spent at anchor or in a harbor. It is usually caused by bad weather, equipment failure, or needed maintenance.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lay_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lay to</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="#heave_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § heave to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">heave to</span></a></span></p>
To bring a vessel into the wind and hold her stationary. A vessel doing this is said to be <i>laying to</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="laying_down" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">laying down</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Keel-laying" class="mw-redirect" title="Keel-laying">Laying</a> the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a> of a ship in a <span title="See entry on this page at § shipyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shipyard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shipyard</a></span>, and thereby beginning her construction. The age of a ship is often indicated by giving the date it was <i>laid down</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="laytime" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Laytime" title="Laytime">laytime</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The amount of time stipulated in a <span title="See entry on this page at § voyage charter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#voyage_charter" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">voyage charter</a></span> for a vessel to be loaded or unloaded. If a vessel is loaded or unloaded in less than the laytime, the shipowner may be required to pay <a href="#despatch"><span title="See entry on this page at § despatch" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">despatch</span></a> to the charter party. If the loading or unloading takes longer than the laytime, the charter party may be required to pay <a href="#demurrage"><span title="See entry on this page at § demurrage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">demurrage</span></a> to the shipowner.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lazaret" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lazaret</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="lazarette"></span><span class="anchor" id="lazaretto"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>lazarette</b> or <b>lazaretto</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A small stowage locker at the <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> end of a boat.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A ship or building used for the quarantine of sick patients.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;An area on some merchant ships where provisions are stored.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;In modern shipbuilding and on powerboats of all sizes, the location of the steering gear equipment for the vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lazy_jacks" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lazy_jack" title="Lazy jack">lazy jacks</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="lazyjacks"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>lazyjacks</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A network of <a href="#cordage"><span title="See entry on this page at § cordage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cordage</span></a> rigged to a point on the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> and to a series of points on either side of the <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> that cradles and guides the sail onto the boom when the sail is lowered.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lazy_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lazy line</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>slime line</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A line used for stern-to mooring attached to a floating pontoon or harbor wall which leads back to a seabed mooring.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leach" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leach</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>leech</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">after</span></a> edge of a sail.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A plummet or mass of lead attached to a line, used in <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sounding</a></span> depth at sea.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In former usage, to estimate velocity in <a href="#knot"><span title="See entry on this page at § knot" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">knots</span></a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The path or route of a line (cordage).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">4.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="/wiki/Lead_(sea_ice)" title="Lead (sea ice)">Lead (sea ice)</a></i>: Large fracture in sea ice creating a navigable waterway.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leadline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leadline</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="sounding_line"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>sounding line</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">An instrument used in navigation to <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">measure water depth</a></span>; the <a href="#line"><span title="See entry on this page at § line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line</span></a> attached to a <a href="#lead"><span title="See entry on this page at § lead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lead</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leadsman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leadsman</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailor who takes <span title="See entry on this page at § sounding" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sounding" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">soundings</a></span> with a <a href="#lead"><span title="See entry on this page at § lead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lead</span></a>, measuring the depth of the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="league" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/League_(unit)" title="League (unit)">league</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A unit of length used to measure distances, normally equal to three <span title="See entry on this page at § nautical mile" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#nautical_mile" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">nautical miles</a></span>, but varies by nationality.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="learn_the_ropes" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">learn the ropes</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To be trained in the identification and proper use of the many various <span title="See entry on this page at § rope" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rope" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ropes</a></span> used on a sailing ship. An apprentice sailor, especially on a <span title="See entry on this page at § square rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#square_rig" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">square-rigged ship</a></span>, needs to know which rope of the many that are <a href="#belay"><span title="See entry on this page at § belay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">belayed</span></a> at deck level does which job. A small square sail will have, at a minimum, two <span title="See entry on this page at § sheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheets</a></span>, two <a href="#clewline"><span title="See entry on this page at § clewline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clewlines</span></a>, several <a href="#buntline"><span title="See entry on this page at § buntline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buntlines</span></a>, and two <a href="#brace"><span title="See entry on this page at § brace" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">braces</span></a>, and may also have a <a href="#halyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § halyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">halyard</span></a>. A single <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> may have up to five square sails. To do his job, a sailor must be able to identify each rope from all the many options – and in the dark. <span title="See entry on this page at § slacking" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#slacking" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">Slacking</a></span> or <a href="#hauling"><span title="See entry on this page at § hauling" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hauling</span></a> the wrong one may not only be inefficient but also potentially dangerous. Once proficient in these tasks, a sailor is said to "<a href="#know_the_ropes"><span title="See entry on this page at § know the ropes" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">know the ropes</span></a>".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lee_helm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lee_helm" title="Lee helm">lee helm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The tendency of a sailboat to turn to <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a> in a strong wind when there is no change in the <span title="See entry on this page at § rudder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rudder" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rudder</a></span>'s position. This is the opposite of <span title="See entry on this page at § weather helm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#weather_helm" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">weather helm</a></span> and is the result of a dynamically unbalanced condition. See also <i><a href="#center_of_lateral_resistance"><span title="See entry on this page at § center of lateral resistance" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">center of lateral resistance</span></a></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lee_side" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lee side</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>leeward side</b> or simply <b><a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a></b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The side of a ship that is sheltered from the wind; i.e. the side that is downwind, or in the direction toward which the wind is blowing. Contrast <i><span title="See entry on this page at § weather side" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#weather_side" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">weather side</a></span></i> or <i><span title="See entry on this page at § windward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windward</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lee_shore" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lee_shore" title="Lee shore">lee shore</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A shore downwind of a ship. A ship that cannot sail well to <span title="See entry on this page at § windward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windward</a></span> risks being blown onto a lee shore and <a href="#grounded"><span title="See entry on this page at § grounded" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">grounded</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leeboard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Leeboard" title="Leeboard">leeboard</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large fan-shaped wooden board or fin mounted in pairs on the side of a boat. They can be lowered on the <a href="#lee_side"><span title="See entry on this page at § lee side" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lee side</span></a> of the ship to reduce <a href="#leeway"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeway" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeway</span></a> (similarly to a <a href="#centerboard"><span title="See entry on this page at § centerboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">centerboard</span></a> on a <a href="#dinghy"><span title="See entry on this page at § dinghy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dinghy</span></a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leeboard_irons" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leeboard irons</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The iron bars that run from the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainmast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainmast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainmast</a></span> case to the head of each <a href="#leeboard"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeboard</span></a>, which they support.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leeboard_pendant" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leeboard pendant</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A wire connecting the fan of the <a href="#leeboard"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeboard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeboard</span></a> to a winch on the barges quarter. They control the fall of the leeboard.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leech" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leech</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>leach</b>.</span></p>
