<dd class="glossary">The <a href="#aft"><span title="See entry on this page at § aft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">aft</span></a> or trailing edge of a <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> sail, the <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a> edge of a <span title="See entry on this page at § spinnaker" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spinnaker" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spinnaker</a></span>, or a vertical edge of a square sail. The leech is susceptible to twist, which is controlled by the <a href="#boom_vang"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom vang" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom vang</span></a>, <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsheet</a></span>, and, if rigged with one, the <a href="#gaff_vang"><span title="See entry on this page at § gaff vang" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gaff vang</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lee-oh" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lee-oh</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="hard_alee"></span><span class="anchor" id="hard-a-lee"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>hard alee</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A command to <a href="#come_about"><span title="See entry on this page at § come about" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">come about</span></a> (<span title="See entry on this page at § tack" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tack" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tack</a></span> through the wind) on a sailing boat. The response by the helmsman to indicate the order has been carried out, is "helm's alee"</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leeward" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">leeward</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(pronounced <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/lj/: &#39;l&#39; in &#39;lute&#39;">lj</span><span title="/uː/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">uː</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span></span>/</a></span></span> in nautical use) In the direction toward which the wind is blowing. Contrast <i><span title="See entry on this page at § windward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windward</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leeway" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Leeway" title="Leeway">leeway</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The amount that a ship is blown <a href="#leeward"><span title="See entry on this page at § leeward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">leeward</span></a> by the wind. Also the amount of open free sailing space available to the <a href="#lee_side"><span title="See entry on this page at § lee side" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lee side</span></a> of a vessel before encountering hazards. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § weatherly" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#weatherly" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">weatherly</a></span></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="leg" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">leg</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In navigation, a segment of a <span title="See entry on this page at § voyage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#voyage" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">voyage</a></span> between two waypoints.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="length_between_perpendiculars" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Length_between_perpendiculars" title="Length between perpendiculars">length between perpendiculars</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="p/p"></span><span class="anchor" id="p.p."></span><span class="anchor" id="pp"></span><span class="anchor" id="LPP"></span><span class="anchor" id="LBP"></span><span class="anchor" id="Length_BPP"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>p/p</b>, <b>p.p.</b>, <b>pp</b>, <b>LPP</b>, <b>LBP</b>, or <b>Length BPP</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">The length of a vessel along the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span> from the forward surface of the <span title="See entry on this page at § stem" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stem" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stem</a></span> or main <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> perpendicular member, to the after surface of the <span title="See entry on this page at § sternpost" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sternpost" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sternpost</a></span> or main <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> perpendicular member. The measure generally allows for a reasonable estimate of the vessel<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s carrying capacity, as it excludes the small, often unusable volume contained in her overhanging ends.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="length_overall_(loa)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Length_overall" title="Length overall">length overall</a> (LOA)</dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="LOA"></span>
<dd class="glossary">The maximum length of a vessel<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="#hull"><span title="See entry on this page at § hull" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hull</span></a> measured parallel to the <span title="See entry on this page at § waterline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#waterline" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">waterline</a></span>, usually measured on the hull alone, and including overhanging ends that extend beyond the main <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> and main <span title="See entry on this page at § stern" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#stern" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">stern</a></span> perpendicular members. For sailing vessels, this may exclude the <a href="#bowsprit"><span title="See entry on this page at § bowsprit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bowsprit</span></a> and other fittings added to the hull, but sometimes bowsprits are included.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="let_go_and_haul" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">let go and haul</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An order indicating that the ship is now on the desired course relative to the wind and that the sails should be trimmed (<a href="#haul"><span title="See entry on this page at § haul" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hauled</span></a>) to suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="letter_of_marque_and_reprisal" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Letter_of_marque" title="Letter of marque">letter of marque and reprisal</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="letter_of_marque"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also simply <b>letter of marque</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">An official warrant granted to a <span title="See entry on this page at § privateer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#privateer" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">privateer</a></span> condoning specific acts of <span title="See entry on this page at § piracy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#piracy" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">piracy</a></span> against a specific target as a redress for grievances.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="liberty" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">liberty</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A relatively short period when a sailor is allowed ashore for recreation. See also <i><span title="See entry on this page at § shore leave" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shore_leave" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shore leave</a></span></i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="licensed_ship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">licensed ship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A term used by the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> from the 17th to the 19th centuries for merchant ships not under <a href="#charter"><span title="See entry on this page at § charter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">charter</span></a> to it which it nevertheless permitted under a license issued by the company to trade between England (later the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>) and ports east of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, a trade over which the company otherwise held a strict monopoly. The company placed strict controls on what ports a licensed ship could visit and what kinds of trade it could engage in. A licensed ship that violated these rules became an <a href="#interloper"><span title="See entry on this page at § interloper" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">interloper</span></a> and faced harsh penalties if caught.<sup id="cite_ref-threedecksshiproles_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-threedecksshiproles-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lie_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lie to</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To arrange a ship<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sails</a></span> so that they counteract each other. A ship in this condition or in the process of achieving this condition is said to be <i>lying to</i>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lifebelt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Personal_flotation_device" title="Personal flotation device">lifebelt</a></dfn></dt><span class="anchor" id="lifejacket"></span><span class="anchor" id="life_preserver"></span><span class="anchor" id="lifebuoy"></span><span class="anchor" id="personal_flotation_device"></span>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>lifebuoy</b>, <b>lifejacket</b>, <b>life preserver</b>, and <b>personal flotation device (PFD)</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A portable or wearable device such as a buoyant ring or inflatable jacket designed to keep a person <a href="#afloat"><span title="See entry on this page at § afloat" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">afloat</span></a> in the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lifeboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lifeboat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Lifeboat_(shipboard)" title="Lifeboat (shipboard)">shipboard lifeboat</a>) A small boat kept on board a vessel and used to take crew and passengers to safety in the event of the ship being abandoned.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Lifeboat_(rescue)" title="Lifeboat (rescue)">rescue lifeboat</a>) A small boat usually launched from shore and used to rescue people from the water or from vessels in difficulty.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="liferaft" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lifeboat_(shipboard)" title="Lifeboat (shipboard)">liferaft</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An inflatable, sometimes covered raft used in the event of a vessel being abandoned or in the evacuation of an aircraft after a water landing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lift" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lift</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A rope that supports a spar on a sailing vessel. Examples include the <a href="/wiki/Topping_lift" title="Topping lift">topping lift</a> on the boom of a fore and aft rigged sail, or the lifts on the yard of a square rigged sail, which can adjust the yard to the horizontal or cock-bill the yard to get it out of the way when unloading cargo or alongside another vessel. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMayne2000_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayne2000-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An enabling shift in the direction of the wind that allows a <a href="#close-hauled"><span title="See entry on this page at § close-hauled" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">close-hauled</span></a> sailing ship to <span title="See entry on this page at § point up" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#point_up" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">point up</a></span> from its current <a href="#course"><span title="See entry on this page at § course" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">course</span></a> to a more favorable one. This is the opposite of a <a href="#header"><span title="See entry on this page at § header" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">header</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="light_irons" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">light irons</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Iron bars mounted near the main <span title="See entry on this page at § shroud" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shroud" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shrouds</a></span> that support the navigation lights.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="light_screens" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">light screens</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Boards on which the navigation lights are hooked and which shield the direction that the red or green light shows.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lighter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lighter_(barge)" title="Lighter (barge)">lighter</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A flat-bottomed <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barge</span></a> used to transfer goods and passengers to and from moored ships, traditionally unpowered and moved and steered using "sweeps" (long <span title="See entry on this page at § oar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#oar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">oars</a></span>), with their motive power provided by water currents.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lightering" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lightering" title="Lightering">lightering</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The process of transferring cargo from one vessel to another in order to reduce the <a href="#draft"><span title="See entry on this page at § draft" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">draft</span></a> of the first vessel, typically done to allow a vessel to enter a <span title="See entry on this page at § port" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#port" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">port</a></span> with limited depth or to help free a <a href="#grounded"><span title="See entry on this page at § grounded" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">grounded</span></a> vessel.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lightvessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lightvessel" title="Lightvessel">lightvessel</a></dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>lightship</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">A permanently anchored vessel performing the functions of a <a href="#lighthouse"><span title="See entry on this page at § lighthouse" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lighthouse</span></a>, typically in a location where construction of the latter is impractical. These have largely been replaced by <a href="#buoy"><span title="See entry on this page at § buoy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">buoys</span></a> or, as construction techniques have improved, actual lighthouses.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="limber_hole" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">limber hole</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A channel cut in the underside of a <a href="#frame"><span title="See entry on this page at § frame" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">frame</span></a>, close to the <a href="/wiki/Keel" title="Keel">keel</a>, to allow <a href="#bilge"><span title="See entry on this page at § bilge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bilge</span></a> water to drain away to the pump well, rather than being trapped between each set of frames.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteffy2013_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteffy2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="limber_board" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">limber board</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A part of the ceiling alongside the <a href="#keelson"><span title="See entry on this page at § keelson" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">keelson</span></a>, easily removable for cleaning out the <a href="#limber_hole"><span title="See entry on this page at § limber hole" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">limber holes</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteffy2013_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteffy2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The correct nautical term for the majority of the <a href="#cordage"><span title="See entry on this page at § cordage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cordage</span></a> or "ropes" used on a vessel. An individual line will always have a more specific name (e.g. the <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzen" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzen</a></span> <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsail</a></span> <a href="#halyard"><span title="See entry on this page at § halyard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">halyard</span></a>) that specifies its use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="line_astern" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">line astern</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In naval warfare, a <a href="#line_of_battle"><span title="See entry on this page at § line of battle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">line of battle</span></a> formed behind a <a href="#flagship"><span title="See entry on this page at § flagship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">flagship</span></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="liner" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">liner</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>, a <span title="See entry on this page at § ship-of-the-line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship-of-the-line" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship-of-the-line</a></span>, or a major <span title="See entry on this page at § warship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#warship" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">warship</a></span> capable of taking its place in the main <a href="#line_of_battle"><span title="See entry on this page at § line of battle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">battle line</span></a> of fighting ships.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Any cargo or passenger ship running scheduled service along a specific route with published <span title="See entry on this page at § port of call" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#port_of_call" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ports of call</a></span>, excluding <a href="/wiki/Ferryboat" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferryboat">ferries</a> and other vessels engaged in short-sea trading. When referring to <a href="#cargo_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § cargo ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cargo ships</span></a>, "liner" contrasts with "<span title="See entry on this page at § tramp" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#tramp" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">tramp</a></span>", which refers to a ship engaged in spot-market trade that does not follow a regular schedule or make regular calls at specific ports. When referring to passenger ships, "<span title="See entry on this page at § ocean liner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ocean_liner" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ocean liner</a></span>" refers to ships providing scheduled transportation between regular ports of call, but excludes <a href="#cruise_ship"><span title="See entry on this page at § cruise ship" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cruise ships</span></a>, which voyage for recreational purposes and not primarily as a form of transportation between ports.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="list" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Angle_of_list" title="Angle of list">list</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The degree or angle to which a vessel leans or tilts to one side, on the <span title="See entry on this page at § roll" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#roll" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">roll</a></span> axos, at equilibrium, i.e. with no external forces acting upon it. The term typically refers to a lean caused by flooding or improperly loaded or shifted cargo, as opposed to <a href="#heeling"><span title="See entry on this page at § heeling" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">heeling</span></a>, which is a consequence of external forces. A vessel with such a lean is said to be <i>listing</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Compare with <a href="#loll"><span title="See entry on this page at § loll" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">loll</span></a> </dd>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg/220px-Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg/330px-Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg/440px-Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="622" data-file-height="467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ivory_Tirupati_with_heavy_list_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A ship with severe <b><a href="#list"><span title="See entry on this page at § list" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">list</span></a></b></div></div></div>
<dt class="glossary" id="lizard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lizard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A short length of <span title="See entry on this page at § rope" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rope" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rope</a></span> with an eye, used to hold another rope in position.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loaded_to_the_gunwales" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loaded to the gunwales</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Literally, having cargo loaded as high as the ship's rail. The term is also used as an idiom meaning "extremely drunk".</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lofting" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lofting" title="Lofting">lofting</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In boat construction, a drafting technique used to convert a scaled drawing to full size.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loggerhead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loggerhead</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A bollard mounted in the <span title="See entry on this page at § sternsheets" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sternsheets" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sternsheets</a></span> of a <a href="/wiki/Whaleboat" title="Whaleboat">whaleboat</a> for snubbing the whale line as a harpooned whale swam away from the boat.<sup id="cite_ref-Ansel_78_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ansel_78-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 144">&#58;&#8202;144&#8202;</span></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;An iron ball attached to a long handle, used for driving caulking into seams and (occasionally) in a fight; hence the expression "at loggerheads".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loll" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loll</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="lolling" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Angle_of_loll" title="Angle of loll">lolling</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#list"><span title="See entry on this page at § list" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">list</span></a> to either side caused by inadequate transverse stability in the upright condition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="long_forties" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Long_Forties" title="Long Forties">Long Forties</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An area of the northern <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> which is fairly consistently 40 <a href="#fathom"><span title="See entry on this page at § fathom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fathoms</span></a> (240 feet; 73 metres) deep. On nautical charts with depths indicated in fathoms, it appears as a long area with many "40" notations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="long_stay" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">long stay</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The relative slackness of an <a href="#anchor_chain"><span title="See entry on this page at § anchor chain" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">anchor chain</span></a>; this term means taut and extended.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="longboat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Longboat" title="Longboat">longboat</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;In the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">Age of Sail</a>, a double-banked open boat carried by a sailing ship, rowed by eight or ten oarsmen, two per <span title="See entry on this page at § thwart" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#thwart" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">thwart</a></span>, although designed also to be rigged for sailing; more seaworthy than a <a href="#cutter"><span title="See entry on this page at § cutter" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">cutter</span></a> or <a href="#dinghy"><span title="See entry on this page at § dinghy" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dinghy</span></a> and with a <a href="#beam"><span title="See entry on this page at § beam" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">beam</span></a> greater than that of a <a href="#gig"><span title="See entry on this page at § gig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gig</span></a>. Eventually supplanted by the <a href="/wiki/Whaleboat" title="Whaleboat">whaleboat</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The largest, and thus the most capable, of boats carried on a ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="longliner" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">longliner</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fishing vessel rigged for <a href="/wiki/Longline_fishing" title="Longline fishing">longline fishing</a> ("longlining").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="longship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Longship" title="Longship">longship</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A type of ship invented and used by the Vikings for trade, commerce, exploration, and warfare, evolving over several centuries and appearing in its complete form between the 9th and 13th centuries.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lookout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lookout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A member of the <a href="#crew"><span title="See entry on this page at § crew" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crew</span></a> specifically assigned to watch surrounding waters for other vessels, land, objects in the water, hazards, threats, etc. Lookouts usually have duty stations high on a vessel's superstructure, in a specially designed <span title="See entry on this page at § top" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#top" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">top</a></span> or <a href="#crow&#39;s_nest"><span title="See entry on this page at § crow&#39;s nest" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crow's nest</span></a>, or in her <span title="See entry on this page at § rigging" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#rigging" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">rigging</a></span>, in order to enhance their field of view.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loose_cannon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loose cannon</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An irresponsible and reckless individual whose behavior (either intentionally or unintentionally) endangers the group he or she belongs to. The term refers to a hypothetical literal loose cannon which, weighing thousands of pounds, would crush anything and anyone in its path, and possibly even break a hole in the hull, thus endangering the seaworthiness of the whole ship.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="loose-footed" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">loose-footed</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fore-and-aft<span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span> that is not connected to a <a href="#boom"><span title="See entry on this page at § boom" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">boom</span></a> along its foot.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lower_deck" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lower deck</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The <a href="#deck"><span title="See entry on this page at § deck" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">deck</span></a> of a ship immediately above the <a href="#hold"><span title="See entry on this page at § hold" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">hold</span></a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;In British usage, those members of a <span title="See entry on this page at § ship&#39;s company" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#ship&#39;s_company" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">ship's company</a></span> who are not officers, often used in the plural (e.g. "the lower decks").</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lowers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lowers</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The lower <a href="#brail"><span title="See entry on this page at § brail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">brails</span></a> on the <span title="See entry on this page at § mainsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mainsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mainsail</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lubber&#39;s_hole" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lubber's hole</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A port cut into the bottom of a <span title="See entry on this page at § masthead" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#masthead" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masthead</a></span> or <span title="See entry on this page at § top" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#top" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">top</a></span> (<a href="#crow&#39;s-nest"><span title="See entry on this page at § crow&#39;s-nest" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">crow's-nest</span></a>) allowing easy entry and exit. It was considered "un-seamanlike" to use this method rather than going over the side from the <span title="See entry on this page at § shroud" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#shroud" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">shrouds</a></span>, and few sailors would risk the scorn of their shipmates by doing so (at least if there were witnesses). In practice, it is often actually quicker and easier for a fit sailor to climb outside the masthead than through the lubber's hole.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955111_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderhill1955111-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lubber&#39;s_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lubber's line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A line or mark inside or on a compass case or binnacle indicating the direction of the ship's head.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975_3-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer1975-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lucky_bag" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lucky bag</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A locker or compartment for storage of unclaimed articles.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">U.S. Naval Academy</a> yearbook.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="luff" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Luff_(sail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luff (sail)">luff</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;The <a href="#forward"><span title="See entry on this page at § forward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">forward</span></a> edge of a sail.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The process of pointing a sailing vessel closer to the wind.<sup id="cite_ref-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary_2-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thames_Sailing_Barge_glossary-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The fullest or roundest part of a ship's <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195160_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195160-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smyth_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smyth-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="luff_and_touch_her" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">luff and touch her</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To bring a vessel so close to the wind that the sails shake.<sup id="cite_ref-Naval_encyclopedia_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naval_encyclopedia-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="luff_barge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">luff barge</dfn></dt>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also <b>paddy boat</b>.</span></p>
<dd class="glossary">An 18th-century term for a sailing barge with a rounded <a href="#bow"><span title="See entry on this page at § bow" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">bow</span></a> and not a <span title="See entry on this page at § swim-head" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#swim-head" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">swim-head</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarr195159_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarr195159-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="luff_perpendicular_(lp)" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">luff perpendicular (LP)</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The shortest distance between the <a href="#clew"><span title="See entry on this page at § clew" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">clew</span></a> and the <a href="#luff"><span title="See entry on this page at § luff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">luff</span></a>, which is a perpendicular line from the luff to the clew. Commonly given as a percentage of the "J" measurement.<sup id="cite_ref-Uksailmakers_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uksailmakers-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="luff_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">luff up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To steer a sailing vessel more towards the direction of the wind until the pressure is eased on the <span title="See entry on this page at § sheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheet</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="luffing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Luffing" title="Luffing">luffing</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;(of a sailing vessel) Being steered far enough to <span title="See entry on this page at § windward" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#windward" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">windward</a></span> that the sail is no longer completely filled with wind; in such a state, the <a href="#luff"><span title="See entry on this page at § luff" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">luff</span></a> of a <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> sail begins to flap first.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Loosening a <span title="See entry on this page at § sheet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sheet" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sheet</a></span> so far past optimal trim that the sail no longer completely fills with wind.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">3.&#160;&#160;The flapping of a sail from having no wind at all.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> </dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lumber_hooker" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lumber_hooker" title="Lumber hooker">lumber hooker</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> ship designed to simultaneously carry her own deck load of lumber and to tow one or two <a href="#barge"><span title="See entry on this page at § barge" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">barges</span></a>. The barges were big old <span title="See entry on this page at § schooner" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#schooner" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">schooners</a></span> stripped of their <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span> and running gear to carry large cargoes of lumber.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lugger" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lugger" title="Lugger">lugger</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A sailing vessel with <a href="#lug_sail"><span title="See entry on this page at § lug sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lug sails</span></a> set on one, two, or more <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">masts</a></span> and perhaps lug <span title="See entry on this page at § topsail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#topsail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">topsails</a></span>, widely used as traditional fishing boats, particularly off the coasts of France, England, and Scotland; also used as privateers and smugglers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lug_sail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lug_sail" title="Lug sail">lug sail</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A four-sided <a href="#fore-and-aft_rig"><span title="See entry on this page at § fore-and-aft rig" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">fore-and-aft</span></a> <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sail</a></span> supported by a <span title="See entry on this page at § spar" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#spar" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">spar</a></span> along the top that is fixed to the <span title="See entry on this page at § mast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mast" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mast</a></span> at a point some distance from the center of the spar. A dipping lug had to be moved to the other side of the mast when <a href="/wiki/Tacking_(sailing)" title="Tacking (sailing)">tacking (sailing)</a> (in larger vessels, by partially lowering the sail and hauling down either the peak or the throat to move the <span title="See entry on this page at § yard" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#yard" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">yard</a></span> across). A standing lug can be used on either tack in the same position. It was common for British fishing luggers to have a dipping lug on the <a href="#foremast"><span title="See entry on this page at § foremast" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">foremast</span></a> and a standing lug on the <span title="See entry on this page at § mizzen" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#mizzen" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">mizzen</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarch1972&#39;&#39;passim&#39;&#39;_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarch1972&#39;&#39;passim&#39;&#39;-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lying_ahull" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Lying_ahull" title="Lying ahull">lying ahull</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Waiting out a storm by <a href="#dousing"><span title="See entry on this page at § dousing" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dousing</span></a> all <span title="See entry on this page at § sail" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms_(M-Z)#sail" title="Glossary of nautical terms (M-Z)">sails</a></span> and simply letting the boat drift.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="lying_to" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">lying to</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">See <i><a href="#lie_to"><span title="See entry on this page at § lie to" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">lie to</span></a></i>.</dd>
</dl>
